00. Basics, Tax Rates (AY 26-27) & Alternate Taxation Regimes (115BAA/BAB/BAC/BAD/BAE)

Where it fits: Foundation chapter — constitutional basis, charging provisions, definitions (AY/PY/Person/Assessee), the full AY 2026-27 rate/surcharge/cess structure, and every concessional "Alternate Taxation Regime" (115BAA/BAB/BAC/BAD/BAE) that later chapters (MAT, AMT, PGBP, Firm/Co-op taxation) all build on.

Constitutional Basis & Sources of Income-tax Law

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Entry 82, List I (Union List), Seventh Schedule to Article 246 of the Constitution — empowers the Central Government to levy tax on income other than agricultural income.
  • Entry 46, List II (State List) — empowers State Governments to tax agricultural income.
  • Concept: Identifies who can legislate income-tax law — a recurring MCQ/theory point.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Do not confuse Entry 82 (non-agricultural income, Centre) with Entry 46 (agricultural income, States).
SourceRole
Income-tax Act, 1961Principal statute — total income, tax liability, assessment procedure; in force all-India w.e.f. 1st April 1962
Income-tax Rules, 1962Made by CBDT under powers in the Act — forms, procedures, depreciation rates, valuation of perquisites
Annual Finance ActFinance Bill (presented by FM, e.g. Finance Bill 2025 on 1 Feb 2025) → becomes Finance Act on receiving Presidential assent (Finance Act 2025 assented 29 March 2025)
CBDT Circulars/NotificationsCirculars clarify scope of provisions — binding on AO, not on assessee/courts (assessee may still rely on a beneficial circular); Notifications give effect to provisions of the Act
Supreme Court / High Court decisionsSC ruling = law of the land; HC ruling binds only within its territorial jurisdiction

Charging Section & Key Definitions

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Sec. 4 — Income-tax is charged for every Assessment Year, on every "person" [Sec. 2(31)], on the total income of the Previous Year, at the rate(s) prescribed by the annual Finance Act.
  • Sec. 2(9) — Assessment Year (AY): 12 months from 1 April; AY 2026-27 = 1 April 2026 to 31 March 2027.
  • Sec. 3 — Previous Year (PY): the financial year immediately preceding the AY; PY 2025-26 (1 April 2025 – 31 March 2026) income is assessed in AY 2026-27. For a business/profession/source of income newly set up during the FY, PY begins on the date of setting up and ends on the following 31 March.
  • Concept: These three sections together fix what is taxed, when it is earned (PY), and when it is assessed (AY) — the year-lag principle, subject to the Sec. 172–176 exceptions below.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Students often reverse AY and PY in the exam — anchor it as "PY is when you earn, AY is when you file/are assessed."
TermMeaning
Sec. 2(31) PersonIndividual, HUF, Company, Firm (incl. LLP), AOP/BOI, Local Authority, Artificial Juridical Person
Sec. 2(7) AssesseeAny person liable to pay tax/any sum under the Act; includes a person in respect of whom proceedings are initiated, a deemed assessee, or an assessee-in-default

Income Assessed in the Previous Year Itself (Exceptions to the AY/PY Rule)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): (all override the normal "PY income taxed in following AY" rule)
  • Sec. 172 — Shipping business of a non-resident: tax must be paid before the ship is allowed to leave an Indian port.
  • Sec. 174 — Person leaving India with no intention of returning: income up to probable date of departure is charged to tax in that current year itself.
  • Sec. 174A — AOP/BOI/AJP formed for a particular event/purpose, likely to be dissolved in the same year: AO may assess income up to the date of dissolution as current-year income.
  • Sec. 175 — Person likely to transfer/dispose of assets to avoid tax liability: total income charged to tax in the current year itself.
  • Sec. 176 — Discontinued business/profession: AO may, at his discretion, charge the income up to the date of discontinuance to tax in the current year.
  • Concept: Revenue-protection provisions — used where waiting for the normal AY would let tax escape assessment (departure, dissolution, asset-stripping, discontinuance).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Match the trigger event to the correct section number — this is a common one-line theory MCQ.

Tax Rates for AY 2026-27 — Individual / HUF / AOP / BOI / AJP (Regular/Old Regime Slabs)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • General (below 60 yrs), Resident or Non-resident:

Tax = Nil & NTI ≤ ₹2,50,000 5% of (NTI - ₹2,50,000) & ₹2,50,000 < NTI ≤ ₹5,00,000 ₹12,500 + 20% of (NTI - ₹5,00,000) & ₹5,00,000 < NTI ≤ ₹10,00,000 ₹1,12,500 + 30% of (NTI - ₹10,00,000) & NTI > ₹10,00,000

  • Resident Senior Citizen (60 ≤ age < 80 yrs): basic exemption ₹3,00,000; same 20%/30% slab structure above ₹5,00,000/₹10,00,000.
  • Resident Super Senior Citizen (age ≥ 80 yrs): basic exemption ₹5,00,000; 20% from ₹5,00,000–₹10,00,000, 30% above ₹10,00,000 (no 5% slab).
  • CBDT Circular No. 28/2016 dated 27.07.2016 — an individual whose 60th/80th birthday falls on 1 April 2026 is deemed to have completed that age on 31 March 2026 (PY 2025-26), and is eligible for the higher exemption limit for AY 2026-27.
  • Concept: These are the old/regular regime slabs — apply only where the assessee has validly opted out of the default regime under Sec. 115BAC(1A).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Age-based slabs apply only to resident individuals; NR individuals always use the general slab regardless of age.
  • Senior/super-senior concessions are not available to HUF/AOP/BOI/AJP.

Surcharge & Marginal Relief (Individual/HUF/AOP/BOI/AJP — Old Regime)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
Total IncomeSurcharge
Up to ₹50 lakhNil
> ₹50 lakh – ₹1 crore10%
> ₹1 crore – ₹2 crore15%
> ₹2 crore (on Special Income — Dividend, CG u/s 111A/112/112A)15% on tax on special income
> ₹2 crore – ₹5 crore, on remaining (non-special) income25% on tax on remaining income
> ₹5 crore, on remaining (non-special) income37% on tax on remaining income
  • Note: the 37% surcharge slab is capped at 15% for Dividend and CG taxable u/s 111A, 112, 112A — it never goes to 25% or 37% on special income, regardless of total income.
  • Marginal relief (general formula, applies at every surcharge-slab threshold — ₹50 lakh/₹1 crore/₹2 crore/₹5 crore for individuals, etc.):

Marginal Relief = [Tax + Surcharge at actual income] - [Tax at threshold + (Actual Income - Threshold)]
i.e. tax + surcharge payable is restricted to: tax at the threshold limit plus the amount of income in excess of the threshold.

  • Concept: Prevents a small rise in income from causing a disproportionately larger rise in tax purely due to crossing a surcharge slab.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Marginal relief is computed before adding Health & Education Cess (cess is added after arriving at the relieved tax+surcharge figure).
  • Apply marginal relief separately if special-income surcharge and normal-income surcharge fall in different slabs (see worked example in source, Ex. 2, page 5-6 style problems).

Tax Rates — Company, Firm/LLP/Local Authority, Co-operative Society (AY 2026-27)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Domestic Company: 25% if total turnover/gross receipts of PY 2023-24 ≤ ₹400 crore; else 30%.
  • Foreign Company: 35%.
  • Firm / LLP / Local Authority: flat 30%.
  • Co-operative Society (regular slabs):
Total IncomeRate
Up to ₹10,00010%
> ₹10,000 – ₹20,00020%
> ₹20,00030%
  • Surcharge:
AssesseeTotal Income > ₹1 cr – ₹10 crTotal Income > ₹10 cr
Domestic Company7%12%
Foreign Company2%5%
Firm/LLP/Local Authority12% (if TI > ₹1 crore)12%
Co-operative Society7%12%
  • Health & Education Cess: 4% on (tax + surcharge) in all the above cases.
  • Sec. 288A/288B — total income and tax payable/refundable are each rounded off to the nearest ₹10.
  • Concept: These are the default rates before considering the concessional regimes (115BAA/BAB/BAD/BAE) below.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • The ₹400 crore turnover test always looks back to PY 2023-24 turnover for AY 2026-27 purposes — this base year is fixed by the Finance Act, not a rolling "two years prior" rule; re-verify the base year each attempt cycle since Finance Acts periodically roll it forward.
  • Firm/LLP surcharge is a single flat 12% (no 7%/10% tier) once TI exceeds ₹1 crore, unlike companies.

Rebate u/s 87A

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Old/regular regime — Resident Individual, Total Income ≤ ₹5,00,000:

Rebate = min(100% of tax payable, ₹12,500)

  • Default regime (Sec. 115BAC(1A)) — Resident Individual, Total Income ≤ ₹12,00,000:

Rebate = min(100% of tax payable as per slab rates, ₹60,000)

  • Marginal relief on rebate (115BAC only) — if Total Income exceeds ₹12,00,000 but does not exceed ≈ ₹12,70,588 (⚠️ VERIFY — OCR prints ₹12,70,585; recomputed break-even = 60,000 ÷ 0.85 + 12,00,000 = ₹12,70,588, small variance likely from rounding under Sec. 288A/288B): tax on such income is capped at the amount by which Total Income exceeds ₹12,00,000.

Tax payable (in marginal relief band) = Total Income - ₹12,00,000

  • Concept: A tax-nil zone for small resident-individual taxpayers; the 115BAC version is far more generous (₹60,000 vs ₹12,500) and is the reason "effective tax-free income" is quoted at ₹12 lakh (or ~₹12.75 lakh for salaried persons after standard deduction) for AY 2026-27.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Rebate is deducted before adding Health & Education Cess.
  • Under both the old regime and 115BAC, 87A rebate is not available against tax on income taxed at special rates (LTCG u/s 112A always excluded; under 115BAC(1A), the rebate applies only to tax computed at slab rates — not to 111A/112/112A special-rate tax).
  • Marginal relief on the rebate itself exists only in the 115BAC regime, not under the old regime.

Section 115BAC — Default Tax Regime: Individual/HUF/AOP/BOI/AJP

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): [Amended w.e.f. AY 26-27]
Total IncomeTax Rate
Up to ₹4,00,000Nil
₹4,00,001 – ₹8,00,0005%
₹8,00,001 – ₹12,00,00010%
₹12,00,001 – ₹16,00,00015%
₹16,00,001 – ₹20,00,00020%
₹20,00,001 – ₹24,00,00025%
Above ₹24,00,00030%
  • Special-rate income (111A, 112, 112A, etc.) is taxed at those special rates even under 115BAC.
  • Surcharge: 10%/15%/25% depending on Total Income — 37% surcharge slab is not applicable even if Total Income exceeds ₹5 crore. Cess: 4% always.
  • Standard deduction u/s 16: enhanced to ₹75,000 under 115BAC (vs ₹50,000 under the old regime).
  • Concept: 115BAC(1A) is the default regime for Individual/HUF/AOP(other than co-op society)/BOI/AJP from AY 2024-25 onward — applies automatically unless the assessee validly opts out.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Denies: self-occupied HP interest u/s 24(b), set-off of HP loss against other heads (and no carry forward of such loss), salary entertainment allowance/professional tax u/s 16(ii)/(iii), LTC u/s 10(5), HRA u/s 10(13A), most u/s 10(14) allowances (except transport allowance for specified/Divyang employees, tour/transfer allowance, daily allowance, conveyance allowance), PGBP incentive deductions (10AA, additional depreciation 32(1)(iia), 33AB, 33ABA, 35 variants, 35AD, 35CCC), minor's income allowance u/s 10(32), MP/MLA allowance u/s 10(17), and Chapter VI-A deductions except 80JJAA, 80CCD(2), 80CCH(2), 80LA.
  • Opting out: assessee with no PGBP income must exercise the option for the regular (old) regime along with the return u/s 139(1) for every PY; an assessee with PGBP income who opts out can withdraw that opt-out only once — thereafter never eligible for the old regime again while PGBP income continues.
  • AMT: assessee paying tax under 115BAC need not pay AMT; b/f AMT credit cannot be set off against 115BAC income — exhaust AMT credit first, then opt in.
  • If PGBP assessee opts into 115BAC and b/f unabsorbed depreciation includes additional depreciation, that portion is not separately set off but is added to the opening WDV of the block as on 01/04/2023 (transitional adjustment).

Section 115BAA — Concessional Regime for Domestic Companies

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): [W.e.f. AY 20-21]

Tax on Sec. 115BAA income = 22%

  • Surcharge: flat 10% irrespective of total income. Cess: 4% always.
  • Effective rates: 115BAA income and other income (IFHP, IFOS etc.) → 22% + 10% + 4% = 25.168%; Chapter XII special income (111A/112/112A etc.) → special rate + 10% + 4%.
  • Concept: Optional flat concessional rate for any domestic company (no manufacturing condition), in exchange for giving up specified deductions/incentives.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Company opting 115BAA need not pay MAT; b/f MAT credit cannot be set off against 115BAA income — exhaust MAT credit first in an earlier year, then opt in.
  • Cannot claim: 10AA, additional depreciation u/s 32(1)(iia), 33AB, 33ABA, 35(1)(ii)/(iia)/(iii), 35(2AA), 35(2AB), 35AD, 35CCC, 35CCD, and Chapter VI-A deductions except 80JJAA, 80LA, 80M.
  • B/f loss/unabsorbed depreciation attributable to the above disallowed deductions cannot be set off — deemed already given full effect, lost permanently.
  • Option exercised in Form 10-IC on or before the due date of ROI u/s 139(1) for AY 20-21 or any subsequent AY; once exercised it applies to all subsequent AYs and cannot be withdrawn once made.

Section 115BAB — New Manufacturing Domestic Companies

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): [W.e.f. AY 20-21]

Tax on Sec. 115BAB manufacturing income = 15%

  • Surcharge: flat 10%. Cess: 4% always.
  • Effective rates: Manufacturing income & STCG on depreciable assets → 15%+10%+4% = 17.16%; STCG on non-depreciable assets & other income (IFHP/IFOS) → 22%+10%+4% = 25.168%; Chapter XII special income → special rate+10%+4%; excess profit computed by AO u/s 115BAB(6) → 30%+10%+4% = 34.32%.
  • Concept: A steep concessional rate to incentivise new manufacturing companies, subject to strict setup/timeline/asset conditions.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips (conditions):
  • Company set up & registered on or after 1 October 2019 and commenced manufacturing on or before 31 March 2024.
  • Not formed by splitting up/reconstruction of an existing business; plant & machinery must be new (exception: up to 20% of total P&M value may be second-hand; imported P&M is always treated as new for this section).
  • Must not use a building previously used as a hotel or convention centre.
  • Business restricted to manufacture/research/distribution of the manufactured article — excludes: software development, mining, converting marble blocks/similar into slabs, bottling gas into cylinders, printing books or film production, and any other notified business (power generation IS treated as manufacturing).
  • Disallowed deductions mirror 115BAA's list (10AA, 32(1)(iia), 33AB, 33ABA, 35 variants, 35AD, 35CCC, 35CCD, Chapter VI-A except 80JJAA & 80M).
  • Sec. 115BAB(6): if close-connection arrangements shift more-than-ordinary profit to the company, AO may recompute and tax the excess at 30%+10%+4%; if the underlying transaction exceeds ₹20 crore, it is a "specified domestic transaction" and transfer pricing provisions apply.
  • Option in Form 10-ID on/before the due date of furnishing the first ROI u/s 139(1); once exercised, applies to subsequent AYs and cannot be withdrawn. If the option becomes invalid due to breach of the new-manufacturing-specific conditions (setup timeline / new P&M / no old hotel building / permitted business), the company may instead exercise the option under 115BAA.

Section 115BAD — Resident Co-operative Societies

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): [W.e.f. AY 21-22]

Tax on Sec. 115BAD income = 22%

  • Surcharge: flat 10% irrespective of total income. Cess: 4% always. Effective rate on 115BAD income = 22%+10%+4% = 25.168%; Chapter XII special income → special rate+10%+4%.
  • Concept: The co-operative-society counterpart of 115BAA.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • No AMT if opted; b/f AMT credit cannot be set off against 115BAD income — exhaust first, then opt in.
  • Disallowed deductions: 10AA, 32(1)(iia), 33AB, 33ABA, 35(1)(ii)/(iia)/(iii), 35(2AA), 35CCC, 35AD, Chapter VI-A except 80JJAA & 80LA; b/f loss/unabsorbed depreciation attributable to these is lost permanently.
  • Option in Form 10-IF on or before the due date of ROI u/s 139(1) for AY 21-22 or any subsequent AY; irrevocable once exercised.

Section 115BAE — New Manufacturing Resident Co-operative Societies

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): [W.e.f. AY 24-25]

Tax on Sec. 115BAE manufacturing income = 15%

  • Surcharge, cess, and effective-rate structure — same as Sec. 115BAB.
  • Concept: The co-operative-society counterpart of 115BAB, for new manufacturing co-operative societies.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips (conditions — mirror 115BAB):
  • Set up & registered on or after 1 April 2023 and commences manufacturing on or before 31 March 2024.
  • Same restrictions as 115BAB on: no splitting/reconstruction, new P&M (20% second-hand exception; imported P&M always "new"), permitted-manufacturing-business list.
  • Disallowed deductions: 10AA, 32(1)(iia), 33AB, 33ABA, 35(1)(ii)/(iia)/(iii), 35(2AA), 35AD, 35CCC, Chapter VI-A except 80JJAA.
  • Option in Form 10-IFA on/before due date of furnishing the first ROI u/s 139(1); irrevocable once exercised. Other points (close-connection excess-profit taxation, transfer pricing trigger) same as 115BAB.

Common Notes — 115BAA / 115BAB / 115BAC / 115BAD / 115BAE

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Maximum depreciation rate allowable under any of these regimes: 40%.
  • MAT (companies)/AMT (non-corporates) is not applicable to income taxed under any of these five sections.
  • Standard deduction under Salary (Sec. 16): ₹50,000 normally; ₹75,000 if the assessee has opted for Sec. 115BAC.
  • Concept: These common threads (capped depreciation, no MAT/AMT, and — only for 115BAC — the enhanced standard deduction) are frequently tested as a comparison table across all five sections.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Do not assume the enhanced ₹75,000 standard deduction applies to 115BAA/BAB/BAD/BAE — it is specific to 115BAC (individual salaried taxpayers).

Other Special Tax Rates (Chapter XII)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Sec. 115BB — Winnings from lotteries, crossword puzzles, races, card games, etc.: 30%.
  • Sec. 115BBE — Deemed income u/s 68 to 69D (unexplained cash credits/investments/expenditure etc.): 60% tax, plus surcharge 25% and HEC 4% → effective ~78%; no set-off of any loss is allowed against such deemed income.
  • Sec. 115BBF — Royalty from a patent developed & registered in India (patentee is a resident, true & first inventor): 10%. "Developed in India" requires ≥ 75% of expenditure incurred in India. Option must be exercised on/before the due date of return u/s 139(1); if the assessee, having opted, fails to offer royalty income under 115BBF in any of the next 5 years, the benefit is denied for the 5 AYs subsequent to the AY of default.
  • Sec. 115BBG — Income from transfer of Carbon Credits: 10%.
  • Sec. 115BBJ — Income from Online Games [Added by FA 2023, w.e.f. AY 24-25]: 30% on net winnings computed as prescribed.
  • Common notes for all the above: no deduction under Sec. 28–44C or Sec. 57 (gross basis); no Chapter VI-A deduction; no basic exemption limit benefit (except LTCG u/s 112, and CG u/s 112A/111A for resident Individuals & HUF, which can absorb any unutilised basic exemption limit).
  • Concept: Chapter XII special-rate incomes are taxed on a stand-alone, deduction-free (largely) basis, distinct from the slab-based alternate regimes above.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Remember the 68–69D "deemed income" 60% rate under 115BBE is one of the highest effective rates in the Act (~78%) and carries an absolute no-loss-set-off bar.

Diversion of Income by Overriding Title vs. Application of Income

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): No numeric formula — a legal-doctrine distinction:
  • Diversion of income: income is diverted from its source to another person under an obligation created by an agreement or by law, before it reaches the assessee → taxable in the hands of that other person, not the assessee.
  • Application of income: income first accrues to/reaches the assessee, who then applies it to discharge an obligation (even if paid directly to a third party) → remains taxable in the assessee's own hands.
  • Concept: Determines whose total income an amount forms part of — a classic case-law-driven theory topic.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Test: does the obligation attach to the source of income (diversion) or merely to the income after receipt (application)? A direct-payment instruction to a third party (e.g., an employer paying alimony directly out of salary) is application, not diversion, since the obligation is personal to the assessee and arises only after the income is his.

References

  1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 2(7), 2(9), 2(31), 3, 4, 87A, 115BAA, 115BAB, 115BAC, 115BAD, 115BAE, 115BB, 115BBE, 115BBF, 115BBG, 115BBJ, 172–176, 288A/288B (bare act provisions as referenced in ICAI DT study material).
  2. Finance Act, 2025 (assented 29 March 2025) — AY 2026-27 slab rates under Sec. 115BAC(1A), enhanced Sec. 87A rebate (₹60,000/₹12,00,000), and the ₹400 crore domestic-company turnover threshold (base year PY 2023-24); cross-verified via TaxGuru and IndiaFilings AY 2026-27 rate summaries.
  3. CBDT Circular No. 28/2016 dated 27.07.2016 — deemed age-completion rule for senior/super-senior citizen exemption limits.
  4. Income Tax Department official "Tax Rates" page (incometaxindia.gov.in) — corporate/co-operative society surcharge slabs and cess rate, cross-checked against TaxGuru's AY 2026-27 corporate tax rate summary.

01. Income from Capital Gains

Where it fits: Charges profits/gains arising on "transfer" of a "capital asset" u/s 45(1); this chapter builds the computation mechanics (Sec 45–55), deemed-transfer situations, exemptions (Sec 54 series) and the special tax rates (Sec 111A/112A) that feed into the final tax computation chapter.

1. Meaning of "Transfer" — Sec. 2(47)

  • Key rule(s)/definitions:
  • "Transfer" includes: sale, exchange or relinquishment of the asset; extinguishment of any right therein; compulsory acquisition under any law; conversion of capital asset into stock-in-trade; part-performance of a contract (possession of immovable property allowed to be taken/retained); any transaction enabling enjoyment of immovable property (e.g., becoming a member of a co-operative society holding a flat); and redemption of Zero-Coupon Bonds (ZCBs).
  • Also includes disposing of / parting with an asset or interest therein, or creating any interest in any asset, directly or indirectly, absolutely or conditionally, voluntarily or involuntarily, by agreement or otherwise.

Concept: Defines the trigger event for capital gains taxation — without a "transfer" as defined, Sec. 45 cannot apply.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Redemption of ZCB is a transfer even though there is no "sale" in the conventional sense — commonly tested.
  • Extinguishment of rights (e.g., surrender of tenancy) is covered even without a third party "buyer."

2. Capital Asset, Period of Holding (POH) & STCA/LTCA Classification

  • Key rule(s)/thresholds (post Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024, w.e.f. transfers on/after 23.07.2024):
CategoryAssetPOH for LTCA (upto 22.07.24)POH for LTCA (from 23.07.24)
Part AListed security (other than unit) on recognised stock exchange in India; Unit of UTI; Unit of equity-oriented MF; ZCB; listed units (incl. business trust units, w.e.f. 23.7.24)> 1 year> 1 year
Part BUnlisted shares; Immovable property> 2 years> 2 years
Part CAny other capital asset> 3 years> 2 years
  • Asset held for more than the prescribed period → Long-Term Capital Asset (LTCA); otherwise → Short-Term Capital Asset (STCA).

Concept: POH decides both the classification (STCA/LTCA) and which tax-rate/indexation regime applies.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Only Part C (residual "any other asset", e.g., unlisted debt instruments, gold, unlisted MLDs not covered u/s 50AA) had its threshold reduced from 3 years to 2 years w.e.f. 23.7.2024 — Parts A and B are unchanged.
  • The phrase "other than Unit" was omitted from Part A w.e.f. 23.7.2024, so listed units of business trusts now also get the 1-year LTCA threshold.

3. Computation of Capital Gains — Sec. 48

  • Key formula:

Capital Gain = FVOC - Expenses on Transfer - COA - COI

where FVOC = Full Value of Consideration; COA = Cost of Acquisition; COI = Cost of Improvement.

  • Provisos to Sec. 48:
  • COA/COI shall not include amounts already deducted as interest u/s 24(b) (home loan interest) or under Chapter VI-A (added by FA 2023) — no double deduction.
  • Indexation (2nd proviso) is NOT available for any transfer on or after 23rd July, 2024, irrespective of holding period — COA/COI are deducted at actual (unindexed) cost for such transfers. Indexation (below) survives only for transfers up to 22.07.2024.
  • 1st proviso — Non-resident (incl. foreign co.) transferring shares/debentures of an Indian company acquired in foreign currency: capital gain computed in foreign currency first, then reconverted (Rule 115A).
  • 3rd proviso — 1st & 2nd provisos (NR/indexation) do not apply to LTCG computed u/s 112A.
  • 4th proviso — No indexation on bonds/debentures, except Capital Indexation Bonds and Sovereign Gold Bonds (SGB) issued by RBI.
  • 5th proviso — Forex gain on rupee appreciation at redemption of Rupee Denominated Bonds (RDB) of an Indian company held by a NR is ignored while computing FVOC.
  • 7th proviso — STT paid on purchase/sale of shares/units is not allowed as a deduction (not a transfer expense if paid on sale; not added to COA if paid on purchase).

Concept: This is the master computation format used (with variations) throughout the chapter.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Since 23.7.2024 the word "Indexed" (ICOA/ICOI) is only relevant for pre-23.7.2024 transfers — don't index for current transfers except where explicitly grandfathered (see Sec. 112 rate comparison, Topic 19).
  • STT is never deductible anywhere in the Sec. 48 computation.

4. Cost Inflation Index (CII) & Indexation Mechanics (pre-23.7.2024 transfers)

  • Key formulas:

Indexed COA = COA × CII of year of transferCII of first year asset held by assessee (or FY 2001-02, whichever is later)

Indexed COI = COI × CII of year of transferCII of year of improvement

  • Cost of pre-01.04.2001 assets:

COA = max(Actual cost, FMV as on 01.04.2001)

with the rider that for immovable property, if Stamp Duty Value (SDV) as on 01.04.2001 is available, the FMV taken cannot exceed such SDV.

  • CII table (as notified by CBDT; base year FY 2001-02 = 100):
FYCIIFYCIIFYCII
2001-021002010-111672019-20289
2002-031052011-121842020-21301
2003-041092012-132002021-22317
2004-051132013-142202022-23331
2005-061172014-152402023-24348
2006-071222015-162542024-25363
2007-081292016-172642025-26376
2008-091372017-18272
2009-101482018-19280
  • Cost of improvement before 01.04.2001 is always ignored (whether or not asset itself acquired before that date).

Concept: Indexation adjusts historical cost for inflation — but note it is now a legacy mechanism, relevant chiefly for transfers up to 22.7.2024 or in the Sec. 112 "lower of two rates" comparison for resident individuals/HUF on immovable property (Topic 19).

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • CII for FY 2024-25 = 363 (Notification 44/2024, 24.5.2024); CII for FY 2025-26 = 376 (Notification 70/2025, 1.7.2025) — both are quoted in Sec. 112 grandfathering comparisons even though indexation is otherwise discontinued.

5. Cost of Acquisition & Improvement — Sec. 55

  • Key rule(s):
  • COA of self-generated intangible assets — goodwill/other intangible asset of business/profession, trademark/brand name, right to manufacture/produce/process (patent/copyright), right to carry on business/profession, tenancy right, loom hours, route permits, or any other right — is determined per Sec. 55, and the FMV-as-on-01.04.2001 option is not available for these assets.
  • COI for such self-generated intangible assets/rights is always Nil; for other assets, COI = capital expenditure incurred on/after 01.04.2001 only.
  • Where depreciation was claimed on goodwill up to PY 2019-20 (before goodwill was excluded from depreciable assets by FA 2021), COA = purchase price minus depreciation claimed.
  • Capital gain on transfer of self-generated goodwill / brand name of a profession was not chargeable to tax up to AY 2020-21 (no cost could be attributed).
  • Bonus shares — POH runs from date of allotment; if Sec. 112A applies and bonus shares were allotted before 01.02.2018, COA = FMV as on 31.01.2018.
  • Right shares (in hands of purchaser of the right): COA = amount paid to company for shares + amount paid to purchase the right; POH from date of allotment of shares.

Concept: Governs what counts as "cost" when the asset has no ascertainable original purchase price (self-generated assets) or arises from a corporate action (bonus/rights).

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Never apply 01.04.2001 FMV substitution to self-generated goodwill/trademarks/patents/business rights — a classic trap.
  • COI is always Nil for the listed intangible/rights category, regardless of actual expenditure incurred.
TermMeaning
COACost of Acquisition
COICost of Improvement
FMVFair Market Value

6. Conversion of Capital Asset ↔ Stock-in-Trade

  • Key formula/rule — Sec. 45(2) (Capital Asset → Stock-in-Trade):

Capital gain is chargeable in the year of conversion, but taxable only in the year the resultant stock-in-trade is sold (partly, if partly sold).

Capital Gain = FMV on date of conversion - COA/ICOA - COI/ICOI
PGBP = Sale price of stock - FMV on date of conversion

  • Amount recorded in books is irrelevant; FMV on date of conversion is what matters.
  • CBDT Circular: for Sec. 54EC purposes, the 6-month investment window on subsequent sale of such stock is counted from the date of sale of the stock, not the date of conversion.
  • Key rule — reverse case, Stock-in-Trade → Capital Asset:
  • Sec. 28(via): FMV of inventory on date of conversion into capital asset is taxable as PGBP in the year of conversion.
  • Sec. 49(9): COA of the resulting capital asset = FMV taxed u/s 28(via).
  • Sec. 2(42A): POH is reckoned from the date of conversion into capital asset.
  • Rule 11UAB — FMV of stock-in-trade on date of conversion: immovable property → SDV; jewellery/art/shares & securities → Rule 11UA value; any other asset → open market price.

Concept: Two mirror-image deeming provisions — one delays taxation of an asset already converted to stock (taxed only on eventual sale), the other advances taxation of stock converted to a capital asset (taxed immediately as PGBP, with capital gains arising only later on eventual transfer).

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Do not confuse the two: Sec. 45(2) → both PGBP and CG arise in the same year (year of sale of stock); Sec. 28(via)/49(9) → PGBP arises on conversion, CG arises later on transfer of the (now) capital asset — different years.

7. Compensation on Compulsory Acquisition — Sec. 45(5)

  • Key formula:

CG on Initial Compensation = FVOC (Initial Compensation) - COA/ICOA - COI/ICOI
CG on Enhanced Compensation = FVOC (Enhanced Compensation) - Litigation Expenses

  • Key rules:
  • Capital gain is taxable in the year the (initial/enhanced) compensation is received, not the year of transfer.
  • Enhanced compensation received due to an interim court order is not taxed on receipt — taxed only in the year the final order is passed.
  • Interest on delayed compensation is taxable under IFOS in the year of receipt, with a flat 50% deduction u/s 57.
  • If compensation is later reduced by a court/authority, the assessment is rectified u/s 155.
  • Nature (STCG/LTCG) of enhanced compensation follows the nature of the initial compensation.
  • If the transferor dies before receiving enhanced compensation, it is taxed as capital gain in the hands of the recipient (legal heir/other person).
  • Sec. 10(37): Capital gains on compulsory acquisition of urban agricultural land used for agricultural purposes by the individual/HUF (or parents, if individual) during the preceding 2 years is fully exempt (Individual/HUF only).
  • CBDT clarification: compensation exempted from income-tax u/s 96 of the RFCTLARR Act, 2013 is also not taxable under the Income-tax Act.

Concept: Shifts the taxable event from "transfer" to "receipt" because compensation amount/timing under compulsory acquisition is often uncertain/disputed at the time of transfer.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Balakrishnan (SC): negotiating with the Collector to enhance compensation (without going to court) does not convert a compulsory acquisition into a voluntary sale — Sec. 10(37) exemption survives.

8. Insurance Claim on Destruction of Capital Asset — Sec. 45(1A)

  • Key formula:

Capital Gain = FVOC (Insurance claim — money/FMV of asset received) - COA/ICOA - COI/ICOI

  • Key rules:
  • Applicable only when asset is destroyed by fire, flood, earthquake, tsunami, riot, civil disturbance, enemy action or other natural calamity, and an insurance claim is actually received.
  • Capital gain taxable in the year the insurance claim is received (not year of destruction).
  • If no claim is received, no capital gain arises at all.

Concept: Like Sec. 45(5), defers taxation to the year of actual receipt of money/asset.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Destruction alone (without an insurance claim) is a non-event for capital gains purposes.

9. Joint Development Agreement (JDA) — Sec. 45(5A) / Sec. 49(7)

  • Key rule:
  • Applicable only to Individual/HUF entering a JDA for developing land/building (or both).
  • Capital gain taxable in the year the Certificate of Completion (CC) for the whole/part of the project is issued by the competent authority (not the year possession is handed over) — unless the assessee transfers his share in the project on/before the date of CC issuance, in which case normal Sec. 45(1) timing (year of possession transfer) applies.
  • FVOC = SDV of assessee's share in the project as on date of CC + monetary consideration received (if any).
  • Sec. 49(7): COA of the flats/share received in the project = the amount deemed as FVOC u/s 45(5A).

Concept: A special deferral: landowner's capital gain crystallises only on CC issuance, not on handing over possession — a major cash-flow relief.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Track two dates carefully: "year of transfer" (possession handed to developer) vs. "year of tax" (CC issued) — POH for a subsequent sale of the received flat runs only from the date of possession of that flat/CC, not from the original land purchase date.
  • If assessee sells his share before CC is issued, Sec. 45(5A) deferral is lost and normal Sec. 45(1) applies from year of possession transfer.

10. Transfer of Capital Asset Between Firm & Partner — Sec. 45(3)/(4), Sec. 9B, Rule 8AB

  • Sec. 45(3) — Partner/member → Firm/AOP/BOI (capital contribution): CG taxable in hands of the partner; FVOC = amount recorded in the books of the firm/AOP/BOI.
  • Sec. 9B — Firm/AOP/BOI → Partner/member (on dissolution or reconstitution), of capital asset and/or stock-in-trade: deemed transfer by the firm, taxable (PGBP and/or Capital Gains) in the year the asset is received by the partner; FVOC/sale value = FMV as on date of receipt.
  • Sec. 45(4) — additional charge on the firm, only on reconstitution, where a partner receives money and/or capital asset:

Capital Gain (A) = Money received (B) + FMV of CA received (C) - Partner's capital a/c balance at reconstitution (D)

If A is negative, it is deemed to be Nil.

  • Rule 8AB — attribution of the Sec. 45(4) gain to the firm's remaining capital assets:

Attributed CG (to a specific asset) = Total CG u/s 45(4) × Increase in value of that asset (revaluation)Total increase in value of all revalued assets

Gain attributed to STCAs, block-of-depreciable-assets, or self-generated goodwill/assets is deemed STCG; all other attributed gain is deemed LTCG. Any amount not relating to revaluation/self-generated assets is not attributed at all.

Concept: "Reconstitution" (partner exit/entry/PSR change) triggers both a deemed-transfer charge on the departing partner's receipt (Sec. 9B) and a separate firm-level charge (Sec. 45(4)) on the balance — the two operate together, not as alternatives. Dissolution attracts only Sec. 9B, not Sec. 45(4).

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Partner's capital account balance (D) for Sec. 45(4) is computed excluding any increase from asset revaluation or self-generated goodwill/asset recognition.
  • On subsequent transfer of the attributed assets, the amount already taxed u/s 45(4) reduces the capital gain computed under Sec. 48 at that later transfer (avoids double taxation).
  • Dissolution → only Sec. 9B applies; Reconstitution → both Sec. 9B and Sec. 45(4) apply.

11. Dematerialised Securities — Sec. 45(2A)

  • Key rule:
  • Capital gain on transfer of D-mat securities is taxable in the hands of the beneficial owner (not the depository).
  • COA and POH determined on FIFO (First-In-First-Out) basis.
  • FIFO applies account-wise if the investor holds multiple D-mat accounts, and applies only to D-mat holdings — not to physical share certificates.
  • Date of transfer/POH does not change merely because shares are dematerialised; where physical stock is dematerialised, the FIFO "entry" date is the date of entry into the D-mat account.

Concept: Solves the practical problem of identifying "which shares were sold" when holdings are fungible in a D-mat account.

Pitfalls / exam tips: FIFO is account-specific — do not aggregate across an investor's multiple demat accounts.

12. ULIP Taxation — Sec. 45(1B), Rule 8AD, Sec. 10(10D)

  • Key rule — Sec. 10(10D) exemption denied (taxable) where:
  • Sum received under a Keyman insurance policy; or
  • Premium paid exceeds the prescribed % of sum assured (10%/15%/20% slabs u/s 80C, depending on policy date) — unless received on death; or
  • ULIP issued on/after 01.02.2021 with annual premium (for any year of the term) exceeding ₹2,50,000 — aggregated across all such ULIPs if more than one is held (exemption then available only for the combination of policies whose aggregate premium is ≤ ₹2,50,000); or
  • Non-ULIP life insurance policy issued on/after 01.04.2023 with annual premium exceeding ₹5,00,000 (aggregated similarly across multiple such policies) — added by FA 2023, w.e.f. AY 2024-25.
  • Exemption is restored regardless of the above limits if the sum is received on death of the insured, or the policy is issued by an IFSC Insurance Office; the ₹5,00,000 limit also does not apply to a pure term insurance policy.
  • Sec. 45(1B)/Rule 8AD — Capital Gain on ULIP (issued on/after 01.02.2021, exemption u/s 10(10D) not applicable):

Taxable amount (first receipt) = A - B, A = amount received (incl. bonus), B = aggregate premium paid till date of receipt
Taxable amount (subsequent receipt) = C - D, C = amount now received (excl. amounts in A), D = aggregate premium (excl. amounts in B)

  • Such gain is deemed to be LTCG on an equity-oriented fund unit, taxable u/s 112A (irrespective of actual holding period).
  • Sec. 56(2)(xiii) (added by FA 2023, w.e.f. AY 2024-25) — for non-ULIP life insurance policies not exempt u/s 10(10D): amount received in excess of aggregate premiums paid (net of amounts already claimed as deduction, e.g., u/s 80C) is taxable under IFOS.
  • Premium limits under Sec. 10(10D)/56(2)(xiii) are computed exclusive of GST on the premium (CBDT clarification).

Concept: Splits life-insurance-linked capital receipts into three buckets — fully exempt, capital-gains-taxable (ULIP under 112A), and IFOS-taxable (other non-exempt policies) — depending on policy type, issue date and premium level.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • ULIP gains go to Capital Gains (112A); non-ULIP LIP gains go to IFOS (56(2)(xiii)) — do not mix the two heads.
  • Where an assessee holds multiple ULIPs each individually within ₹2,50,000 but exceeding in aggregate, exemption should be claimed for the combination that minimises tax (student must compare options).

13. Sec. 50AA — Capital Gain on Specified Mutual Funds, MLDs & Unlisted Bonds/Debentures

(amended by FA 2024, w.e.f. 23.07.2024)

  • Key formula (always STCG, regardless of holding period):

STCG = FVOC (on transfer/redemption/maturity) - Transfer Expenses - Cost of Acquisition

  • Applies to:

(a) units of a Specified Mutual Fund acquired on/after 01.04.2023, or a Market Linked Debenture (MLD); or (b) unlisted bonds/unlisted debentures transferred, redeemed, or maturing on/after 23.07.2024.

  • STT is not deductible anywhere in this computation; no indexation (deemed STCA/STCG).
  • "Specified Mutual Fund" = a fund investing >65% of proceeds in debt/money-market instruments (or ≥65% in units of such a fund); equity percentage measured by annual average of daily closing figures.

Concept: Denies the concessional LTCG regime to debt-oriented/market-linked instruments by deeming the gain as short-term irrespective of actual holding period.

Pitfalls / exam tips: Do not apply Part-C 2-year LTCA test to these instruments — Sec. 50AA overrides the classification with a blanket STCG deeming fiction.

14. Slump Sale — Sec. 50B, Rule 11UAE

  • Key formula:

Capital Gain = FVOC (higher of FMV-1 or FMV-2, per Rule 11UAE) - Transfer Expenses - Net Worth of Undertaking (COA, unindexed)

Net Worth = Assets (WDV for depreciable assets; book value for others) - Liabilities (book value)

  • Key rules:
  • Undertaking held > 3 years → LTCG; ≤ 3 years → STCG (note: this 36-month test is specific to Sec. 50B and is not affected by the general Part-C reduction to 2 years).
  • Revaluation of assets is ignored for net worth; if net worth is negative, COA = Nil.
  • Assets on which Sec. 35AD deduction was claimed, and self-generated goodwill, are taken at Nil value for net worth computation.
  • No PGBP profit arises separately even if stock is transferred as part of the slump sale.
  • CA report (in prescribed form) certifying net worth computation must be furnished by the tax-audit due date u/s 44AB.
  • Rule 11UAE — FMV on date of transfer = higher of FMV-1 (of undertaking transferred: A+B+C+D−L, per prescribed asset/liability adjustments) or FMV-2 (of consideration received: E+F+G+H).

Concept: A lump-sum "business transfer" (undertaking/division sold as a going concern without item-wise price allocation) is taxed on the difference between deemed FMV consideration and the undertaking's net worth.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Slump sale retains its own 3-year LTCA/STCA threshold — do not confuse with the general Part-C 2-year rule (which applies to other residual assets, not undertakings under Sec. 50B).
  • Tax-efficient alternatives: transfer via a wholly-owned Indian subsidiary [Sec. 47(iv)] or via demerger [Sec. 47(vib)] instead of slump sale, to avoid/defer the charge.

15. Deemed Full Value of Consideration — Sec. 50C / 50CA / 50D; Advance Forfeiture — Sec. 51

  • Sec. 50C — Immovable property (capital asset): if Stamp Duty Value (SDV) exceeds 110% of actual consideration, SDV is deemed to be FVOC. Assessee may dispute SDV before the Valuation Officer (AO can refer suo motu too, if SDV not already contested in appeal). Where date of agreement differs from date of registration, SDV as on the date of agreement can be adopted if at least part consideration was received by that date via account-payee cheque/DD/ECS/other prescribed electronic modes (Notification 8/2020: credit/debit card, net banking, IMPS, UPI, RTGS, NEFT, BHIM Aadhaar Pay).
  • Sec. 50CA — Unquoted shares (capital asset) transferred for consideration less than FMV: FMV (per prescribed valuation rules) deemed to be FVOC. Carve-out for share transfers pursuant to an NCLT-approved resolution plan where the company's board has been superseded by CG-nominated directors.
  • Sec. 50D — Where consideration for transfer is not ascertainable/cannot be determined, FMV of the asset on date of transfer is deemed FVOC.
  • Sec. 51 — Advance/token/earnest money forfeited by the present owner before 01.04.2014 reduces COA (before indexation); forfeiture by a previous owner is not considered. Forfeiture on/after 01.04.2014 is instead taxed as IFOS in the year of forfeiture (Sec. 56(2)(ix)) and does not reduce COA.

Concept: These are anti-avoidance "deeming" provisions ensuring consideration is not understated relative to fair/market value, plus a timing rule for forfeited advances.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • 110% tolerance band under Sec. 50C — SDV is substituted only if it exceeds 110% of stated consideration, not merely if it is higher at all.
  • Do not net pre-2014 vs post-2014 forfeitures under the same rule — the treatment (COA reduction vs IFOS) depends entirely on the forfeiture date.

16. Transactions Not Regarded as Transfer (Exempt Transfers) — Sec. 47 / Sec. 47A / Sec. 49(1)

  • Key rule(s) — selected high-frequency clauses (no capital gain arises):
  • HUF partition (total/partial) — 47(i).
  • Gift/will/irrevocable trust by individual/HUF — 47(ii) (but not for ESOP shares/debentures/warrants gifted; FVOC there = FMV on date of gift, per 6th proviso to Sec. 48).
  • Holding Co. ↔ 100%-owned Indian subsidiary Co. — 47(iv)/(v) (not if transferred as stock-in-trade).
  • Amalgamation — transfer to an Indian amalgamated company — 47(vi); cross-border share-swap conditions — 47(via)/(viab).
  • Demerger — transfer to Indian resulting company — 47(vib); cross-border conditions — 47(vic)/(vicc); issue of resulting-co. shares to demerged-co. shareholders is not a transfer — 47(vid).
  • Non-resident-to-non-resident transfers outside India of specified bonds/GDRs/RDBs/G-Secs — 47(vii)/(viiaca)/(viiib).
  • Sovereign Gold Bond redemption by an Individual — 47(viic) (only on redemption/maturity; a sale before maturity is a normal taxable transfer, with indexation available).
  • Conversion: Sole Proprietorship → Company [47(xiv)]; Firm/AOP-BOI → Company [47(xiii)]; Unlisted Public/Private Co. → LLP [47(xiiib)] — each subject to shareholding/turnover/asset-value continuity conditions (e.g., LLP conversion needs turnover ≤ ₹60 lakh and total assets ≤ ₹5 crore in each of the preceding 3 years, plus ≥50% PSR continuity for 5 years and no capital withdrawal for 3 years).
  • Conversion of bonds/debentures/preference shares into shares of the same company — 47(x)/(xb); conversion of Gold ↔ Electronic Gold Receipt (EGR) — 47(viiid).
  • Reverse mortgage of a capital asset under a notified scheme — 47(xvi) (loan amount is separately exempt u/s 10(43)).
  • Merger of MF schemes/plans (equity-with-equity or debt-with-debt only) — 47(xviii)/(xix).
  • Sec. 47A — withdrawal of exemption: For Sec. 47(iv)/(v) (holding-subsidiary transfers), if within 8 years the asset is converted to stock-in-trade by the transferee, or the holding company ceases to hold 100% of the subsidiary, the exemption is withdrawn and taxed in the transferor's hands in the year of original transfer (rectification u/s 154); COA to the transferee in that case = its original acquisition price [Sec. 49(3)]. Similar claw-backs under Sec. 47A(3)/(4) apply to violations of conditions under Sec. 47(xiii)/(xiv)/(xiiib), taxed in the hands of the successor entity.
  • Sec. 49(1) — Cost to previous owner: where asset is acquired via gift/will/inheritance/HUF partition or any of the specified Sec. 47 exempt modes, COA = cost to the previous owner, POH also includes the previous owner's holding period, and (per Manjula J. Shah, Bom HC) indexation runs from the year the previous owner first held the asset:

Indexed COA = COA to previous owner × CII of year of transferCII of year asset first held by previous owner

Concept: Sec. 47 is an exhaustive list of transactions Parliament has chosen to exclude from the definition of "transfer" for CG purposes (usually corporate restructuring, family transfers, or specified cross-border/bond transactions) — Sec. 47A claws the exemption back if the underlying restructuring rationale is later defeated.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • ESOP shares/debentures/warrants gifted by employer are excluded from the general Sec. 47(ii) gift exemption — a favourite exam trap.
  • Sec. 47A's 8-year look-back is specific to the holding-subsidiary clauses [47(iv)/(v)]; other clauses have their own separate claw-back conditions/timeframes (e.g., 5-year continuity tests under 47(xiii)/(xiv)/(xiiib)).

17. Segregated Portfolio (Side-Pocketing) — Sec. 49(2AG)/(2AH), Sec. 2(42A)(hh)

  • Key formulas:

COA of units in segregated portfolio = COA of units in total portfolio × NAV of assets transferred to segregated portfolioNAV of total portfolio before segregation

COA of units in main portfolio = COA of original units in total portfolio - COA of segregated portfolio units

  • POH of segregated-portfolio units includes the period the original (total-portfolio) units were held.

Concept: When a mutual fund isolates its bad/illiquid debt (segregated portfolio) from good debt (main portfolio) following a credit event, the original cost is apportioned between the two by relative NAV, with continuity of holding period.

Pitfalls / exam tips: No transfer/capital-gain event arises at the point of segregation itself — only apportionment of cost; gain/loss arises only on eventual redemption of either set of units.

18. Exemptions under Capital Gains — Sec. 54, 54B, 54D, 54EC, 54F, 54G, 54GA, 54H

  • Sec. 54F additional conditions: on date of transfer of the original LTCA, assessee must not own more than one other residential HP, and must not purchase another house within 2 years or construct within 3 years after transfer — breach makes the exempted LTCG taxable in the year of such purchase/construction.
  • Locking period (Sec. 54/54B/54D/54F/54G/54GA): new asset transferred within 3 years of purchase/construction → exemption withdrawn (Sec. 54/54B/54D/54G/54GA: COA of new asset reduced by exempted CG for computing CG on its transfer; Sec. 54F: exempted LTCG becomes taxable as LTCG in year of transfer).
  • Sec. 54EC locking period: 5 years — early transfer/conversion into money, or taking a loan/advance against the bonds as security, triggers taxability of the exempted LTCG in that year.
  • Capital Gains Account Scheme (CGAS): if the new asset is not acquired by the due date of filing return, the CG (or net consideration for 54F) must be deposited in CGAS before the earlier of the due date or actual date of filing return; unutilised amount is taxed as CG of the PY in which the specified period expires (proportionately, for 54F). CBDT: unutilised CGAS balance is not taxable in the hands of legal heirs if the individual dies before the stipulated period.
  • Sec. 54H: where original transfer is by compulsory acquisition, the time limits for acquiring the new asset/depositing in CGAS run from the date of receipt of compensation, not the date of compulsory acquisition.
  • Sec. 10(37A): exemption for specified persons in Andhra Pradesh under the Amaravati land-pooling scheme.

Concept: Reinvestment-linked exemptions that defer/eliminate tax where the sale proceeds of specified assets are reinvested into specified replacement assets within prescribed windows.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • The ₹10 crore cap (Sec. 54 & 54F) and the ₹50 lakh cap (Sec. 54EC) are absolute rupee ceilings on the cost of new asset considered, not on the exemption itself when cost is lower.
  • 54EC bond list has grown over time — HUDCO and IREDA are the latest additions (w.e.f. 01.04.2025 and 09.07.2025 respectively); confirm the notification date in force for the relevant PY in the exam.
  • Key case laws: Syed Ali Adil (AP HC) — two adjoining, internally-connected flats treated as one house for Sec. 54; Kamal Wahal (Delhi HC) — Sec. 54 exemption not deniable merely because new house is registered solely in spouse's name; T.N. Aravinda Reddy (SC) — co-owner buying out other co-owners' share is a "purchase" for Sec. 54; Ravinder Kumar Arora (Delhi HC) — full Sec. 54F exemption to the co-owner who funded the entire purchase, despite joint registration; Gouli Mahadevappa (Kar HC) — reinvestment in excess of actual net consideration (where Sec. 50C SDV was adopted as FVOC) still qualifies for Sec. 54F; V.S. Dempo & Co. (SC) — Sec. 50's STCG deeming fiction does not disqualify a depreciable LTCA from Sec. 54EC eligibility.

19. Special Tax Rates on Capital Gains — Sec. 111A, Sec. 112A & Others

  • Sec. 112A — LTCG on listed equity shares/equity-oriented fund units/business trust units (STT paid on acquisition* and transfer):

Tax = (LTCG - ₹1,25,000) × 10% & transfer before 23.07.2024 12.5% & transfer on/after 23.07.2024

  • The ₹1,25,000 basic exemption (raised from ₹1,00,000 by FA 2024) applies once on the aggregate LTCG across both sub-periods in a year of transition.
  • Applies also to gains from transactions on a recognised stock exchange in an IFSC where consideration is in foreign currency, even if STT is not paid.
  • Deduction under Chapter VI-A and rebate u/s 87A are not available against Sec. 112A LTCG (rebate u/s 87A restriction applies as clarified/legislated).
  • *STT-on-acquisition condition is waived by CG notification for specified modes (e.g., shares acquired before 01.10.2004; specified non-STT acquisitions such as those approved by SC/HC/NCLT/SEBI/RBI, ESOP allotments, acquisitions by non-residents under FDI norms, etc., subject to conditions).
  • COA (for shares/equity fund units/business trust units acquired before 01.02.2018, transferred on/after 01.04.2018) — grandfathering:

COA = max(Actual COA, min(FMV as on 31.01.2018, FVOC))

FMV as on 31.01.2018 = highest quoted price on that date (or last trading day before it, if no trading that day) for listed shares/units; NAV as on 31.01.2018 for unlisted units.

  • Sec. 111A — STCG on the same asset class (STT paid on transfer):

Tax = STCG × 15% & transfer before 23.07.2024 20% & transfer on/after 23.07.2024

Chapter VI-A deductions not available against Sec. 111A STCG; concessional rate also extends to IFSC-RSE foreign-currency transactions without STT.

  • Other capital gains (not covered by 111A/112A):
Transfer dateLTCG rateSTCG rate
Before 23.07.202420% (with indexation)Slab (normal) rate
On/after 23.07.202412.5% (without indexation)Slab (normal) rate
  • Grandfathering for resident Individual/HUF on immovable property acquired before 23.07.2024: tax = lower of [12.5% without indexation] or [20% with indexation].
  • Non-resident/foreign company: LTCG on unlisted securities/shares (without benefit of 1st/2nd proviso to Sec. 48) taxed at 10% (before 23.07.2024) / 12.5% (on/after 23.07.2024).
  • Unexhausted basic exemption set-off: a resident Individual/HUF whose total income (excluding Sec. 112/112A LTCG and Sec. 111A STCG) is below the basic exemption limit may use the shortfall against such special-rate gains before applying the concessional rate.

Concept: Equity/equity-fund/business-trust gains get concessional, STT-linked rates (111A/112A); all other capital gains fall back to the "Other Capital Gains" table, which itself was restructured (indexation withdrawn) w.e.f. 23.07.2024, with a one-time grandfathering comparison for resident individuals/HUFs on immovable property.

Pitfalls / exam tips:

  • Rebate u/s 87A and Chapter VI-A deductions are blocked against both 111A STCG and 112A LTCG — a recurring MCQ/theory trap.
  • Always check the transfer date against 23.07.2024 before picking a rate — many candidates default to the old 10%/15%/20% rates out of habit.
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — the precise current interplay of Sec. 87A rebate denial with 112A/111A gains has seen conflicting CPC processing positions/litigation in recent assessment years; confirm against the applicable Finance Act/CBDT position for the specific exam attempt before relying on it in a numerical answer.

20. Miscellaneous — Reference to Valuation Officer & Key Case Laws

  • Sec. 55A — reference to Valuation Officer (VO): AO may refer valuation to the VO where (i) FMV claimed (per a registered valuer) appears, in the AO's opinion, at variance with actual FMV; or (ii) in any other case, where AO's estimate of FMV exceeds the assessee's claimed value by more than the lower of 15% of claimed value or ₹25,000, and having regard to the nature of the asset/other circumstances, a reference is necessary.
  • Key case laws:
CasePrinciple
Aditya Kumar Jajodia (Cal HC, 2018)Cost of perfecting title (leasehold → full ownership) of inherited property, before sale, is includible in COA under Sec. 48/55.
Sakthi Metal Depot (SC, 2021)An asset does not exit the depreciable "block of assets" merely because it was unused for business in recent years, as long as the business continues — gain on its sale remains STCG.
Gujarat State Fertilizers & Chemicals Ltd. (Guj HC, 2018)Loss on sale of fertiliser subsidy bonds (received in lieu of a business subsidy) is allowable as a business loss, since the underlying subsidy itself is business income.
Govindbhai Mamaiya (SC, 2014)Land inherited by legal heirs and compulsorily acquired is taxed in their individual capacities, not in AOP status (mere co-ownership by inheritance ≠ AOP).

Concept: Rounds out the chapter with the valuation-dispute mechanism and a curated set of frequently examined judicial principles.

Pitfalls / exam tips: The 15%-or-₹25,000 (whichever is lower) variance threshold under Sec. 55A(b) is a precise, examinable figure — do not confuse with the unrelated 10% Sec. 50C tolerance band.

References

  1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 2(14), 2(42A), 2(47), 45, 47, 47A, 48, 49, 50, 50AA, 50B, 50C, 50CA, 50D, 51, 54, 54B, 54D, 54EC, 54F, 54G, 54GA, 54H, 55, 55A, 56(2)(x)/(xiii), 111A, 112, 112A — bare act text and provisos (as amended up to Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024).
  2. Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024 — amendments effective 23.07.2024 (holding-period rationalisation, withdrawal of indexation u/s 48, Sec. 111A rate to 20%, Sec. 112A rate to 12.5% with ₹1,25,000 exemption, Sec. 50AA scope widened) — summarised in Taxmann, "Key Amendments to Capital Gains Provisions under the Finance (No. 2) Act 2024" (taxmann.com/post/blog).
  3. CBDT Notification No. 44/2024 dated 24.05.2024 (CII for FY 2024-25 = 363) and Notification No. 70/2025 dated 01.07.2025 (CII for FY 2025-26 = 376).
  4. CBDT Press Release/PIB (10.07.2025) and related coverage — notification of IREDA bonds as "long-term specified asset" u/s 54EC w.e.f. 09.07.2025 (₹50 lakh cap); HUDCO bonds notified w.e.f. 01.04.2025.
  5. ICAI CA Final Direct Tax Laws & International Taxation — Study Material/Module on Capital Gains (relevant chapter), for structure of Sec. 45(3)/(4)/9B, Rule 8AB and JDA provisions consistent with the current CA Final syllabus.

02. Income from Other Sources & Taxation of Dividend/Deemed Dividend

Where it fits: Residuary head (Sec. 56–59) that taxes gifts/undervalued property, casual income, family pension, and interest, and then hands off into how shareholders are taxed on real dividends and on transactions the Act artificially recharges as "deemed dividend" u/s 2(22)(a)-(e).

Sec. 56(2)(x) — Gifts / Property received without or for inadequate consideration

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Money received without consideration: entire sum taxable if aggregate > ₹50,000 in the P.Y.
  • Immovable property received without consideration: Stamp Duty Value (SDV) taxable if SDV > ₹50,000.
  • Immovable property received for inadequate consideration: taxable amount is—

Taxable = SDV - Consideration, only if (SDV - Consideration) > max(₹50,000, 10% of Consideration)

  • Movable property (shares/securities, jewellery, drawings, paintings, sculptures, archaeological collections, any work of art, bullion, virtual digital assets — 10 specified categories) received without consideration: FMV taxable if FMV > ₹50,000.
  • Movable property for inadequate consideration: taxable amount is—

Taxable = FMV - Consideration, only if this excess > ₹50,000

  • Concept: Anti-abuse provision to tax gifts/undervalued transfers of money and specified property (both movable & immovable) as Income from Other Sources, subject to a relative/occasion-based exemption list u/s 56(2)(x) proviso.
  • Not applicable / exempt cases (CBDT Notification No. 40/2020 + Finance Act amendments):
  • Immovable property received by a resident of an unauthorised colony in NCT Delhi where CG has regularised the transaction.
  • Unquoted shares received by a shareholder pursuant to an NCLT-approved resolution plan (company under CG-appointed new directors after BOD suspension).
  • Equity shares of Yes Bank Ltd. received under the Yes Bank Ltd. Reconstruction Scheme, 2020.
  • Equity shares of a public sector company received from CG/SG under strategic disinvestment.
  • Covid-19 relief money received by an individual for treatment expenses (no limit), or by a family member of a deceased person within 12 months of death — without limit if from the employer, up to ₹10 lakh if from any other person(s) (death must be within 6 months of testing Covid positive).
  • Any property received as gift/inadequate consideration other than the 10 specified categories (e.g., car, iPhone, TV, furniture, wrist watch) — not taxable even if value exceeds ₹50,000, since Sec. 56(2)(x) only covers specified "property".
  • Property received on occasions covered by the relative/marriage/will/inheritance exemption, or from specified trusts/funds u/s 10(23C), registered u/s 12A/12AB, in contemplation of death, or under Sec. 47 exempt transfers — clauses (i), (iv), (v), (vi), (via), (viaa), (vib), (vic), (vica), (vicb), (vid), (vii), (viiac), (viiad), (viiae), (viiaf).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Sec. 56(2)(x) applies only if the property is a capital asset in the hands of the recipient; if received as stock-in-trade, Sec. 56(2)(x) does not apply (Note 5).
  • Applies even to gift of money made outside India by a Resident to a Non-Resident (Note 6).
  • If assessee disputes SDV, case may be referred to the Valuation Officer (VO), mirroring Sec. 50C machinery.
  • If date of agreement and date of registration differ, SDV on the date of agreement can be adopted, provided at least part of the consideration was paid on/before the agreement date by account-payee cheque/DD/ECS through a bank account.
  • Sec. 49(4): where COA is fixed at the FMV/SDV already taxed u/s 56(2)(x), the previous owner's holding period is NOT included while computing the recipient's period of holding.
  • Bonus shares: no "release of assets" occurs, so bonus share allotment is not hit by Sec. 56(2)(x) — confirmed judicially in Dr. Ranjan Pai (2021, Kar).
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Relative (Individual)Spouse; brother/sister of self or spouse; brother/sister of either parent; lineal ascendant/descendant of self or spouse; spouse of any of the aforesaid
Relative (HUF)Any member of the HUF
SDVStamp Duty Value — value adopted/assessed/assessable by a state authority for stamp duty on transfer of immovable property
Specified movable propertyShares & securities, jewellery, drawings, paintings, sculptures, archaeological collections, any other work of art, bullion, immovable property, Virtual Digital Assets

Sec. 43CA — SDV as deemed sale consideration for stock-in-trade (immovable property)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

If SDV > 110% × Actual Consideration ⇒ Deemed Sale Consideration (for PGBP) = SDV

  • Applies where immovable property is held as stock-in-trade and transferred; contrast with Sec. 50C which applies where it is a capital asset.
  • Concept: Business-income parallel of Sec. 50C — prevents under-reporting of sale consideration on transfer of immovable property forming stock-in-trade.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Decision tree: Capital Asset → Sec. 50C → Capital Gains | Stock-in-Trade → Sec. 43CA → PGBP.
  • Same VO-reference right and same "agreement-date SDV" concession (part/full consideration by A/c payee cheque/DD/ECS up to agreement date) as Sec. 50C.
  • The 110% safe-harbour tolerance band (raised from 105%) applies identically under Sec. 43CA and Sec. 50C.

Sec. 56(2)(xi) — Compensation on termination of employment

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): Any compensation (or consideration for modification of terms of employment) received from a person other than the employer → taxable as IFOS.
  • Concept: Plugs the gap where such compensation is received from a third party; if received from the employer, it is taxed as "Salaries" u/s 17(3)(i), not under IFOS.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Always check the payer first — employer vs non-employer decides the head of income.

Sec. 57 — Allowable deductions from Income from Other Sources

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Deduction for interest on dividend/MF income = min≤ft(Interest expense, 20% × Dividend or MF/UTI income)
Deduction for family pension = min≤ft(tfrac13× Family pension, ₹15,000) [₹25,000 if opting default/new regime u/s 115BAC]
Deduction for interest on compensation/enhanced compensation (Sec. 56(2)(viii)) = 50% × such interest

  • Only interest expenditure (not other charges like collection charges) qualifies for the 20% cap deduction on dividend/MF income — no deduction for any other expense against such dividend.
  • Any other expenditure (not capital in nature) is allowable if incurred wholly and exclusively for earning such income (residual clause).
  • Concept: Sec. 57 lists the specific and general deductions permitted while computing IFOS — mirrors the PGBP "wholly & exclusively" test but is narrower for dividend/MF and family pension.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Dividend/collection charges, demat charges etc. are never deductible — only interest on borrowed capital, capped at 20% of the dividend/MF income (classic exam trap: students deduct actual interest without capping, or add collection charges).
  • For interest u/s 56(2)(viii), the flat 50% deduction is a standard deduction — no other clause of Sec. 57 can be additionally claimed against that interest.
  • Family pension exemptions (outside Sec. 57 deduction) exist separately: pension to family of armed-forces personnel dying in operational duty is fully exempt u/s 10(19); pension to family of a CG/SG employee awarded Param Vir Chakra/Ashok Chakra/Maha Vir Chakra or other notified gallantry award is exempt u/s 10(18)(ii).
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Family pensionRegular payment made by an employer to family members of a deceased employee
Enhanced compensationAdditional compensation awarded (e.g., on appeal) over and above original compulsory-acquisition compensation

Sec. 58 — Expenses NOT deductible under IFOS

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Disallowance for cash payment = Full expenditure, if any single payment > ₹10,000 (Sec. 40A(3) applied)
Disallowance for non-deduction of TDS (resident payee) = 30% × sum payable (Sec. 40(a)(ia) applied)

  • Concept: Sec. 58 imports PGBP-style disallowances (cash payment limit, TDS default) into the IFOS computation and independently bars personal expenses and expenses tied to casual income.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Interest or salary payable outside India without TDS deduction/payment is wholly disallowed (no partial 30% relief as under domestic-resident TDS default).
  • No expenditure is allowed against casual income (lottery/game-show winnings etc.) at all — not even the wholly-and-exclusively type expenses.
  • Any personal expense of the assessee is never allowable.

Casual Income — Sec. 115BB

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Tax on winnings from lotteries, crossword puzzles, races, card games, gambling/betting = 30% (flat, plus applicable surcharge & cess)

  • Concept: Flat special rate overrides the head of income — even if such winnings were somehow held to be business income, Sec. 115BB still taxes them at 30% (per Manju & Co. (2011), Kerala HC).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: No deduction, no basic exemption limit, and no Chapter VI-A deduction is available against casual income.

Taxation of Dividend & Deemed Dividend — Basic Framework

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Dividend from domestic or foreign company → taxable in shareholder's hands at normal slab/tax rates (Sec. 115BBDA's 10% additional tax on dividend > ₹10 lakh stood withdrawn once dividend became fully taxable in the recipient's hands w.e.f. AY 2021-22).
  • Year of taxability:
  • Final dividend → year in which declared at the AGM.
  • Interim dividend → year in which received by the shareholder.
  • Deemed dividend → year in which distributed/paid by the company.
  • Concept: Since the dividend distribution tax (DDT) regime was withdrawn (Finance Act 2020), dividends are back to being taxed conventionally in the hands of shareholders, with distinct trigger points for interim vs final vs deemed dividend.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: A very common exam trap: match each dividend cash-flow to the correct P.Y. using the three different triggers above, not merely the date of receipt.
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Indian CompanyCompany formed and registered under the Companies Act, 2013 (or earlier corresponding law) in India
Domestic CompanyAn Indian Company, or any other (including foreign) company that has made prescribed arrangements for declaration & payment of dividends within India
Foreign CompanyA company that is not a Domestic Company

Sec. 2(22)(a)/(b)/(c)/(d) — Deemed Dividend (all companies)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): Each limb is deemed dividend to the extent of accumulated profits (whether capitalised or not) of the company:
  • 2(22)(a): Any distribution of assets by the company to shareholders.
  • 2(22)(b): Distribution of debentures/debenture-stock/deposit certificates to shareholders, or bonus shares to preference shareholders.
  • 2(22)(c): Distribution of assets on liquidation.
  • 2(22)(d): Distribution to shareholders on reduction of share capital.

Deemed Dividend (a/b/c/d) = min(Value of distribution, Accumulated Profits (incl. capitalised))

  • Concept: These four limbs apply to all companies (widely-held and closely-held alike) and tax the shareholder on the value of the benefit to the extent accumulated profits exist.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Issue of bonus shares is not deemed dividend under 2(22)(a) — there is no "release of assets" of the company.
  • Where assets are distributed under 2(22)(a)/(c)/(d), the FMV of the asset on date of distribution is the value considered as dividend.
  • "Accumulated profits" for (a)-(d) includes capitalised profits (e.g., amounts transferred to capital reserve, bonus issue) — a wider base than for 2(22)(e).
  • If the company has accumulated losses, none of these deeming provisions apply.

Sec. 2(22)(e) — Deemed Dividend: Loans/Advances by a Closely Held Company

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Deemed Dividend u/s 2(22)(e) = min(Loan/Advance given, Accumulated Profits (excl. capitalised, as per Companies Act))

  • Applies only to a closely held company (company in which the public are not substantially interested) granting a loan/advance to:
  • a shareholder holding not less than 10% of the voting power, or
  • a "concern" in which such shareholder holds a substantial interest (≥ 20% share in profits/voting power/PSR).
  • "Substantial interest" (general test used across the Act, incl. for the concern) = 20% or more of voting power/profit-sharing at any time during the P.Y.
  • Concept: Targets the classic tax-avoidance route of a closely-held company routing profits to its controlling shareholder (or an entity they control) as a "loan" instead of a dividend, so as to avoid dividend taxation.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Even if the loan is subsequently repaid, or the company charges a market rate of interest on it, the amount is still treated as deemed dividend at the time it was given.
  • "Accumulated profits" here = accounting profits per the Companies Act, NOT the assessable/taxable profits computed under the Income-tax Act — a key distinguishing point vs profits under 2(22)(a)-(d).
  • Trade advances (advances in the nature of a genuine commercial transaction, e.g., advance for job work, or for installing plant & machinery at the shareholder's premises to execute the company's export order) are excluded — CBDT Circular No. 19/2017.
  • Where the loan/advance is given to a "concern", it is deemed dividend taxable in the hands of the concern; however, several court rulings have taxed it in the hands of the shareholder instead — a live controversy, flag both views in an exam answer.
  • Dividend excluded under proviso to 2(22): (a) loans/advances by a company where money-lending is a substantial part of its business (SPOB) (fact-based test — turnover, profit, manpower, capital employed); (b) any dividend later paid by the company that is set off against a loan already taxed as deemed dividend u/s 2(22)(e); (c) shares allotted by the resulting company to shareholders of a demerged company under a demerger; (d) distribution u/s 2(22)(c)/(d) in respect of preference shares; (e) inter-group loans/advances where one entity is a "Finance company/unit" and the group's parent/principal entity is listed on a foreign stock exchange.
  • Vir Vikram Vaid (2014, Bom): Repair/renovation expenditure incurred by the company (as lessee) on a building owned by a shareholder is not deemed dividend — no money was "paid" to the shareholder.
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
ConcernHUF, Firm, Company, or AOP/BOI (in which the shareholder has a substantial interest)
Substantial interest (concern)Beneficial holding of ≥ 20% of the profits of the concern at any time during the P.Y.
SPOBSubstantial Part Of the Business — money-lending forming a genuinely significant part of the company's overall business

Sec. 80M — Deduction for Inter-Corporate Dividend

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Deduction u/s 80M = min(Aggregate dividend income received (incl. deemed dividend), Dividend distributed by the assessee-company up to the "due date")

  • "Due date" = one month before the due date for filing the return of income u/s 139(1).
  • Available to a domestic company that includes in its GTI dividend received from another domestic company, a foreign company, or a business trust.
  • Concept: Removes the cascading effect of taxing dividend at each corporate layer by allowing a deduction for dividend received-and-redistributed within the specified window (reintroduced by Finance Act 2020 after DDT abolition).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Only the dividend actually received and redistributed by the due date qualifies — dividend distributed after the due date does not count for the deduction, even if distributed within the same P.Y.
  • Deduction is claimed under Chapter VI-A against Gross Total Income, so it cannot exceed GTI and follows normal Chapter VI-A ordering rules.
  • The "dividend income received" limb of the Sec. 80M comparison is the amount actually included in Gross Total Income, i.e. dividend net of the Sec. 57 interest deduction (not the gross dividend received) — confirmed by the standard worked illustration where net dividend of ₹9,60,000 (after 20% interest deduction) is used, not the gross ₹12,00,000.
  • Sree Rama Multi Tech Ltd. (2018, SC): Interest earned on share-application money kept in a separate mandatory bank account (pending allotment) is incidental to a statutory compliance requirement, not an independent intention to earn interest — hence set off against public-issue expenses and not taxed as IFOS.

References

  1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sec. 56(2)(x), Sec. 57, Sec. 58, Sec. 2(22)(a)-(e), Sec. 80M, Sec. 43CA, Sec. 115BB (bare act text, incometaxindia.gov.in).
  2. CBDT Notification No. 40/2020 — exemptions from Sec. 56(2)(x) (unauthorised colonies, NCLT resolution plans, Yes Bank scheme, strategic disinvestment).
  3. CBDT Circular No. 19/2017 — trade advances excluded from Sec. 2(22)(e) deemed dividend.
  4. Finance Act, 2020 — abolition of Dividend Distribution Tax and introduction of Sec. 80M; Finance Act, 2020 raising the Sec. 43CA/50C safe-harbour to 110%.
  5. Case laws: Manju & Co. (2011) Kerala HC; Dr. Ranjan Pai (2021) Kar HC; Vir Vikram Vaid (2014) Bom HC; Sree Rama Multi Tech Ltd. (2018) SC.

03. Corporate Reorganisation: Liquidation, Buy-Back, Amalgamation & Demerger

Where it fits: This chapter covers the capital-gains and deemed-dividend consequences when a company winds up (liquidation), buys back its own shares, merges with another company (amalgamation), or spins off an undertaking (demerger) — a recurring 6-10 mark area in CA Final DT, tested both as standalone theory and inside larger capital-gains problems.

Liquidation

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • In the hands of the company: distribution of assets to shareholders on liquidation is deemed dividend to the extent of accumulated profits u/s 2(22)(c); but the distribution itself is not a "transfer" u/s 46(1), so the company has no capital gains.
  • In the hands of the shareholder, capital gain on liquidation:

FVOC = (Money received + FMV of asset received on date of distribution) - Amount already taxed as deemed dividend u/s 2(22)(c)

STCG/LTCG = FVOC - COA/ICOA of shares

  • Cost of the asset so received by the shareholder (for its subsequent sale) = FMV on the date of distribution [Sec. 55].
  • Concept: Liquidation triggers two separate tax events — dividend taxation at the company/shareholder interface, and capital gains on the shareholder's shares (not on the underlying assets, which the company transfers tax-free under 46(1)).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Do not tax the company on liquidation distribution — a common trap is applying capital gains at the company level.
  • Period of holding of shares = date of acquisition of shares to date of liquidation.
  • Capital gain is taxable in the shareholder's hands in the year assets are actually received, not the year the company goes into liquidation.
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Deemed dividend u/s 2(22)(c)Distribution on liquidation, to the extent of accumulated profits (whether capitalised or not), immediately before liquidation
FVOCFull value of consideration for the shareholder's capital gains computation

Buy-Back — Unlisted/Foreign Shares & Other Specified Securities (pre-existing regime)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • No tax in the hands of the company on buy-back of shares/specified securities (other than domestic company shares covered below).
  • Shareholder — capital gains u/s 46A:

STCG/LTCG = Buy-back price (FVOC) - COA/ICOA of shares

  • Period of holding = date of acquisition to date of buy-back.
  • Concept: Sec. 46A treats buy-back as extinguishment of shareholder rights, taxed as capital gains at the buy-back price.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Where any part of the buy-back consideration is separately taxed as deemed dividend u/s 2(22)(f), FVOC for 46A purposes becomes NIL for that amount [inserted by Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024, w.e.f. 01-10-2024] — see next section for the current domestic-company regime.

Buy-Back of Shares by a Domestic Company — w.e.f. 1 October 2024

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • No tax in the hands of the company (Sec. 115QA does not apply to buy-backs undertaken on or after 01-10-2024).
  • Entire buy-back consideration received by the shareholder is deemed dividend u/s 2(22)(f), taxable under IFOS at normal slab/applicable rates (no deduction for cost of acquisition against this dividend income).
  • Simultaneously, u/s 46A, buy-back is treated as extinguishment of rights, but FVOC is deemed NIL:

STCL/LTCL = NIL - COA of shares = -(COA of shares)

  • This capital loss can be set off against any other STCG/LTCG (as applicable) and carried forward for 8 assessment years.
  • TDS: company deducts tax at source on the deemed dividend u/s 194 (10% for residents, subject to threshold) / Sec. 195 for non-residents.
