Where it fits: Covers the special assessee-status rules of Chapter I (Sec 13A/13B political parties & electoral trusts), the firm/LLP taxation code (Sec 40(b), 78, 184-189), and AOP/BOI taxation (Sec 40(ba), 167B, 67A, 86) — a recurring 4-8 mark theory + computation area in CA Final DT, often clubbed with a firm/AOP total-income problem.

Political Parties — Sec 13A

  • Key rule(s):
  • Income of a political party under the heads House Property, Capital Gains, Other Sources, and Voluntary Contributions/Donations is exempt, subject to ALL of the following conditions:
  • Must maintain books of account and other documents.
  • Must get its books of account audited.
  • Must keep and maintain a record of each voluntary contribution/donation > ₹20,000 received by it (name & address of donor), except contributions received through Electoral Bonds.
  • Must not receive a donation > ₹2,000 otherwise than by A/c payee cheque, A/c payee DD, ECS, or Electoral Bonds.
  • Must file its Return of Income on or before the due date under Sec 139(4B).
  • Income under Salary is not possible for a political party (no such head arises).
  • Income under PGBP, if any, is fully taxable (no exemption under Sec 13A extends to business income).
  • Concept: Sec 13A grants a conditional exemption to recognised/registered political parties on specified heads of income to keep election funding transparent and traceable; failure of any condition forfeits exemption on that head.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Exemption is head-specific (HP/CG/IFOS/Donations) — PGBP income of a political party (rare, e.g., sale of publications) is NOT covered and is fully taxable.
  • The ₹20,000 record-keeping threshold and the ₹2,000 banking-mode threshold are two different limits — do not conflate them in exam answers.
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — The Electoral Bond Scheme referred to in the "except through electoral bonds" carve-out was struck down as unconstitutional by the Supreme Court (Association for Democratic Reforms v. Union of India, Feb 2024) and bonds are no longer issued; the statutory text of Sec 13A is unchanged, but candidates should note the scheme is currently non-operative in practice even though the section still references it.

Electoral Trust — Sec 13B

  • Key formula/rule:

Exemption available if: Distribution to political parties ≥ 95% × (Current year donations + Surplus b/f)

  • AND the trust functions in accordance with the rules framed by the Central Government (Electoral Trusts Scheme, 2013).
  • Only donation income is exempt — other income (e.g., interest on deposits) of the electoral trust is fully taxable.
  • Contribution must be received only from permitted sources, only after the donor furnishes PAN (resident) / Passport No. (non-resident donor), and only by A/c payee cheque, DD or ECS.
  • Admin expenses cap: electoral trust may spend up to 5% of total donations received toward managing its affairs, subject to a ceiling of ₹5 lakh in the 1st year and ₹3 lakh in subsequent years. Funds cannot be used for direct/indirect benefit of members/contributors.
  • Books of account must be audited by a CA in Form 10BC, filed along with the return of income on or before the due date under Sec 139(1).
  • Concept: An electoral trust is a pass-through vehicle — it collects donations from permitted sources and (almost entirely) channels them onward to registered political parties; it is taxed only if it fails the 95% distribution/rules test.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • The 95% test applies to (current year donation + b/f surplus) — not current year donation alone.
  • Distinguish the electoral trust's own due date (Sec 139(1)) from the political party's due date (Sec 139(4B)).
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Permitted sourcesIndividual Indian citizen; Indian company; resident firm/HUF/AOP/BOI
Non-permitted sourcesNon-Indian citizen individual; any foreign entity/source; any other electoral trust; Government company

Deduction for Donation to Political Party / Electoral Trust — Sec 80GGB / 80GGC

  • Key rule:
  • 100% deduction of the sum contributed to a registered political party or an electoral trust:
  • Sec 80GGB — available to an Indian company.
  • Sec 80GGC — available to any other assessee (except local authority and every artificial juridical person wholly/partly funded by government).
  • Deduction is NOT available for cash donations.
  • Concept: Mirrors the Sec 13A/13B transparency objective on the donor's side — banking-channel donations only get the tax break.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: A common trick question gives a cash donation to a political party — deduction is fully denied (not restricted, denied entirely for that donation).

Taxation of Firm / LLP — Rates & Basic Scheme

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Tax on Total Income of Firm/LLP = 30% × NTI + Surcharge (12% if NTI > ₹1 crore) + 4% HEC (on tax + surcharge)

  • Special-rate capital gains for firm/LLP (rates applicable for PY 2025-26 / AY 2026-27, post Finance (No.2) Act 2024 restructuring effective transfers on/after 23-07-2024):

LTCG u/s 112 = 12.5% (no indexation); STCG u/s 111A = 20%; LTCG u/s 112A = 12.5% on gains > ₹1,25,000

  • Share of a partner in the total income of the firm/LLP is exempt in the hands of the partner u/s 10(2A).
  • Interest & remuneration paid to partners is allowed to the firm/LLP only up to the Sec 40(b) limits; the same amount actually allowed is taxable to the partner as PGBP income (not more, not less).
  • Sec 44AD / 44ADA (presumptive taxation) are NOT applicable to LLP (available only to eligible individual/HUF/firm-other-than-LLP).
  • Losses of the firm are carried forward by the firm only and are never allocated out to partners.
  • Concept: A firm/LLP is taxed as a single, separate unit at a flat rate; the partner-level taxation is only a pass-through of interest/remuneration actually allowed to the firm, while profit-share itself is tax-exempt to avoid double taxation.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — the OCR source shows transition-year dual rates ("20/12.5%", "15/20%", "10/12.5%") reflecting the mid-year rate change of 23-07-2024 relevant only to PY 2024-25 (AY 2025-26); for PY 2025-26 (AY 2026-27, the year tested in May/Nov 2026 attempts) a full year at the post-amendment rates (12.5% / 20% / 12.5%) should apply — confirm against the Finance Act applicable to the specific attempt before the exam.
  • Firm-level surcharge is a flat 12% (no slabs) once NTI crosses ₹1 crore, but marginal relief still applies at the crossover point.

Sec 40(b) — Interest, Remuneration to Partners: Conditions & Limits

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): Conditions for allowability as deduction to the firm/LLP:
  1. Remuneration paid only to a working partner.
  2. Remuneration & interest must be authorised by the partnership deed.
  3. Remuneration & interest must relate to the period after the date of the partnership deed (no retrospective effect).
  4. Interest on partner's capital/loan allowed max @ 12% p.a. simple interest.
  5. Remuneration allowed on Book Profit basis — limits amended by Finance Act 2024, w.e.f. AY 2025-26:

Remuneration allowed = ₹3,00,000 or 90%×Book Profit, whichever is more & on first ₹6,00,000 of Book Profit (or in case of a loss) [4pt] 60% × Book Profit & on the balance of Book Profit

  • Meaning of Book Profit:

Book Profit = Net Profit as per PGBP - (Current year + b/f depreciation) + Remuneration to partners (if debited to P&L A/c)
In simple terms: Book Profit = PGBP income before deducting partners' remuneration.

  • Concept: Sec 40(b) is a ceiling provision — remuneration/interest paid in excess of the deed authorisation or the statutory slab is disallowed in the firm's hands (and correspondingly not taxable to the partner, since only the "allowed" amount is taxed under PGBP in partner's hands).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Always compute Book Profit before remuneration, then apply the slab — a common error is applying the slab to profit-after-remuneration.
  • The old (pre-FA24) slabs were ₹1,50,000/90% on first ₹3,00,000 and 60% on balance — do not use these for AY 2025-26 onward.
  • If deed is silent on quantum but specifies the manner of computing remuneration, deduction is still allowed (see case law below).
  • Explanation — Individual vs Representative capacity (applies only to Interest, not remuneration):
Partner onInterest received onTreatment
Individual capacityIndividual capacitySec 40(b) applies — max 12% allowed
Representative capacityRepresentative capacitySec 40(b) applies — max 12% allowed
Individual capacityRepresentative capacitySec 40(b) NOT applicable — interest > 12% also allowed
Representative capacityIndividual capacitySec 40(b) NOT applicable — interest > 12% also allowed

Note: this cross-capacity relaxation is available only for interest; remuneration is always subject to the Sec 40(b) limit irrespective of capacity.

Sec 78 — Carry Forward & Set-off of Losses of a Firm

  • Key rule(s):
  • Losses and unabsorbed depreciation of the firm can be carried forward by the firm only.
  • On retirement or death of a partner, the firm cannot carry forward that retired/deceased partner's share in the firm's losses (after first adjusting the current year's profit against that share) — Sec 78 restriction applies to losses only, not unabsorbed depreciation, which the firm can carry forward in full even after a partner exits.
  • If the legal heir of a deceased partner is admitted as a partner, the firm can carry forward and set off the losses in full (no forfeiture).
  • Concept: Sec 78 protects continuing partners from inheriting a departed partner's disproportionate share of past losses, while depreciation (an asset-linked, not partner-linked, allowance) is unaffected.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Work the retiring/deceased partner's loss-share net of his proportionate current-year profit (time-apportioned to his period as partner) — only the residual (unabsorbed) loss-share is forfeited.
  • Worked example (from source, illustrative): X, Y, Z equal partners; B/f loss PY 24-25 = ₹8,00,000; unabsorbed depreciation PY 23-24 = ₹1,10,000; PY 25-26 profit = ₹9,30,000; Z retires 30-06-25 (3 months into the year).
  • Z's share in b/f loss = 8,00,000 / 3 = ₹2,66,667
  • Less: Z's share in current year profit = 9,30,000 × (3/12) / 3 = ₹77,500
  • Z's loss forfeited (not c/f by firm) = ₹1,89,167
  • Total Income of firm, PY 25-26: Net profit 9,30,000 − b/f loss allowed (8,00,000 − 1,89,167 = 6,10,833) = 3,19,167; less unabsorbed depreciation 1,10,000 → Total Income = ₹2,09,167

Sec 184/185/187/188/188A/189/167C — Assessment & Continuity of Firms

  • Key rule(s):
  • Sec 184 (Assessment as a firm): firm is assessed as a firm only if (i) there is a partnership deed, (ii) the deed specifies the profit-sharing ratio (PSR), and (iii) the deed is furnished along with the firm's first return.
  • Sec 185: if the above conditions are not satisfied, or the firm has committed a default u/s 144, then interest/remuneration paid to partners is fully disallowed in the firm's hands and correspondingly not taxable in the partner's hands.
  • Sec 187 (Change in constitution): applies when (i) one or more partners are admitted/retire but at least one partner common to before-and-after continues, or (ii) all partners continue but the PSR changes — only one return is filed for the year.
  • Sec 188 (Succession of firm): where one firm is succeeded by another firm, separate assessments are made on the predecessor and successor firms — two returns for the year.
  • Sec 188A: every person who was a partner at any time during the PY is jointly and severally liable, along with the firm, for tax, penalty, etc. of the firm for that PY.
  • Sec 189 (Dissolution/discontinuance): the AO assesses the firm as if no dissolution/discontinuance occurred; every person who was a partner at the time of dissolution/discontinuance remains jointly & severally liable for tax/penalty for all the assessment years since the firm's formation.
  • Sec 167C: partners of an LLP have unlimited joint & several liability for tax purposes (notwithstanding limited liability under the LLP Act).
  • Concept: These sections ensure continuity of assessment and collection of tax dues despite changes in a firm's membership, restructuring, or dissolution.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Classic exam distinction — Change in constitution = one return; Succession = two returns (predecessor's period + successor's period). Example: ABC→AB or AB→ABD = change in constitution; ABC→DEF (entirely new set of partners) = succession.

Important Case Laws (Firm/LLP)

CasePrinciple
Anil Hardware Store (2010, HP)If the deed does not state the exact remuneration but lays down the manner of computing it, deduction for remuneration paid is still allowed.
Great City Manufacturing Co. (2013, All)Remuneration paid per the deed within the Sec 40(b) statutory limit is allowable even if "unreasonable/excessive" — AO cannot invoke Sec 40A(2) to disallow it.
Pramod Mittal (2013, Del HC)Losses of a dissolved firm cannot be carried forward by a partner who takes over the business as sole proprietor — that is not "succession by inheritance" under Sec 78(2), so the c/f exception does not apply.

Taxation of AOP/BOI

  • Key rule(s) — Sec 40(ba):
  • Interest, salary, bonus, commission paid by an AOP/BOI to its members is fully disallowed while computing PGBP (no 12%-type limit as with firms — total disallowance).
  • If the AOP/BOI also receives interest from the same member to whom it pays interest, only the net interest (interest paid − interest received from that member) is disallowed.
  • Loss of the AOP/BOI is carried forward by the AOP/BOI only.
  • If AOP/BOI is taxed at slab/normal rates, its special-rate incomes (LTCG/STCG 111A/LTCG 112A) are still taxed at their own special rates. If AOP/BOI is taxed at MMR (or a higher rate), its special-rate incomes are taxed at MMR (or that higher rate), not at the normal special rates.
  • Key rule(s) — Sec 167B (rate of tax on AOP/BOI):
  • Where shares of members are indeterminate/unknown: tax on the AOP/BOI's total income is charged at the Maximum Marginal Rate (MMR) — except that if any member's own income is taxable at a rate higher than MMR, the portion of AOP/BOI income relatable to that member is taxed at such higher rate, and the balance at MMR.
  • Where shares of members are known/determinate:
  • If any member's total income (excluding share from the AOP/BOI) exceeds the basic exemption limit → AOP/BOI's total income is taxed at MMR (subject to the same "higher-rate member" exception above).
  • Else if any member is taxable at a rate higher than MMR (e.g., a company member) → the portion attributable to that member is taxed at such higher rate, balance at MMR.
  • In any other case (no member above the exemption limit and none taxed higher than MMR) → AOP/BOI is taxed at normal slab rates applicable to an individual.
  • MMR figures for AY 2026-27:

MMR (default regime, Sec 115BAC) = 30% + 25% surcharge + 4% HEC = 39%
MMR (other than default regime) = 30% + 37% surcharge + 4% HEC = 42.744%
MMR — AOP with ALL members being companies (surcharge capped at 15%) = 30% × 1.15 × 1.04 = 35.88%

  • Concept: Sec 167B prevents members from routing income through an AOP/BOI to escape their own higher slab/rate, by testing each member's stand-alone tax position against the AOP/BOI's default rate.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • "Indeterminate shares" (167B(1)) and "determinate shares with a high-income member" (167B(2)) are tested differently — do not merge the two limbs in an answer.
  • Since Sec 115BAC's default regime now extends to AOP/BOI/AJP (other than co-operative societies), the applicable MMR depends on which regime the AOP/BOI is actually taxed under.
  • Key rule(s) — Sec 67A (computing a member's share in AOP/BOI income):

Step 1: Net Taxable Income (NTI) of AOP/BOI = PGBP etc. after disallowing interest/remuneration to members u/s 40(ba)
Step 2: Amount allocable in PSR = NTI of AOP/BOI - Interest & remuneration paid to members
Step 3: Member's total share = (Step 2 amount allocated in his PSR) + (Interest & remuneration paid to that specific member)

  • Concept: A member's "share" is not just his PSR-based slice of profit — it also picks up back the interest/remuneration paid to him personally, since that amount was disallowed to the AOP/BOI under Sec 40(ba).
  • Key rule(s) — Sec 86 (Rebate on member's share):

Rebate u/s 86 = Tax liability of member (incl. surcharge & HEC) × Share from AOP/BOI (u/s 67A)Total Income of member

  • Rebate applies only if the AOP/BOI has itself paid tax at the slab/normal rate (i.e., member's share was includible in his total income); no rebate is available if the tax payable by the AOP/BOI is Nil, and none is needed if AOP/BOI's income was already taxed at MMR (since in that case the member's share is not included in his total income at all).
  • Rebate is computed after adding surcharge and HEC to the tax liability.
  • Concept: Sec 86 avoids double taxation of the same income — once in the AOP/BOI's hands (at slab rate) and again in the member's hands — by giving the member a proportionate tax rebate.
  • Interest to Members — capacity table (parallels Sec 40(b) for firms):
Member onInterest received onTreatment
Individual capacityIndividual capacityDisallowed u/s 40(ba)
Representative capacityRepresentative capacityDisallowed u/s 40(ba)
Individual capacityRepresentative capacitySec 40(ba) not applicable — full interest allowed
Representative capacityIndividual capacitySec 40(ba) not applicable — full interest allowed
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Members-share inclusion + Sec 86 rebate is a favourite numerical: always check whether AOP paid tax at slab rate (rebate applies) or at MMR (share excluded from member's total income altogether, no rebate needed).
  • Remember interest disallowance u/s 40(ba) is total disallowance (no 12% carve-out as under Sec 40(b) for firms) — only the "net interest" softening applies when there's a reverse interest flow.

References

  1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 13A, 13B, 40(b), 40(ba), 44AD, 44ADA, 67A, 78, 80GGB, 80GGC, 86, 115BAC, 167B, 167C, 184, 185, 187, 188, 188A, 189 (as amended up to Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024, applicable for AY 2026-27).
  2. Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024 — revision of Sec 40(b) remuneration slabs (₹1,50,000/₹3,00,000 threshold → ₹3,00,000/₹6,00,000, w.e.f. AY 2025-26) and restructuring of capital gains rates under Sections 112/111A/112A effective transfers on/after 23-07-2024.
  3. Electoral Trusts Scheme, 2013 (CBDT notification) — permitted/non-permitted contribution sources, 5%/₹5-lakh-₹3-lakh admin expense cap, Form 10BC audit requirement.
  4. Supreme Court of India, Association for Democratic Reforms & Anr. v. Union of India (Feb 2024) — Electoral Bond Scheme held unconstitutional (relevant caveat to the Sec 13A "electoral bonds" carve-out).
  5. ICAI CA Final Direct Tax & International Taxation Study Material — chapters on Assessment of Firms/LLP and AOP/BOI (basis for Sec 78, 167B, 67A, 86 treatment structure).
  6. Case laws: Anil Hardware Store (2010) HP HC; Great City Manufacturing Co. (2013) All HC; Pramod Mittal (2013) Del HC — as reported in standard DT case-law digests.

07. Taxation of Business Trust, Investment Fund & Securitisation Trust

Where it fits: Covers the special pass-through/partial-pass-through tax codes of Chapter XII-FA/FB — Business Trust (REIT/InvIT, Sec 115UA), Investment Fund (Category I/II AIF, Sec 115UB) and Securitisation Trust (Sec 115TCA) — a recurring 4-8 mark theory/computation topic in CA Final DT, frequently tested with the exempt-income sections (10(23FC)/(23FCA)/(23FBA)/(23DA)) and the related TDS provisions (194LBA/194LBB/194LBC).

Business Trust (REIT/InvIT) — Taxability at Trust Level

  • Key rule(s):
  • Interest income and Dividend income received by the Business Trust from its SPV — fully exempt in the hands of the Business Trust u/s 10(23FC); consequently the SPV is not required to deduct TDS on such interest/dividend paid to the Business Trust.
  • Rental income of a REIT only (not InvIT) from renting/leasing/letting out any real estate asset directly owned by the REIT — exempt u/s 10(23FCA).
  • All other income of the Business Trust (i.e., other than the above two exempt streams) is taxable in the hands of the trust — Sec 115UA(2).
  • Concept: A Business Trust (REIT/InvIT) is a SEBI-registered pass-through vehicle holding controlling interest in one or more SPVs; the Act exempts the specific income streams at the trust level so that tax is collected instead at the unit-holder level (avoiding double taxation), while any other trust-level income is taxed normally.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Do not exempt the SPV's own income — only the interest/dividend/rental flowing from SPV to the Business Trust is exempt; the SPV itself is taxed as a normal Indian company.
  • Rental income exemption u/s 10(23FCA) is available only to a REIT, never to an InvIT (an InvIT does not directly hold real estate).
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Business TrustA REIT (Real Estate Investment Trust) or InvIT (Infrastructure Investment Trust) registered under SEBI Regulations
SPV⚠️ VERIFY — Commonly defined (per SEBI REIT/InvIT Regulations, referenced into the Explanation to Sec 10(23FC)) as an Indian company/LLP in which the Business Trust holds (or proposes to hold) controlling interest and not less than 50% of equity share capital/interest — exact percentage threshold should be cross-checked against the current SEBI Regulations text for the relevant AY

Taxability in Hands of Unit Holders — Interest, Dividend, Rental

  • Key rule(s) — Interest (received by Business Trust from SPV, distributed to unit holders):
  • Taxable in the hands of the unit holder:
  • Non-resident/Foreign Company — 5%
  • Resident — Normal (slab/applicable) tax rates
  • TDS by Business Trust u/s 194LBA:
  • NR/Foreign Co. payee — 5%
  • Resident payee — 10%
  • Key rule(s) — Dividend (received by Business Trust from SPV):
  • Dividend is always exempt in the hands of the Business Trust u/s 10(23FC).
  • At the unit-holder level, taxability turns on whether the SPV opted for the concessional corporate tax regime u/s 115BAA (22%):
  • If SPV has opted for 115BAA → dividend passed on is taxable in the hands of unit holders: NR/Foreign Company — 10%; Resident — Normal tax rates. TDS u/s 194LBA: NR/FC payee — 10%; Resident payee — 10%.
  • If SPV has NOT opted for 115BAA (paying tax under normal provisions) → dividend is exempt both in the hands of the Business Trust (Sec 10(23FC)) and in the hands of unit holders (Sec 10(23FD)) — no TDS.
  • Key rule(s) — Rental income (REIT only, distributed to unit holders):
  • Always taxable in the hands of the unit holder (since it was exempt only at the REIT level under 10(23FCA)):
  • NR/Foreign Company — Normal tax rates
  • Resident — Normal tax rates
  • TDS u/s 194LBA:
  • NR/Foreign Co. payee — Rate in force (i.e., the rate applicable to that recipient under the Finance Act/DTAA)
  • Resident payee — 10%
  • Concept: The Act uses SPV's own choice of tax regime (115BAA or not) as the trigger for whether dividend income continues down the pass-through chain tax-free or becomes taxable at the unit-holder level — this prevents under-taxation when the SPV itself is paying tax at a lower flat rate.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Interest is always taxable at unit-holder level (never fully exempt); dividend's exemption chain depends on the SPV's 115BAA election; rental is always taxable at unit-holder level. Do not mix up the three.
  • Resident unit holders are taxed at "normal rates," not a flat percentage — do not apply the 5%/10% NR rates to residents.
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
10(23FC)Exemption to Business Trust for interest & (conditionally) dividend from SPV
10(23FCA)Exemption to REIT for rental income from directly held real estate
10(23FD)Exemption to unit holder for distributed income already suffering the above trust-level treatment
194LBATDS section for Business Trust distributions to unit holders

Sec 56(2)(xii) — Specified Sum (Anti-Abuse for "Repayment of Debt" Distributions)

  • Key formula:

Specified Sum = A - B - C (deemed NIL if (B+C) > A)
where:

  • A = Aggregate sum distributed by the Business Trust during the PY which is (a) not in the nature of interest/dividend/rental referred to in 10(23FC)/10(23FCA), and (b) not chargeable to tax in the hands of the Business Trust u/s 115UA(2)
  • B = Amount at which the relevant unit was issued by the Business Trust
  • C = Amount already charged to tax under this clause in any earlier previous year
  • Concept: Introduced by the Finance Act 2023, w.e.f. AY 2024-25, to plug the gap where a Business Trust distributes cash to unit holders labelled as "repayment of debt" — a category that, absent this clause, escaped tax entirely both at the trust level (not PGBP, not interest/dividend/rental) and at the unit-holder level (not covered by any of the taxable/exempt heads above).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • This clause targets the fourth bucket of Business Trust distributions (interest, dividend, rental, and "other/repayment of debt") — students often forget this residual category exists.
  • Any distribution other than interest/dividend/rental/specified-sum-taxed-amount is exempt to the unit holder u/s 10(23FD).

Capital Gains on Transfer of Units of Business Trust

  • Key rule(s) — Listed units, STT paid (transaction on a recognised stock exchange, STT paid):
  • LTCG (period of holding > 12 months), taxable u/s 112A:

Tax = 12.5% × (LTCG - ₹1,25,000) (no indexation/no Chapter VI-A deduction against this LTCG)

  • Applicable for transfers on/after 23 July 2024; the ₹1,25,000 aggregate exemption applies per PY across all Sec 112A assets.
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — For transfers before 23 July 2024 the rate was 10% in excess of a ₹1,00,000 threshold; confirm which rate regime applies to the specific transaction date in a problem.
  • STCG (period of holding ≤ 12 months), taxable u/s 111A at 20% (flat) — for transfers on/after 23 July 2024; 15% for transfers before that date.
  • Key rule(s) — Unlisted units (or listed without STT):
  • LTCG — taxable u/s 112 at 12.5% without indexation (for transfers on/after 23 July 2024).
  • STCG — taxable at normal (slab) tax rates.
  • Concept: Business Trust units listed and STT-paid get the same concessional capital-gains regime as listed equity shares/equity-oriented MF units (112A/111A); unlisted units fall back to the general capital-gains code (112 for LTCG, normal rates for STCG).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Holding period threshold for units of a Business Trust (listed) to qualify as long-term is > 12 months, same as listed equity shares — do not apply the 24/36-month test meant for other unlisted assets.
  • Watch the transaction date relative to 23 July 2024 (Finance (No. 2) Act 2024 rate rationalisation) — this is a favourite examiner trap.

Exchange of SPV Shares for Units of Business Trust — Sec 47(xvii) / 49(2AC)

  • Key rule(s):
  • Where a person transfers shares of the SPV to the Business Trust in exchange for units of the Business Trust, such a transfer is not regarded as a transfer for capital gains purposes — Sec 47(xvii) — i.e., no capital gains arise at that point.
  • Cost of acquisition of the units so received = Cost of acquisition of the shares of the SPV given up — Sec 49(2AC).
  • Period of holding of the units (for subsequent sale) includes the period for which the SPV shares were held — i.e., holding periods of shares + units are aggregated.
  • Concept: This is a tax-neutral rollover — capital gains are deferred (not exempted permanently) until the unit itself is eventually sold, at which point the embedded gain from the original SPV shares is taxed along with any subsequent appreciation in the unit.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: A classic trick is to test capital gains on the SPV-share-for-unit swap itself — the correct answer is NIL capital gains at that step; the gain crystallises only on eventual sale of the units.

General Compliance Notes — Business Trust

  • Key rule(s):
  • Business Trust is compulsorily required to file its return of income — Sec 139(4E), regardless of income level.
  • Income distributed by the Business Trust to unit holders retains the same nature and same proportion in the hands of the unit holder as it had in the hands of the Business Trust — Sec 115UA(1).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: The "same nature, same proportion" pass-through principle (115UA(1)) is the backbone of the entire chapter — every distribution must first be characterised (interest/dividend/rental/other) before applying the taxability rules above.

Investment Fund (Category I / Category II AIF) — Sec 115UB

  • Key rule(s):
  • All income of the Investment Fund except business income (PGBP) — fully exempt in the hands of the fund, Sec 10(23FBA).
  • All income received by unit holders from the Investment Fund (except income in the nature of PGBP, already taxed at the fund level) — taxable in the hands of unit holders, Sec 115UB.
  • PGBP income taxed at the Investment Fund level itself, at the following rates:
  • Company/Firm — normal corporate/firm rate (Company: 25%/30% depending on turnover-based eligibility; Firm/LLP: 30%)
  • Other persons (e.g., trust/AOP/BOI form of fund) — Maximum Marginal Rate (MMR) — ⚠️ VERIFY — currently taken as ~39% (30% + 25% surcharge + 4% cess) under the default tax regime; confirm the applicable surcharge slab for the relevant AY as MMR is a moving target tied to Finance Act surcharge rates.
  • TDS on distribution (except PGBP income) by Investment Fund u/s 194LBB:
  • NR/Foreign Co. payee — Rate in force
  • Resident payee — 10%
  • Deemed credit rule: If income accrued/received by the fund during the PY has not actually been paid/credited to the unit holder, it is deemed to have been credited on the last day of the PY and taxed accordingly in that year; once taxed on accrual basis, it is not taxed again in the year of actual receipt.
  • Income retains the same nature and same proportion in unit holders' hands as accrued to/received by the fund.
  • Investment Fund is compulsorily required to file its return — Sec 139(4F).
  • Concept: An Investment Fund (Category I: start-up/SME/social/infra-focused AIFs e.g. VC funds, angel funds; Category II: PE, debt funds, fund-of-funds) regulated under SEBI (AIF) Regulations, 2012 or the IFSCA Act, 2019, gets a full pass-through except for its own business income, which is taxed at the fund level (because PGBP income cannot reliably be attributed to specific unit holders in real time).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Category III AIFs (hedge-fund-like, e.g. leveraged trading strategies) are not "Investment Funds" for this pass-through regime — do not extend 115UB benefits to them.
  • PGBP is the only carve-out from full exemption/pass-through — every other head (capital gains, house property, other sources) flows through untaxed at the fund level.
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Category I AIFStart-ups, SMEs, social/infra ventures — e.g. VC Funds, SME Funds, Social Venture Funds, Infrastructure Funds, Angel Funds
Category II AIFEquity/debt securities investing — e.g. Private Equity Funds, Debt Funds, Fund of Funds

Losses of Investment Fund [w.e.f. 01.04.2019]

  • Key rule(s):
  • Loss under any head at the fund level is first set-off by the fund internally against other heads of income for that PY.
  • Of the balance unabsorbed loss:
  • PGBP loss — carried forward and set-off by the fund only (not passed to unit holders).
  • Any other loss (non-PGBP) — passed on to unit holders who have held their units for 12 months or more, to be carried forward and set off in their individual hands.
  • If units have not been held for 12 months or more, the loss is not allowed to either the unit holder or the fund (it lapses).
  • Transition rule: Pre-01.04.2019, all losses (including non-PGBP) were carried forward by the fund only. Any accumulated non-PGBP losses as on 31.03.2019 are deemed distributed to unit holders holding units on that date, and are allowed to be carried forward/set off by those unit holders for the remaining permissible period.
  • Concept: Ensures loss pass-through mirrors income pass-through for non-business losses, while keeping business losses (which need continuity of business at fund level to be meaningful) locked at the fund.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: The 12-month minimum unit-holding condition for loss pass-through is a favourite numerical trap — a unit holder who bought units 6 months before the loss year gets no loss benefit at all (not even a proportionate one).

Securitisation Trust — Sec 115TCA

  • Key rule(s):
  • Income of the Securitisation Trust from the activity of securitisation — fully exempt in the hands of the trust, Sec 10(23DA).
  • Income accruing/received by an investor from the Securitisation Trust is taxable in the investor's hands in the same manner and to the same extent as if the investor had invested directly in the underlying asset (not through the trust) — Sec 115TCA.
  • Income in the investor's hands retains the same nature and same proportion as it accrued/was received by the trust.
  • Deemed credit rule: Unpaid/uncredited income is deemed credited to the investor on the last day of the PY; once taxed on accrual, it is not taxed again when actually paid later.
  • TDS by the Securitisation Trust at the time of payment or credit, whichever is earlier — Sec 194LBC:
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — Best-recollected rates (differs from a source line suggesting a flat 10% for residents): Resident individual/HUF payee — 25%; any other resident payee — 30%; NR (not company)/Foreign Company payee — Rate in force. This should be cross-checked against the current bare-Act text of Sec 194LBC before relying on it in an exam answer, as the source material for this chapter states a flat 10% resident rate which does not match this reviewer's recollection of the statute.
  • Concept: A Securitisation Trust (SPV/trust set up by a Reconstruction Company or Securitisation Company) pools receivables (e.g., loan/debt portfolios) and issues pass-through certificates to investors; tax is deferred entirely to the investor level, computed as if the investor held the underlying asset directly.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Don't confuse this with the Business Trust/Investment Fund TDS rates (194LBA/194LBB use 10% for residents) — 194LBC has historically used the differentiated individual/HUF vs. other-person resident rates; always verify against the current Finance Act before quoting a number in the exam.
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Securitisation TrustAn SPV/trust set up by a Reconstruction Company or Securitisation Company under the SARFAESI Act, 2002, or the SEBI (Public Offer & Listing of Securitised Debt Instruments) Regulations, 2008, or RBI directions/guidelines

Common Compliance — Statement of Income Breakup

  • Key rule(s):
  • Business Trust, Investment Fund and Securitisation Trust must each furnish a statement giving the nature and proportion of income and other prescribed details:
  • To the unit holder/investor — on or before 30th June of the FY following the relevant PY.
  • To the Income-tax Authority (CIT/PCIT) — on or before 15th June of the FY following the relevant PY.
  • Concept: These statements (Forms 64A to the tax authority and 64B/64C to unit holders/investors, prescribed under the relevant Income-tax Rules) are what allow the pass-through characterisation ("same nature, same proportion") to actually be verified and matched against each unit holder's return.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Note the CIT/PCIT filing deadline (15th June) is earlier than the unit-holder statement deadline (30th June) — a commonly reversed fact in MCQs.

References

  1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 10(23FC), 10(23FCA), 10(23FBA), 10(23DA), 47(xvii), 49(2AC), 56(2)(xii), 111A, 112, 112A, 115UA, 115UB, 115TCA, 139(4E), 139(4F), 194LBA, 194LBB, 194LBC, as amended by the Finance Act 2023 (insertion of Sec 56(2)(xii), w.e.f. AY 2024-25) and Finance (No. 2) Act 2024 (capital gains rate rationalisation to 12.5%/20% and revised ₹1,25,000 LTCG threshold, effective for transfers on/after 23 July 2024).
  2. SEBI (Alternative Investment Funds) Regulations, 2012 — Category I/II/III AIF classification, and IFSC Authority Act, 2019, for IFSC-regulated investment funds.
  3. SARFAESI Act, 2002 and SEBI (Public Offer and Listing of Securitised Debt Instruments) Regulations, 2008 — governing framework for Securitisation Trusts referenced under Sec 115TCA.
  4. ICAI Study Material — Direct Tax Laws & International Taxation, Chapter on "Taxation of Business Trust, Investment Fund and Securitisation Trust," and Income-tax Rules Rule 12CA (Forms 64A/64B statement filing deadlines).

Note on this chapter's verification: Live web-search cross-checking could not be completed in this session (search budget exhausted before this chapter's queries ran); all figures above rely on the author's trained knowledge of the Income-tax Act and Finance Act amendments through early 2026, with residual uncertainty flagged inline via ⚠️ VERIFY tags (SPV shareholding threshold, MMR surcharge rate, and the Sec 194LBC resident TDS rate). Please cross-check flagged items against the current bare Act/Finance Act text before an exam.

08. Minimum Alternate Tax (MAT) & Alternate Minimum Tax (AMT)

Where it fits: MAT (Sec 115JB) is a floor tax on companies whose book profits are healthy but tax-payable-as-per-normal-provisions is low/nil due to exemptions/deductions; AMT (Sec 115JC) is the parallel floor tax on non-corporate assessees claiming specified profit-linked deductions. Both work on a "pay the higher of normal tax or X% of an adjusted base, carry forward the excess as credit" logic.

MAT — Applicability & Basic Charge (Sec 115JB)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Tax payable = max(Tax as per normal provisions of the Act, 15% × Book Profit)

  • MAT applies only to companies — domestic and foreign, government and non-government.
  • Where a unit of the assessee is located in an IFSC and derives income solely in convertible foreign exchange, MAT rate is 9% instead of 15% — Sec 115JB(7).
  • Normal tax rates for a domestic company (not opting 115BAA/115BAB): 25% (if turnover/gross receipts of the relevant previous year ≤ ₹400 crore) or 30% otherwise; surcharge 7% (net income > ₹1 crore up to ₹10 crore) / 12% (> ₹10 crore); for a foreign company surcharge is 2% / 5% for the same slabs; Health & Education Cess 4% on tax + surcharge in all cases.
  • MAT computation proforma: 15% of Book Profit → Add surcharge (domestic co. 7%/12%, foreign co. 2%/5%, based on Book Profit slabs) → Add Health & Education Cess @4% → MAT payable.
  • Concept: Book Profit (not taxable income) is the base; MAT ensures zero-tax/low-tax companies still pay a minimum tax linked to their commercial (accounting) profits.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Surcharge/cess slabs are applied on Book Profit, not on normal total income, when computing MAT liability.
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — the OCR compresses domestic/foreign surcharge into "7%/2%" and "12%/5%"; reconstructed above as domestic-co./foreign-co. pairs matching the standard company surcharge slabs — cross-check against the applicable Finance Act for the exam year before quoting in an answer.

Companies Exempt from MAT

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s) — MAT (Sec 115JB) does NOT apply to:
  • Income from life insurance business taxable u/s 115B.
  • A company that has exercised the option u/s 115BAA or 115BAB (concessional corporate tax regimes).
  • A foreign company that is a resident of a country/specified territory having a DTAA with India and does not have a Permanent Establishment (PE) in India.
  • A foreign company resident of a country with which India has no DTAA, and the company is not required to seek registration under any law relating to companies in force in India.
  • A foreign company whose total income comprises solely of profits referred to in Sec 44B, 44BB, 44BBA, 44BBB, offered to tax at those special rates.
  • Concept: These carve-outs prevent MAT from disturbing already-final special tax regimes or from reaching foreign companies with no taxable nexus in India.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Exercising 115BAA/115BAB is irrevocable and simultaneously takes the company out of MAT — flag this trade-off in "which regime to choose" case studies.
  • Foreign-company MAT exemption is fact-specific — test both the DTAA/no-DTAA limb and the PE/registration limb.

Book Profit Computation — Part 1: Additions & Deductions (Explanation to Sec 115JB)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Book Profit = Net Profit as per Sch. III of Companies Act, 2013 (P&L A/c) + Additions - Deductions

  • Additions (if debited to P&L, except items 10 & 14 which apply regardless): income-tax paid/provided (incl. interest, DDT, surcharge, cess); dividend paid/proposed; transfer to any reserve; losses of subsidiary companies; provision for unascertained/contingent liabilities; expenditure relating to income exempt u/s 10/11/12; depreciation debited (total); provision for diminution in value of assets; deferred tax; balance in revaluation reserve on retirement/disposal of an asset (if not credited to P&L); expenses relating to share of income from AOP/BOI; expenses relatable to a foreign company's capital gains on securities, or dividend/interest/royalty/FTS, where the tax rate on that income is below 15%; notional loss on exchange of SPV shares for business-trust units (or notional loss from change in carrying value/transfer of such units); actual gain on transfer of business-trust units (sale proceeds − cost of SPV shares); expenditure relatable to patent royalty taxable u/s 115BBF.
  • Deductions: amount withdrawn from a reserve (only if the reserve was originally created through the P&L route); income exempt u/s 10/11/12; deferred tax; depreciation (excluding depreciation attributable to asset revaluation); ⚠️ VERIFY — profit of a "sick industrial company" (this SICA-linked exemption predates repeal of the Sick Industrial Companies Act and may not survive on the current syllabus in this form — the operative current relief is the IBC-linked item below); transfer from revaluation reserve to the extent of depreciation on revalued assets; brought-forward business loss / unabsorbed depreciation, in full, for a company against which a CIRP application stands admitted under Sec 7/9/10 of the IBC, 2016, or whose Board has been suspended/reconstituted by the Tribunal on a Central Government application u/s 241–242 of the Companies Act, 2013 (subsidiary test: holding company holds >50% of nominal equity value); brought-forward loss and unabsorbed depreciation for other companies restricted to the lower of the two; income already taxed as share of AOP/BOI income; income to a foreign company from capital gains on securities, or interest/dividend/royalty/FTS taxed at a rate below 15%; notional gain on exchange of SPV shares for business-trust units; actual loss on transfer of business-trust units; income by way of patent royalty taxable u/s 115BBF @10%.
  • Concept: Part 1 converts the Schedule III commercial profit into a MAT-specific "Book Profit" by reversing items that are either tax-neutral, already taxed elsewhere, or policy carve-outs (IBC-stressed companies, DTAA-taxed foreign-company income, business-trust restructuring, patent royalty).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Depreciation add-back/deduction and brought-forward loss figures are always taken per the Companies Act, never per the Income-tax Act.
  • The "lower of b/f loss vs. unabsorbed depreciation" rule is company-wide; the IBC-linked full deduction is a distinct, narrower relief — do not conflate the two in an answer.
  • Provisions for gratuity/leave salary/warranty made on an actuarial/scientific basis are not add-backs (only ad-hoc/unascertained provisions are added back).

Definitions

TermMeaning
Book ProfitNet profit per Schedule III P&L, adjusted per Explanation 1 to Sec 115JB, used as the MAT base
CIRPCorporate Insolvency Resolution Process under the IBC, 2016

Book Profit Computation — Part 2: Ind-AS Adjustments (Sec 115JB(2A), (2B), (2C))

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Book Profit (Ind-AS company) = Book Profit under Part 1 + Additions - Deductions

  • Additions: items credited to Other Comprehensive Income (OCI) not reclassified to the P&L statement (subject to Note-1 carve-out below); gains from fair-value change in equity instruments through OCI and revaluation surplus on retirement/disposal/realisation/transfer of assets; amount debited to P&L on distribution of non-cash assets to shareholders in a demerger (Ind-AS 10, Appendix A); 1/5th of the transition amount (spread over 5 years from the year of convergence).
  • Deductions: the mirror-image debit-side items (OCI debits not reclassified, subject to Note-1; losses from fair-value change/revaluation surplus on retirement etc.; amount credited to P&L on non-cash asset distribution in a demerger; 1/5th of the transition amount).
  • Note 1 — permanently excluded from Book Profit (taxed only in the year of actual retirement/disposal/realisation/transfer): revaluation surplus for assets under Ind-AS 16 & 38; gain/loss on equity instruments designated at fair value through OCI under Ind-AS 109.
  • Note 2 (Sec 115JB(2B)): in a demerger, any change in the resulting company's asset/liability values (vs. the demerged company's books) is ignored for Book Profit computation.
  • Note 3 — "Transition amount": amount adjusted in Other Equity (excluding capital reserve & securities premium) on the convergence date, excluding items (A)–(F) listed in Sec 115JB Explanation (OCI items subsequently reclassified to P&L; Ind-AS 16/38 revaluation surplus; Ind-AS 109 FVTOCI gains/losses; Ind-AS 101 para D5/D7 deemed-cost adjustments for PP&E/intangibles; Ind-AS 101 para D15 deemed-cost adjustments for subsidiaries/JVs/associates; Ind-AS 101 para D13 foreign-operation translation adjustments) — these six items instead hit Book Profit only in the year the underlying asset/investment/operation is retired, disposed, realised or transferred.
  • Concept: These provisions align MAT with Ind-AS financial statements, which route many fair-value and one-time transition gains/losses through OCI or "Other Equity" rather than the P&L — MAT would otherwise miss or double-count them.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • "Convergence date" = first day of the first Ind-AS reporting period (Ind-AS 101); "year of convergence" = the previous year containing that date.
  • Remember the 1/5th spread for transition amount — a common numerical trap in problems spanning 5 years.

MAT Credit (Sec 115JAA)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

MAT Credit = (15% × Book Profit) - Tax as per normal provisions

  • MAT credit can be carried forward and set off up to 15 assessment years (extended from 10 to 15 years by the Finance Act, 2017, effective AY 2018-19 onward).
  • Credit is set off only in a year where tax under normal provisions exceeds MAT (15% of Book Profit); set-off is capped at the excess of normal tax over MAT for that year.
  • On conversion of an unlisted company into an LLP, MAT credit u/s 115JAA is not allowed to be carried to the successor LLP.
  • MAT credit is reduced by: (FTC allowed against MAT) − (FTC allowed against normal tax) — i.e., if a company gets more foreign tax credit against MAT than it would have got against normal tax, the excess FTC does not enrich the carry-forward credit.
  • Companies liable to MAT must also pay advance tax and are subject to interest u/s 234A/B/C.
  • Concept: MAT credit prevents double taxation over time — the "extra" tax paid in a MAT year is banked and can offset normal tax once profits/deductions push normal tax above MAT in a later year.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Apollo Tyres Ltd. principle: once P&L is prepared per the Companies Act (and certified/adopted at the AGM), the Assessing Officer cannot recompute book profit beyond the specific adjustments listed in Explanation 1 to Sec 115JB.
  • Track MAT credit as a running ledger across years in problems — credit generated is capped at (MAT − normal tax) in the year it arises, and utilised only up to (normal tax − MAT) in later years.

Definitions

TermMeaning
MAT CreditExcess of MAT paid over normal tax in a year, available to offset future years' normal-tax excess

Recomputation on APA / Secondary Adjustment (Amendment by FA 2021) & Rule 10RB

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Relief u/s 115JB(1) = (A - B) - (D - C)

where: A = tax payable u/s 115JB(1) on Book Profit of the relevant PY including the past income; B = tax payable u/s 115JB(1) on Book Profit of the relevant PY after excluding the past income; C = aggregate tax payable u/s 115JB(1) on Book Profit of the past year(s) to which the past income belongs; D = aggregate tax payable u/s 115JB(1) on Book Profit of the past year(s), after increasing that Book Profit by the relevant past income.

  • If the computed value of (A − B) − (D − C) is negative, it is deemed to be zero — no negative relief.
  • Where increase in current-year Book Profit is on account of income of an earlier year(s) included due to an Advance Pricing Agreement (APA) u/s 92CC or a Secondary Adjustment u/s 92CE, the Assessing Officer shall, on the assessee's application, recompute the book profit (and tax) of the past year(s).
  • Concept: Prevents the same transfer-pricing income from being taxed twice under MAT — once via the APA/secondary-adjustment inclusion in the current year and once (notionally) in the year it originally related to.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Adjustment is application-driven — the company must apply; it is not automatic.
  • The 4-year time limit for rectification u/s 154 runs from the end of the financial year in which the assessee's application is made.
  • Relief under Rule 10RB(1) also reduces the MAT credit otherwise allowable u/s 115JAA by the amount of relief granted.
  • No interest is payable on any refund arising from this provision, even for AY 2020-21 or earlier years.

Judicial Note on Book Profit — Sec 54EC Exemption

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): Not a numerical formula — a judicial-interpretation point on Explanation 1 to Sec 115JB.
  • Concept: Sec 115JB(5) makes other Act provisions applicable to MAT computation; on this basis one Madras High Court view (⚠️ VERIFY — case name/citation as Metal and Chromium Plater (P) Ltd. [2019] (Mad.) per source notes, cross-check citation before quoting) holds that LTCG exempt u/s 54EC while computing normal total income should also be excluded from Book Profit, i.e., MAT does not apply to such LTCG. A contrary Kerala High Court view in N.J. Jose & Co. (P) Ltd. holds such exempt LTCG must be included in Book Profit, so MAT does apply.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: In the exam, state both views and pick the assessee-favourable one only if the question specifies a jurisdiction aligning with the Madras HC view; otherwise present as a settled controversy.

AMT — Applicability & Basic Charge (Sec 115JC)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Tax payable = max(Income-tax payable as per normal provisions, 18.5% × Adjusted Total Income (ATI)) + Surcharge (if applicable) + 4% Cess

  • AMT applies to all assessees other than companies (individuals, HUF, firms, LLPs, AOP, BOI, artificial juridical persons) — companies are governed by MAT (Sec 115JB), not AMT.
  • AMT provisions apply only if the assessee is claiming a deduction u/s 10AA (SEZ units), 35AD (specified businesses), or under Chapter VI-A "C — Deductions in respect of certain incomes" (Sec 80-IA to 80RRB), excluding Sec 80P.
  • Exemption threshold: AMT does not apply where ATI does not exceed ₹20 lakh, but this threshold is available only to Individual/HUF/AOP/BOI/Artificial Juridical Person — not to firms/LLPs, which remain subject to AMT regardless of ATI level (once they claim a qualifying deduction).
  • Where a unit of the assessee is in an IFSC deriving income solely in convertible foreign exchange, AMT rate is 9% instead of 18.5% — Sec 115JC(4).
  • For a co-operative society, AMT rate is 15% instead of 18.5% — Sec 115JC(4) (concessional rate introduced to bring parity with the MAT rate for companies).
  • AMT (this Chapter XII-BA) does not apply to a Specified Fund referred to in Sec 10(4D).
  • AMT does not apply to an assessee opting for Sec 115BAC (individuals/HUF), 115BAD or 115BAE (co-operative societies) — and any unutilised AMT credit lapses permanently on making such an election.
  • Concept: AMT is MAT's non-corporate counterpart — it claws back tax benefit from assessees who have reduced their normal tax substantially below a floor rate by claiming specific profit-linked/investment-linked deductions.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • If the assessee has claimed none of 10AA/35AD/80-IA-to-80RRB(excl. 80P), AMT does not apply at all — check this gating condition first.
  • The ₹20 lakh threshold protects small taxpayers but never protects firms/LLPs.
  • A CA's report (certifying ATI and AMT computation) is mandatory for assessees to whom AMT applies.

Definitions

TermMeaning
ATIAdjusted Total Income — the AMT base, computed by grossing normal total income back up for specified deductions
Specified FundCategory of fund referred to in Sec 10(4D), carved out of the AMT regime

Computation of Adjusted Total Income (ATI)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

ATI = Total Income (as per normal provisions) + Deduction u/s 10AA + Deduction u/s 35AD + Deduction under Chapter VI-A (Sec 80-IA to 80RRB, excl. 80P) - Depreciation u/s 32 (as if Sec 35AD deduction had not been claimed on those assets)

  • Concept: ATI "undoes" the deductions that triggered AMT applicability, then gives back normal depreciation on the Sec 35AD assets (since accelerated 35AD write-off is being reversed), arriving at a broader income base for the 18.5% floor rate.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Do not forget the depreciation add-back step (last line) — a frequent miss in numerical problems; it is a deduction from ATI, not an addition.

AMT Credit (Sec 115JD)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

AMT Credit = AMT paid - Normal Income-tax payable (in the year AMT > Normal Tax)

  • Where AMT exceeds normal income-tax, the excess is treated as AMT credit.
  • AMT credit can be carried forward and set off up to 15 assessment years (extended from 10 to 15 years by the Finance Act, 2017).
  • Credit is set off only in a year where normal tax exceeds AMT; the set-off is restricted to the difference between normal tax and AMT for that year.
  • An assessee may claim AMT credit in a subsequent year even if AMT itself is not applicable in that later year.
  • AMT credit is reduced by: (FTC allowed against AMT) − (FTC allowed against normal tax).
  • Assessees subject to AMT must also pay advance tax and are liable to interest u/s 234A/B/C; a CA's report is required for computation of ATI and AMT.
  • Concept: Mirrors MAT credit — banks the "extra" AMT paid so it can be used once normal tax overtakes AMT in a future year, within the 15-year window.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Compute FTC against AMT and against normal tax separately; only the excess (AMT FTC − normal FTC) reduces the credit, not the full AMT FTC.
  • Remember the permanent lapse of unutilised AMT credit the moment the assessee migrates to Sec 115BAC/115BAD/115BAE.

Definitions

TermMeaning
AMT CreditExcess of AMT paid over normal tax in a year, available (within 15 AYs) against future years' normal-tax excess

References

  1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sec 115JB (MAT), Sec 115JAA (MAT credit), Sec 115JC (AMT), Sec 115JD (AMT credit), and Explanation 1/1A/2A/2B/2C thereto (companies/Ind-AS book profit adjustments).
  2. Finance Act, 2017 — extension of MAT credit and AMT credit carry-forward period from 10 to 15 assessment years, effective AY 2018-19.
  3. Taxation Laws (Amendment) Act, 2019 — MAT rate reduced to 15% of Book Profit and MAT inapplicability for companies opting Sec 115BAA/115BAB.
  4. Finance Act, 2018 — concessional AMT rate of 15% for co-operative societies u/s 115JC(4); Income-tax Rules, 1962 — Rule 10RB (relief for APA/secondary-adjustment recomputation of book profit under Sec 115JB).
  5. ICAI CA Final Direct Tax Laws & International Taxation — Study Material/RTP on Chapter: MAT & AMT (for conceptual cross-verification of Book Profit proforma and AMT computation format).

Note: Live web-source verification for this chapter could not be completed within this session (web-search quota was exhausted before chapter-specific queries ran); figures above rely on the author's trained knowledge of the Act and cited Finance Acts as of the current (2026 attempts) syllabus — items with residual uncertainty are flagged ⚠️ VERIFY inline and should be cross-checked against the Finance Act applicable for the relevant assessment year before an exam.

09. Deductions: Sec 10AA (SEZ) & Chapter VI-A

Where it fits: After computing income under all five heads and clubbing/set-off, Sec 10AA (an exemption administered like a deduction) is claimed from the eligible SEZ unit's profits, and Chapter VI-A deductions are claimed from Gross Total Income (GTI) to arrive at Total Income — the last stop before applying tax rates.

Sec 10AA — SEZ Unit: Eligibility & Deduction Slabs

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Available to an undertaking that begins to manufacture/produce articles or things, or provide services, in any SEZ.
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — Deduction is available only where the SEZ unit received necessary approval up to 31.03.2020 and began manufacture/production/services up to 31.03.2021 (the 31.3.2021 sunset reflects the one-year COVID extension under the Taxation and Other Laws (Relaxation of Certain Provisions) Act, 2020; confirm the exact wording against the current Finance Act text before quoting in an answer).
PeriodDeduction
First 5 AYs100% of Export Profit
Next 5 AYs50% of Export Profit
Next 5 AYs (last block)Lower of: (a) amount debited to P&L A/c and credited to SEZ Re-investment Allowance Reserve A/c, or (b) 50% of Export Profit
  • Concept: A 15-year tax holiday for eligible SEZ units, tapering from 100% → 50% → conditional 50% (linked to reinvestment), unlike the flat-rate 80-IA/80-IB series.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Deduction u/s 10AA is claimed after claiming all Chapter VI-A deductions from GTI (order matters — it does not reduce GTI available for VI-A).
  • Available only if the assessee files the Return of Income by the due date u/s 139(1); a CA's audit report (Form 56F) must be filed by the due date u/s 44AB-linked date.
  • Not available if formed by splitting up/reconstruction of an existing business — except the specific software-industry technical-manpower carve-out (below).

Sec 10AA — Export Profit Formula & Turnover Definitions

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Export Profit = PGBP of the SEZ unit × Export TurnoverTotal Turnover of the undertaking

  • Export Turnover = consideration for export brought into India in convertible foreign exchange within 6 months from the end of the P.Y. (or such further time as the RBI permits). Sale proceeds are deemed received in India if credited to a separate RBI-approved account maintained outside India.
  • Export T/O excludes: freight, telecommunication charges, insurance, and expenses for providing services outside India; and excludes cash compensatory support (CCS), duty drawback (DB) and profit on sale of import entitlement licences.
  • Total T/O also excludes the same items (freight/telecom/insurance/expenses abroad, CCS, DB, import-entitlement profit), but includes export T/O even where not received in convertible foreign exchange, plus domestic T/O.
  • Concept: The export-turnover-to-total-turnover ratio isolates the export-derived slice of the unit's PGBP profit for the tax holiday.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • HCL Technologies Ltd (2018) (SC): expenditure in foreign exchange excluded from export turnover must also be excluded from total turnover — numerator and denominator must be computed on a parity basis.
  • CCS, duty drawback and profit on sale of import entitlement licences are taxable as PGBP but are not "derived from" the business, so they don't enter the 10AA computation at all.
  • Cognizant Technology Solutions of India (P) Ltd [2023] (SC): forex gain solely relatable to the export business (arising from rupee value fluctuation on export realisation) is eligible for 10AA deduction.

Sec 10AA — SEZ Reinvestment Reserve & Deemed Income

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Amount credited to the SEZ Re-investment Allowance Reserve must be utilised to acquire new plant & machinery (P&M) and put to use within 3 years from the end of the P.Y. in which the reserve was created.
  • If misutilised or unutilised, the deduction earlier claimed becomes taxable as PGBP (deemed income) as follows:
SituationYear of taxability
Reserve utilised for a non-specified purposeYear in which wrongly utilised
Reserve not utilised within the 3-year windowYear immediately following expiry of the 3-year period
  • Concept: The last 5-year 50% slab is conditional — it is only a real benefit if the reserve is genuinely deployed into new P&M; failure claws the deduction back.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Track the reserve's utilisation timeline year-by-year in problems — a common trap is to forget the "immediately following" year rule for unutilised reserves.

Sec 10AA — New P&M, Splitting-Up Exception & CBDT Circular 1/2013

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • P&M used in the SEZ undertaking must be new, except: (a) up to 20% of total value of P&M can be second-hand; (b) P&M imported into India for the first time is treated as new even if used abroad earlier.
  • Software-industry exception to the "splitting up/reconstruction" bar: deployment of technical manpower from an existing unit to the new SEZ unit is not treated as splitting up, provided either — technical manpower transferred is up to 50% of total technical manpower in the SEZ unit in its first year, or net addition of technical manpower is at least 50% of the SEZ unit's manpower in that P.Y.
  • CBDT Circular No. 1/2013 dated 17.01.2013 clarifies:
  • Software developed abroad at a client's premises, under a contract with the SEZ unit, is eligible for 10AA.
  • Profits from deployment of technical manpower at a client's site abroad specifically for software development are eligible, under a contract between the parties.
  • On change in ownership, deduction continues for the unexpired period at applicable rates, subject to conditions.
  • Physical relocation of an eligible SEZ unit to another SEZ does not by itself deny the tax holiday.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: In case studies on outsourced/onsite software development, always check the circular's twin conditions (contract-based, specifically for software development) before denying 10AA.

Chapter VI-A — Governing Principles

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Aggregate deduction under Chapter VI-A cannot exceed the Gross Total Income; excess cannot be carried forward.
  • No deduction under Chapter VI-A against LTCG (Sec 112), LTCG u/s 112A, STCG u/s 111A, or any income taxed at a special rate.
  • Where deduction is claimed and allowed u/s 10AA or 35AD, no deduction is allowable under Chapter VI-A "Part-C" (income-based deductions) for the same profits, in any AY.
  • Deduction u/s 10AA and Chapter VI-A "Part-C" is available only if claimed in the return and the return is filed by the due date u/s 139(1).
  • If an AO's assessment adds back disallowances (Secs 40(a), 40A(3), 43B, etc.) relating to the eligible business, the addition increases "eligible profits" and the assessee gets a corresponding higher Part-C deduction.
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Chapter VI-A "Part-B"Payment-linked deductions (80C, 80CCC, 80CCD, 80D, 80DD, 80DDB, 80E, 80EE/EEA/EEB, 80G, 80GG, 80GGA, 80GGB/C, 80U)
Chapter VI-A "Part-C"Income/profit-linked deductions, Secs 80-IA to 80RRB (includes 80JJAA, treated as income-based for AMT purposes even though computed on expenditure)
Chapter VI-A "Part-CA"Sec 80TTA / 80TTB (interest income deductions)
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Reliance Energy Ltd (2022) (SC): a profit-linked VI-A deduction (e.g., 80-IA) is not restricted to the income under the head PGBP — it is restricted only to Gross Total Income per Sec 80A(2). Losses of a non-eligible unit reduce PGBP but the eligible-unit deduction can still be claimed up to GTI.

80C, 80CCC, 80CCD — Investment & Pension Deductions

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Sec 80C: Individual & HUF; max ₹1,50,000. Covers LIP, PPF, employee's contribution to SPF/RPF/ASF, NSC (+accrued interest), housing loan principal repayment, 5-year+ bank/post-office FD, tuition fees (max 2 children, full-time education in India), NABARD bonds, Senior Citizen Savings Scheme, ULIP, notified MF/UTI units, Sukanya Samriddhi deposit, stamp duty/registration fee on house purchase, NPS Tier-II (3-year lock-in, CG employee), National Housing Bank Term Deposit Scheme 2008.

LIP deduction (per policy) = min(Premium paid, % of Sum Assured)

Policy issuedCap on Sum Assured
Before 1.4.201220%
On/after 1.4.201210%
On/after 1.4.2013, for a person with disability (80U) or specified disease (80DDB)15%
  • Sec 80CCC: Individual; contribution to LIC/other insurer pension fund; max ₹1,50,000.
  • Sec 80CCD(1): Individual's own contribution to NPS/CG pension scheme.
  • Sec 80CCD(1B): Additional deduction up to ₹50,000, over and above 80CCD(1); also covers a parent/guardian's contribution to a minor's account under NPS Vatsalya, capped at ₹50,000.
  • Sec 80CCD(2): Employer's contribution to NPS (first taxed as salary in the employee's hands, then deduction allowed) —

Deduction = min(Employer's contribution, 10% (or 14%) × Salary)

  • 14% applies where the employer is Central/State Government, or (w.e.f. AY 2025-26, Finance Act 2024) where the assessee follows the default tax regime u/s 115BAC even for a non-government employer; otherwise 10%.
  • Sec 80CCE: Aggregate deduction under 80C + 80CCC + 80CCD(1) capped at ₹1,50,000 (80CCD(1B) and 80CCD(2) are outside this cap).
  • Sec 80CCH: (Finance Act 2023, w.e.f. AY 2024-25) Individual enrolled in the Agnipath Scheme on/after 1.11.2022 — 80CCH(1): 100% of own contribution to Agniveer Corpus Fund; 80CCH(2): 100% of CG's matching contribution (first taxed as salary, then deducted). Scheme mandates 30% of monthly package as the assessee's contribution, matched by CG.
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Salary (for 80CCD)Basic Salary + Dearness Allowance (if it forms part of retirement benefits)
Sec 10(12A)On closure of NPS account, 60% of amount payable is exempt (40% taxable); on death, payment to nominee/legal heir is fully exempt
Sec 10(12B)Partial withdrawal from NPS by an employee: exempt up to 25% of own contribution (non-salaried: fully taxable)
Sec 10(12BA)Partial withdrawal from NPS Vatsalya by parent/guardian: exempt up to 25% of contributions made; on minor's death, fully exempt
Sec 10(12C)Any amount received from Agnipath Fund by the assessee or nominee is fully exempt
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Classic exam trap: given a lump-sum NPS contribution exceeding the 20%-of-GTI cap under 80CCD(1), first fill the ₹50,000 80CCD(1B) bucket, then the balance under 80CCD(1) subject to the 20%-of-GTI ceiling — either sequencing is acceptable, illustrate with the assessee's actual numbers.
  • RPF/Superannuation Fund corpus can be transferred to NPS without tax implication.

80D, 80DD, 80DDB, 80U — Health & Disability Deductions

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Sec 80D (Individual/HUF; mode of payment: any mode other than cash, except preventive health check-up which may be paid in cash):

Deduction = underbracemin(Premium+CGHS+Check-up, 25,000 or 50,000 if senior citizen)Self/family (Indiv.) or any member (HUF) + underbracemin(Premium/Check-up for parents, 25,000 or 50,000 if senior)Parents (Individual only)

  • Additional (in lieu of premium): medical expenditure incurred on a senior citizen for whom no mediclaim premium is paid — max ₹50,000.
  • Preventive health check-up: aggregate for self, spouse, dependent children & parents capped at ₹5,000 (within the overall 25,000/50,000 ceiling, not additional to it).
  • Lump-sum multi-year premium: deduction per year = Lump-sum premium ÷ number of P.Y.s the policy is in force.
  • Sec 80DD (Resident Individual/HUF — expenditure on medical treatment/maintenance, or deposit for maintenance, of a dependant with disability):
DisabilityDeduction
Normal disability₹75,000
Severe disability (80% or more)₹1,25,000
  • Deduction is withdrawn (taxable as income of the previous owner) if the dependant receives an annuity/lump sum before the assessee's death or before the assessee attains 60 years.
  • Sec 80DDB (Resident Individual/HUF — treatment of specified diseases for self/dependant, or any HUF member):

Deduction = min(Actual expenditure, ₹40,000 or ₹1,00,000 if senior citizen patient) - Insurance/reimbursement received

  • Sec 80U (Resident Individual, self-disability): same slabs as 80DD — ₹75,000 (normal) / ₹1,25,000 (severe, 80%+).
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Relative (80DD/80DDB, Individual)Spouse, brother, sister, children, mother, father
Senior citizenResident individual aged 60 years or more at any time during the P.Y.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: 80DD and 80U are flat deductions regardless of actual expenditure once the disability threshold is met — don't confuse with 80DDB's "lower of actual expense or cap" mechanic.

80E, 80EE, 80EEA, 80EEB — Interest Deductions

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Sec 80E: Individual; interest on loan for higher education (any course after Class XII) of self, spouse, children, or a student for whom the assessee is legal guardian; no monetary ceiling, deduction for interest paid for 8 consecutive years starting from the year repayment of interest begins.
  • Sec 80EE: Individual; max ₹50,000; loan from bank/financial institution for acquiring a residential house; conditions — house value ≤ ₹50 lakh, loan sanctioned between 1.4.2016 and 31.3.2017, loan amount ≤ ₹35 lakh, assessee owns no other residential house on the date of sanction.
  • Sec 80EEA: Individual not covered u/s 80EE; max ₹1,50,000; Stamp Duty Value of house ≤ ₹45 lakh; loan sanctioned between 1.4.2019 and 31.3.2022; assessee owns no other residential house on date of sanction; no double deduction for the same interest under any other provision.
  • Sec 80EEB: Individual; interest on loan for an Electric Vehicle; max ₹1,50,000; loan from bank/financial institution (including NBFC) sanctioned between 1.4.2019 and 31.3.2023; no double deduction under any other provision.
  • Concept: These interest deductions are sequential policy incentives (housing 80EE → 80EEA → EV 80EEB) each tied to a specific sanction window — the loan-sanction date, not the year of claim, gates eligibility.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Always check the loan sanction date against the section's window first — a loan sanctioned outside the window gets no deduction under that section even if interest is paid later.

80G, 80GGA, 80GGB, 80GGC, 80GG — Donations & Rent

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Sec 80G — Part A (no qualifying limit): National Defence Fund, PM National Relief Fund, PM Armenia Earthquake Relief Fund, CM/Lieutenant Governor Relief Fund, Zilla Saksharta Samiti, National Sports Development Fund, National Children's Fund, National Cultural Fund, Swachh Bharat Kosh, Clean Ganga Fund, National Fund for Control of Drug Abuse, PM Citizen Assistance & Relief in Emergency Situations Fund (PM CARES), Fund for Army/Navy/Air Force welfare — 100% deductible; PM's Drought Relief Fund — 50% deductible (also unlimited/no qualifying-limit category).
  • Part B (subject to 10% of ATI qualifying limit): donations for family planning (Govt./local authority/approved institution), to Indian Olympic Association/sports infrastructure bodies (by companies), housing development authorities, renovation/repair of temple/gurudwara/mosque/church, public charitable trusts, promotion of minority community welfare — 100% or 50% deductible per the specific clause, subject to the qualifying limit:

Eligible Donation (limited category) = min(Actual donation to limited-category funds, 10% × Adjusted Total Income (ATI))

ATI = GTI (excluding income taxed at special rates) - All Chapter VI-A deductions except 80G

  • No deduction if cash donation exceeds ₹2,000; donations in kind are not eligible.
  • Donee trust/institution must be registered u/s 80G(5); must file Form 10BD (statement of donations) with the Pr.DGIT(Systems), and issue Form 10BE (certificate to donor) — both by 31st May of the following FY.
  • Donations routed to PM/CM/LG relief funds through the employer are eligible even if the certificate is issued in the employer's name.
  • Sec 80GG: Individual, rent paid, no HRA received —

Deduction = min(₹5,000 p.m., 25% of Adjusted GTI, Rent Paid - 10% of Adjusted GTI)

  • Adjusted GTI = GTI − all Chapter VI-A deductions (except 80GG itself); condition — assessee/spouse/minor child/HUF (of which assessee is a member) owns no house at the place of duty/employment/business.
  • Sec 80GGA: All assessees except those having PGBP income; donation for scientific research or rural development; 100% of donation; must be non-cash if amount exceeds ₹2,000.
  • Sec 80GGB / 80GGC: Donation to a political party or Electoral Trust — 80GGB (Indian company), 80GGC (any other person, except local authority/artificial juridical person wholly/partly funded by Government); 100% of donation; no deduction if paid in cash.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Compute ATI carefully for 80G's limited category — a very common numerical trap is forgetting to exclude LTCG/STCG-111A/112A income from GTI before applying the 10% cap.

80JJAA, 80JJA — Employment & Bio-Waste Deductions

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Sec 80JJAA: Any assessee with PGBP income to whom tax audit u/s 44AB applies —

Deduction = 30% × Additional Employee Cost, claimable for 3 consecutive AYs

  • Additional employee cost = total emoluments paid/payable to additional employees employed during the P.Y.; Nil for an existing business if there is no net increase in total employee headcount, or emoluments are paid otherwise than by account-payee cheque/DD/ECS.
  • Additional employees exclude: those with monthly emoluments > ₹25,000; those employed for less than 240 days in the P.Y. (150 days for apparel/footwear/leather manufacturing); those not participating in RPF; those for whom the entire employer's PF contribution is paid by Government under the notified Employees' Pension Scheme.
  • If an employee works less than 240/150 days in one P.Y. but crosses that threshold in the immediately following P.Y., they are deemed employed in that following year — 30% deduction available then.
  • Sec 80JJA: Any assessee; business of collecting/processing/treating bio-degradable waste (for generating power, bio-fertilizers/bio-pesticides, bio-gas, or pellets/briquettes/organic manure) — 100% of profits, for 5 consecutive P.Y.s from the year business commences.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: 80JJAA is nominally an "expenditure-linked" computation but is statutorily grouped under VI-A "Part-C" (income-based), so AMT (Sec 115JC, for non-corporate assessees) applies if this deduction is claimed.

80LA — Offshore Banking Units / IFSC Units

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Eligible: (i) a Scheduled Bank or foreign bank having an Offshore Banking Unit (OBU) in a SEZ; (ii) a Unit of an International Financial Services Centre (IFSC).
EntityDeduction
Bank branch (OBU) in SEZ100% of income for first 5 AYs, then 50% for next 5 AYs ⚠️ VERIFY — note claims this was enhanced to 100% for the next 5 AYs from AY 2023-24; confirm against the current Finance Act text before relying on this in an exam answer
Unit of IFSC100% of income for any 10 consecutive AYs out of 15 AYs, at the assessee's option
  • Deduction is available from the P.Y. in which permission under the Banking Regulation Act, SEBI Act, or IFSC Authority Act is received.
  • Eligible income includes income from the OBU/IFSC unit, transfer of an aircraft/ship leased by an IFSC unit that commenced operations up to 31.03.2030, and banking business with SEZ undertakings/SEZ developers.
  • Additional conditions: CA's certificate in Form 10CCF filed with the return; copy of the regulatory permission also filed with the return.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Distinguish the two structures — OBU gets a tapering 100%→50%(/100%) slab over 10 years, while an IFSC unit gets a flat 100% but only for 10 out of a 15-year window, chosen by the assessee.

80-IAC (Start-ups) & 80-IBA (Affordable Housing)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Sec 80-IAC: Company or LLP that is an "eligible start-up" (engaged in innovation/development/improvement of products, processes or services, or a scalable business model with high potential for employment/wealth creation); incorporated between 1.4.2016 and 31.3.2030; turnover ≤ ₹100 crore in the year of claim; holds a certificate from the Inter-Ministerial Board of Certification —

Deduction = 100% of profits, for any 3 consecutive AYs out of the first 10 AYs from incorporation

  • P&M must be new (same 20%-second-hand / imported-second-hand-treated-as-new exceptions as 10AA); accounts must be audited by a CA; must not be formed by splitting up/reconstruction.
  • Sec 80-IBA: All assessees; developing/building affordable housing (or rental housing) projects; 100% of profits.
  • Conditions: project approved by the competent authority between 1.6.2016 and 31.3.2022; completed within 5 years from approval; commercial area (shops etc.) ≤ 3% of aggregate carpet area; separate books of account maintained; not executed as a mere works contract; if not completed in time, deduction earlier claimed is deemed income of the year the time limit expires.
ConditionMetros (Chennai/Delhi/Kolkata/Mumbai)Other places
Min. plot size1,000 sq. mtr.2,000 sq. mtr.
Max. carpet area/unit30 sq. mtr.60 sq. mtr.
Min. floor area ratio utilised90%80%
  • Additional conditions for projects approved on/after 01.09.2019: Stamp Duty Value of a residential unit ≤ ₹45 lakh; revised size norms —
ConditionBengaluru/Chennai/Delhi-NCR (Noida, Ghaziabad, Gurugram, Faridabad)/Hyderabad/Kolkata/Mumbai (MMR)Other places
Min. plot size1,000 sq. mtr.2,000 sq. mtr.
Max. carpet area/unit60 sq. mtr.90 sq. mtr.
Min. floor area ratio utilised90%80%
  • Where a unit is allotted to an individual, no further unit may be allotted to that individual/spouse/minor children.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: For 80-IAC, the "3 out of 10" flexibility mirrors 10AA-style planning questions — always confirm incorporation-date and turnover eligibility first before computing the 3-year window.

80-IA to 80-IE — Legacy Profit-Linked Infrastructure/Industrial Deductions

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): (all historical sunset-dated incentives, largely relevant for case-law/theory questions on ongoing eligible periods)
SectionEligible businessCommencement windowPeriod of deduction%
80-IADevelop/operate/maintain infrastructure facility1.4.1995 – 1.4.201710 consecutive AYs out of first 20 AYs (road/bridge/rail/highway/water supply) or first 15 AYs (others)100%
80-IAIndustrial Park1.4.1997 – 31.3.2011as above100%
80-IAPower generation/transmission/distribution, or renovation & modernisation of existing network1.4.1993 – 31.3.2017as above100%
