80-IBProcessing/preserving/packing of fruits, vegetables, meat, poultry, marine, dairy; handling/storage/transport of food grainsMeat/poultry/marine/dairy: on/after 1.4.2009; Others: on/after 1.4.200110 consecutive AYs100% (first 5 AYs), 25% balance (30% for a company)
80-ICManufacturing undertaking in Himachal Pradesh & Uttaranchal1.4.2003 – 31.3.201210 consecutive AYs100% (first 5 AYs), 25% balance (30% for a company)

  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Container Corporation of India Ltd [2018] (SC): an Inland Container Depot is an "inland port" and thus an infrastructure facility eligible u/s 80-IA(4). Chetak Enterprises Pvt. Ltd [2020] (SC): deduction survives conversion of a firm into a company where the company legally succeeds to the firm's infrastructure agreement. Praveen Soni (2011) (Delhi): the deduction period need not start from the first eligible year — an assessee can begin claiming in a later year and still get the remaining years within the eligible block. Swarnagiri Wire Insulations Pvt. Ltd (2012) (Kar.): losses of an eligible unit may be set off against profits of a non-eligible unit, but once set off, deduction to that extent is barred in later years. Nestor Pharmaceuticals / Sidwal Refrigerations (2010) (Delhi): the 5/10-year period runs from the F.Y. of commercial production, not mere trial production.

80P, 80QQB, 80RRB, 80TTA, 80TTB — Co-op Societies, Royalty & Interest

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Sec 80P (Co-operative societies): 100% deduction on profits from specified activities — credit facilities to members (except co-op banks), cottage industry, marketing of members' agricultural produce, collective disposal of members' labour, fishing & allied activities, processing (without aid of power) of members' agricultural produce, purchase of agricultural implements/seeds/livestock for supply to members, interest/dividend from investment in other co-op societies, income from letting godowns/warehouses, and supply of milk/oilseeds/fruits/vegetables by a primary society to a federal co-op society/Government/Government company.
  • General deduction for other activities: consumers' co-op society — max ₹1,00,000; any other case — max ₹50,000.
  • Interest on securities / house property income of a co-op society is fully deductible if GTI ≤ ₹20,000 and it is not a housing society, urban consumers' society, transport-business society, or a society doing manufacturing with the aid of power.
  • Sec 80QQB (Resident Individual — royalty on books of literary/artistic/scientific nature):

Deduction = min(Eligible royalty received, ₹3,00,000)

  • Eligible royalty: lump-sum royalty — full amount received; otherwise — max 15% of the value of books sold.
  • Sec 80RRB (Resident Individual — royalty on patents):

Deduction = min(Royalty received, ₹3,00,000)

  • For both 80QQB and 80RRB, royalty earned outside India is deductible only if brought into India in convertible foreign exchange within 6 months from the end of the P.Y. (or such extended time as the RBI allows).
  • Sec 80TTA (Individual & HUF — savings account interest, bank/co-op bank/post office):

Deduction = min(Interest amount, ₹10,000)

  • Not available to a resident senior citizen eligible for 80TTB.
  • Sec 80TTB (Resident Senior Citizen — interest on deposits, bank/co-op bank/post office):

Deduction = min(Interest amount, ₹50,000)

  • Where the deposit is held by/on behalf of a firm/AOP/BOI, the partner/member gets no separate 80TTA/80TTB deduction on that interest.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Annasaheb Patil Mathadi Kamgar Sahakari Pathpedi Ltd [2023] (SC): a co-op society providing credit facilities solely to members is eligible u/s 80P and is not treated as a co-operative bank (which would otherwise be excluded).

10. Clubbing of Income & Set-off/Carry Forward of Losses

Where it fits: These are two independent "computation-protection" chapters clubbed together in the syllabus — Clubbing (Sec 60–65) stops income-splitting within the family/related parties, while Set-off & Carry Forward (Sec 70–80) governs how losses of the current year, or brought forward from earlier years, can be adjusted against income — both are applied after computing income under each head and before arriving at Gross Total Income.

A. Clubbing of Income — Income Transfer & Revocable Transfer (Sec 60, 61)

  • Key rule(s):
  • Sec 60 — Transfer of income without transfer of asset: if only the income is transferred (asset retained by transferor), such income is taxable in the hands of the transferor, irrespective of whether the transfer is revocable or irrevocable.
  • Sec 61 — Revocable transfer of asset: where the asset itself is transferred but the transfer is revocable, income from the asset is taxable in the hands of the transferor, even though received by the transferee.
  • Exception: not applicable if the transfer is revoked only after the death of the transferee/beneficiary, or takes effect only during the lifetime of the beneficiary and is not revocable during their lifetime.
  • Concept: These are the foundation/anti-abuse provisions — even without any family relationship, splitting income from an asset you still control does not shift the tax liability.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Sec 60 applies regardless of the existence of any relationship between transferor and transferee.
  • Distinguish "transfer of income" (Sec 60 — always clubbed) from "transfer of asset" (clubbed only if revocable, or if within Sec 64 relationships).

B. Income of Minor Child (Sec 64(1A))

  • Key rule(s):
  • Income of a minor child is clubbed with the income of the parent whose total income (before including the minor's income) is higher.
  • Exceptions — taxable in the minor's own hands:
  • Income earned by the minor's manual work.
  • Income earned by application of the minor's own skill, talent, or specialized knowledge.
  • Income of a minor child suffering from a disability specified under Sec 80U (or Sec 80U-referenced disability).
  • Exemption on clubbing: where a minor's income is clubbed with a parent, an exemption under Sec 10(32) of ₹1,500 per child per annum (or the actual income clubbed, if lower) is available to that parent.
  • Concept: Prevents parents from diverting income-generating assets to a minor child to reduce the family's overall tax; the child's own-effort income is carved out and left taxable in the child's hands.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Once clubbed with one parent, it continues with that parent in later years too — AO can shift it to the other parent only after giving that parent an opportunity of being heard.
  • Where parents' marriage does not subsist, income is clubbed with the parent who maintains the minor child in the relevant PY.
  • Clubbing applies even to income of a minor married daughter.
  • "Child" includes a step-child and an adopted child.
  • Sec 10(32) exemption is ₹1,500 per child, capped at the amount actually clubbed — do not apply it if the minor's income is not clubbed (e.g., falls under an exception).
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Minor childA child (including step-child/adopted child) who has not completed 18 years of age
Sec 10(32)Exemption of up to ₹1,500 per minor child per year against income clubbed under Sec 64(1A)

C. Asset Transferred to Spouse (Sec 64(1)(iv))

  • Key rule(s):
  • Where an individual transfers an asset to their spouse without consideration, or for inadequate consideration, income arising from that asset is clubbed in the hands of the transferor.
  • Conditions: the relationship of husband-wife must exist both at the time of transfer and at the time the income arises.
  • Not applicable if the transfer is under an agreement to live apart.
  • If a house property is transferred to spouse (or a minor child, not being a married minor daughter) without/for inadequate consideration, the transferor is a deemed owner under Sec 27, and in that case Sec 64 does not apply separately (to avoid double clubbing of the same HP income).
  • Concept: Blocks the common practice of gifting income-yielding assets to a spouse to reduce the transferor's tax slab exposure.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • "Adequate consideration" is a fact-based test; natural love and affection is a good consideration in law but not an adequate consideration for this section.
  • If the relationship breaks (divorce) before income arises, Sec 64(1)(iv) does not apply.
  • For HP specifically — apply Sec 27 (deemed owner), not Sec 64, to avoid double counting.

D. Asset Transferred to Son's Wife / to a Third Person for Their Benefit (Sec 64(1)(vi), (vii), (viii))

  • Key rule(s):
  • Sec 64(1)(vi): asset transferred to son's wife without/for inadequate consideration → income clubbed in the hands of the transferor (father/mother-in-law). Condition: relationship of father/mother-in-law and daughter-in-law must exist at both the time of transfer and the time income arises.
  • Sec 64(1)(vii)/(viii): asset transferred to any person without/for inadequate consideration, for the benefit of the spouse or son's wife → income clubbed in the transferor's hands (an indirect-transfer anti-avoidance rule).
  • Concept: Extends the spouse-clubbing logic to the daughter-in-law and to indirect transfers routed through a third party for the benefit of a covered relative.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Relationship-timing condition (both at transfer and at income-accrual) is examiner-favourite for tricky MCQs.
  • Note there is no clubbing provision for assets transferred directly to a son or to a major married daughter (outside these specific clauses).

E. Spouse's Remuneration from a Concern with Substantial Interest (Sec 64(1)(ii))

  • Key rule(s): Income of the spouse is clubbed in the hands of the assessee if both conditions are satisfied:
  1. Income is in the nature of salary, commission, fees, or bonus (remuneration), and
  2. Remuneration is received from a concern in which the assessee has a substantial interest.
  • Exception: not clubbed if the remuneration is attributable to the spouse's technical or professional qualification and experience.
  • Both spouses have substantial interest & both draw remuneration: clubbed with the spouse whose total income (excluding such remuneration) is higher. Once clubbed with one spouse, continues with that spouse in future years unless AO — after hearing that spouse — decides otherwise.
  • Concept: Stops routing a spouse's "no-work" salary through a family-controlled company/firm/AOP to shift income to the lower-taxed spouse.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Test for the "qualified spouse" exception is genuine possession and application of a technical/professional qualification — not merely holding a degree.
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Substantial interest (company)Assessee beneficially holds equity shares carrying ≥ 20% of voting power (alone or with relatives), at any time during the PY
Substantial interest (non-company concern, e.g. firm)Assessee is entitled to ≥ 20% of the profits of the concern (alone or with relatives), at any time during the PY

F. Transfer of Asset to HUF (Sec 64(2)) & Cross-cutting Clubbing Notes

  • Key rule(s):
  • If an individual (being a member) transfers an asset to their HUF without/for inadequate consideration, income from that asset is clubbed in the hands of the transferor-member.
  • On partition of the HUF, income from such converted/allotted asset that is received by the transferor's spouse continues to be clubbed in the hands of the transferor.
  • Business-investment clubbing formula — where a spouse/son's wife invests a gifted amount in a business, the proportionate profit clubbed is:

Income clubbed = Profit of the business × Amount gifted by the transferor and included in capitalCapital of the business on the first day of the P.Y. (opening capital)

  • Concept: These are the general/residuary anti-avoidance notes that apply across all the Sec 64 clubbing clauses above.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Income includes loss — if the clubbable "income" is actually a loss, the loss is clubbed too (not ignored).
  • If the transferred asset is converted into another form, income from the converted asset is still clubbed.
  • Natural love and affection ≠ adequate consideration.
  • If the transferee sells the transferred asset, the resulting capital gain is also income liable to be clubbed.
  • Cross gifts / interconnected transactions: where two transfers are interlinked (a device to defeat clubbing — e.g., X gifts to his brother's wife and the brother simultaneously gifts a matching sum to X's wife), the transactions are treated as a single scheme and clubbing applies — but only to the extent of income on the matching (lower) amount of the cross gifts.
  • The business-investment clubbing formula applies only if the gifted money is actually included in the opening capital of the business.
  • Second-generation income (income earned on income — i.e., income from accretion of the already-clubbed/transferred asset) is not clubbed under any of the Sec 64 clauses; it is taxed in the hands of the transferee.

G. Set-off of Losses — Intra-head (Sec 70) & Inter-head (Sec 71)

  • Key rule(s):
  • Sec 70 — Intra-head set-off: loss from one source can be set off against income from another source under the same head, subject to exceptions below.
  • Sec 71 — Inter-head set-off: loss remaining under one head (after Sec 70) can be set off against income of another head, in the same previous year only (no inter-head adjustment is allowed for losses carried forward to later years).
  • Common exceptions to both Sec 70 and Sec 71:
  • Speculative business loss → set off only against speculative business income.
  • Specified business loss (Sec 35AD) → set off only against specified business income.
  • Long-term capital loss (LTCL) → set off only against long-term capital gains (LTCG).
  • Loss from owning & maintaining race horses → set off only against income from owning & maintaining race horses.
  • Additional Sec 71-only restrictions:
  • Short-term capital loss (STCL) → can be set off against STCG and LTCG (broader than LTCL).
  • Loss from business/profession cannot be set off against salary income (Sec 71(2A)).
  • House Property loss inter-head cap: loss from house property set off against any other head of income is restricted to a maximum of ₹2,00,000 in a year; the balance is carried forward.
  • Concept: Sec 70 first nets losses within a head; Sec 71 then allows the residual loss (subject to exceptions) to be absorbed against other heads — but only in the same year.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Once a loss is carried forward to a later AY, it can be set off only within the same head in that later year (Sec 71's cross-head relief is a current-year-only benefit).
  • Watch for: HP loss vs other-head income → ₹2,00,000 ceiling is an inter-head cap, not an intra-head one (within HP itself, the entire HP loss nets off without ceiling).

H. Head-wise Set-off & Carry Forward Summary

  • Key rule(s) — Order and time-limits by head:
Head / Loss typeStep 1 (current year)Step 2Carry forward period
SalaryLoss not possible––
House PropertyIntra-head, then inter-head (max ₹2,00,000)–8 AYs (Sec 71B)
Speculative businessSet off only vs speculative business income–4 AYs (Sec 73)
Specified business (35AD)Set off only vs specified business income–Unlimited (Sec 73A)
Any other business lossIntra-head, then inter-head (except salary)–8 AYs (Sec 72)
STCLSet off vs STCG or LTCG–8 AYs (Sec 74)
LTCLSet off vs LTCG only–8 AYs (Sec 74)
Race-horse owning/maintaining lossSet off only vs race-horse income–4 AYs (Sec 74A)
Other IFOS lossesIntra-head, then inter-headCarry forward not allowed–
Unabsorbed depreciationSet off vs any head except salary–Unlimited (Sec 32(2))
  • Consolidated carry-forward table:
SectionLoss carried forwardSet off against (in future AY)Time limitReturn filed on time required?
71BLoss from house propertyIncome from house property8 yearsNo
72Normal business lossAny business income8 yearsYes
73Speculative business lossSpeculative business income4 yearsYes
73ASpecified business loss (35AD)Specified business incomeUnlimitedYes
74Short-term capital lossSTCG & LTCG8 yearsYes
74Long-term capital lossLTCG only8 yearsYes
74ALoss from owning & maintaining race horsesRace-horse income4 yearsYes
32(2)Unabsorbed depreciationAny head of income except salaryUnlimitedNo
  • Concept: This table is the single most exam-critical reference in the chapter — memorize the section, the permissible set-off income, the time limit, and whether timely ROI filing is a precondition.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Losses under Sec 71B, 72, 73, 73A, 74, 74A generally require the original return to be filed within the due date u/s 139(1) to be eligible for carry forward (Sec 80) — except house property loss (71B) and unabsorbed depreciation (32(2)), which can be carried forward even if the return is filed late.
  • Losses under IFOS (other than race-horse loss) cannot be carried forward at all — use it in the current year or lose it.
  • Order of set-off in a year (CBDT-clarified sequence): (1) current year depreciation, (2) brought-forward business loss, (3) unabsorbed depreciation.
  • Where there is current-year income under a head and an eligible brought-forward loss under another head, the current year's loss/deduction is set off first, before absorbing brought-forward losses (CBDT circular position — maximizes the brought-forward loss preserved).
  • Brought-forward business loss can be set off even if that business is discontinued in the year of set-off.
  • No set-off/carry-forward for losses from lottery, card games, races, gambling, betting etc.; and such losses cannot be adjusted against Sec 115BB income (winnings from lotteries, crossword puzzles, card games, races, TV game shows, etc.).
  • Sec 115BBE: no set-off of any loss is allowed against unexplained income/investment/money/expenditure taxed under Sec 68 to 69D.
  • If income under a head is otherwise exempt, any corresponding loss also gets no tax treatment (i.e., ignore it — it cannot be set off or carried forward).

I. Restriction on Carry Forward for Closely Held Companies (Sec 79) & Search Cases (Sec 79A)

  • Key rule(s):
  • Sec 79: For a closely held company (company in which the public are not substantially interested), if there is a change in shareholding during the PY, brought-forward losses of an earlier year cannot be carried forward and set off unless, on the last day of the loss-set-off PY, at least 51% of the voting equity shares are beneficially held by the same persons who held at least 51% of such shares on the last day of the year(s) in which the loss was incurred.
  • Exception for eligible start-ups (Sec 80-IAC): even if the 51% test fails, carry forward is allowed if all shareholders holding shares on the last day of the loss year continue to hold those shares on the last day of the set-off year, and the loss was incurred within 10 years from the year of incorporation.
  • Changes NOT treated as a "change in shareholding" (Sec 79 relief situations):
  • Change due to the death of a shareholder.
  • Change due to a gift of shares to a relative.
  • Change in shareholding of an Indian subsidiary of a foreign company, pursuant to amalgamation/demerger of the foreign holding company, provided ≥ 51% of shareholders of the foreign predecessor continue as shareholders of the foreign successor.
  • Change pursuant to a resolution plan approved under the IBC, 2016 (or under Sec 241–242 of the Companies Act, 2013 via NCLT).
  • Change in an erstwhile public sector company (PSC) pursuant to strategic disinvestment, provided the ultimate holding company continues to hold (directly/through subsidiaries) at least 51% of voting power post-disinvestment — if this condition later fails, Sec 79 applies from that PY onward.
  • Sec 79A: where, consequent to a search (Sec 132), requisition (Sec 132A), or survey (Sec 133A, other than a TDS/TCS survey), the total income of a PY includes any undisclosed income, no set-off of any loss or unabsorbed depreciation is allowed against such undisclosed income.
  • Concept: Sec 79 stops "loss shell company" trading — buying a loss-making closely held company merely to shelter unrelated future profits from tax; Sec 79A denies the shelter of brought-forward losses against income unearthed in search/survey action.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Sec 79's test is on beneficial equity voting shareholding, not on total capital or preference shares.
  • The 10-year window for the start-up exception (moved up from an earlier 7-year window) is a common trap — always check the incorporation date against the loss year.
  • Sec 79A denies set-off only against the undisclosed income component; other regularly disclosed income of the same year is unaffected.
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — the OCR's illustrative numeric examples under Sec 79 (Example-1/2 shareholding patterns) are directionally consistent with the 51%-test logic as reproduced, but exact percentage figures in the source table should be cross-checked against the original if used for a numerical answer.

J. Carry Forward on Amalgamation, Demerger & Succession (Sec 72A, Sec 2(1B)/2(19AA))

  • Key rule(s) — carry forward matrix:
CaseAccumulated business loss ofCarried forward byTime limit
Amalgamation [Sec 2(1B)]Amalgamating Co.Amalgamated Co.Fresh 8 years*
Demerger [Sec 2(19AA)]Demerged Co.Resulting Co.Remaining part of original 8 years
Conversion of firm/proprietary concern into company [Sec 47(xiii)/(xiv)]Firm/proprietary concernSuccessor companyFresh 8 years*
Conversion of unlisted company into LLP [Sec 47(xiiib)]Unlisted companyLLPFresh 8 years*

\* ⚠️ VERIFY — effective for amalgamations/successions on or after 1/4/2025, the source states the "fresh 8 years" benefit is replaced by carry-forward for only the remaining part of the original 8-year period (i.e., no fresh lease of life). This aligns with a Finance Act 2025 change; confirm against the Finance Act 2025 text/CBDT notification before relying on it in a live exam answer, since it could not be freshly cross-checked against a primary source in this session.

  • Unabsorbed depreciation can be carried forward by the Amalgamated Co./Resulting Co./Successor Co./LLP for an unlimited period in all the above cases.
  • Only business losses (excluding speculative business loss) are eligible to be carried forward by the successor entity in these restructuring situations.
  • Sec 72A applicability (amalgamation of):
  1. A company owning an industrial undertaking, a ship, or a hotel, with another company; or
  2. A banking company with a specified bank (post Finance Act 2018 insertion); or
  3. One or more public sector company(ies) with one or more public sector company(ies); or
  4. An erstwhile public sector company (PSC) with one or more companies, where the share purchase agreement under strategic disinvestment restricted immediate amalgamation, and amalgamation is carried out within 5 years from the end of the PY in which that restriction ends.
  • Conditions — Amalgamating Co.:
  • Engaged in the business for 3 years or more prior to the date of amalgamation.
  • Holds at least 75% of the book value of fixed assets held 2 years prior to the date of amalgamation, continuously till the date of amalgamation.
  • Conditions — Amalgamated Co.:
  • Continues the business of the amalgamating company for a minimum of 5 years from the date of amalgamation.
  • Where an industrial undertaking is amalgamated, achieves at least 50% of the installed capacity before the end of 4 years from the date of amalgamation, and maintains that minimum level till the end of 5 years (Central Government may relax this on application).
  • Holds continuously, for a minimum of 5 years from the date of amalgamation, at least 75% of the book value of fixed assets of the amalgamating company acquired under the scheme.
  • Deemed income (Sec 72A): if any of the above amalgamated-company conditions are violated, the set-off loss/depreciation already allowed is treated as the income of the amalgamated company, taxable in the year of non-compliance.
  • Demerger: accumulated loss/unabsorbed depreciation directly relatable to the transferred undertaking is carried forward by the resulting company; if not directly relatable, it is apportioned between demerged and resulting company in the same proportion as the value of assets transferred.
  • Concept: Sec 72A is a relief provision that lets a genuine business restructuring (not a loss-shell purchase) inherit the predecessor's tax losses/depreciation, subject to strict continuity conditions on both sides.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • "Industrial undertaking" for Sec 72A purposes is specifically defined — manufacture/processing of goods, computer software, generation/distribution of power, telecom services, mining, and construction of ships/aircraft/rail systems.
  • Distinguish demerger (loss follows the specific undertaking, apportioned by asset value if not directly traceable) from amalgamation (loss/UD moves wholesale, subject to the 3-year/75%/5-year conditions).
  • Judicial note (Pramod Mittal, Delhi HC, 2013): loss of a dissolved firm cannot be carried forward by a partner who takes over the business as a sole proprietor — succession by inheritance (the only judicially/statutorily recognised exception under Sec 78(2)) requires succession by death/inheritance, not mere dissolution and takeover.
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Strategic disinvestmentSale of shareholding by Central/State Government in a PSC resulting in reduction of its shareholding below 51%, along with transfer of control to the buyer
Amalgamated companyThe company into which one or more companies merge (the surviving/new entity)
Resulting companyThe company to which an undertaking is transferred pursuant to a demerger

K. Practical Classification — Stock & Commodity Market Transactions (context for set-off rules)

  • Key rule(s):
  • Shares with actual delivery: PGBP income if held as stock-in-trade; Capital Gains if held as a capital asset.
  • Shares without delivery (intraday): always treated as speculative business income.
  • Derivatives (futures, options, currency futures) on a recognised stock exchange: always treated as normal (non-speculative) business income.
  • Concept: This classification decides which set-off "bucket" (Sec 70/71/73 speculative vs normal business) a trading loss falls into — critical before applying the set-off rules in Section G/H above.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • A common trap: intraday equity delivery-less trades are speculative (4-year carry forward, restricted set-off), while exchange-traded derivative F&O trades are normal business (8-year carry forward, broader set-off) — do not conflate the two.

  2.   3. Pramod Mittal v. ITO / CIT (Delhi HC, 2013) — on non-carry-forward of a dissolved firm's loss by the successor sole proprietor under Sec 78(2), as cited in source material.

11. Advance Tax, TDS & TCS

Where it fits: This is the "collection & recovery" chapter — instead of taxing income once at year-end, the Act collects tax throughout the year via (a) Advance Tax paid by the assessee himself, (b) TDS deducted by the payer, and (c) TCS collected by the seller/collector; interest (234A/B/C/D) and fees (234E/F/G/H) enforce timely compliance. Heavy on section-wise rate/threshold recall — this chapter alone carries a large weight in DT papers via MCQs and practical problems.

Advance Tax — Meaning, Liability & Computation

  • Key rule(s):
  • Advance tax = tax paid during the F.Y. itself (i.e., the P.Y.), in advance of assessment for the following A.Y.
  • Computed by estimating current-year total income, applying the applicable tax rates, and then reducing it by TDS + TCS + MAT/AMT credit + Foreign Tax Credit + Relief u/s 89 to arrive at the advance tax liability.
  • Sec 208: Advance tax is payable only if the estimated liability is ₹10,000 or more.
  • Sec 207(2) — Exception: A Resident Senior Citizen (60 years or more) not having any income chargeable under "PGBP" is not required to pay advance tax.

Advance Tax Liability = [Tax on estimated total income] - [TDS + TCS + MAT/AMT credit + FTC + Relief u/s 89]

  • Concept: Ensures the exchequer receives tax on a pay-as-you-earn basis rather than waiting till the return is filed.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • The senior-citizen exemption is lost the moment the senior citizen has any PGBP income, however small.
  • Don't forget to net off relief u/s 90/91 (DTAA/unilateral relief) too, in addition to relief u/s 89, while arriving at liability.

Due Dates & Instalments of Advance Tax (Sec 211)

  • Key rule(s) — for ALL assessees (including corporates):
Due dateCumulative advance tax payable
On or before 15th June of P.Y.Up to 15%
On or before 15th September of P.Y.Up to 45%
On or before 15th December of P.Y.Up to 75%
On or before 15th March of P.Y.Up to 100%
  • Assessee opting for presumptive taxation u/s 44AD/44ADA: entire 100% of advance tax payable in a single instalment by 15th March of the P.Y.
  • Tax paid up to 31st March of the P.Y. is treated as advance tax (even though technically paid after the last statutory instalment date).
  • Concept: The staggered percentages let the assessee build up liability gradually as the year's income becomes clearer.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: A very common MCQ trap — presumptive-income assessees get only one instalment (15th March, 100%), not the four-instalment schedule.

Advance Tax on AO's Order (Sec 210(3)/(4))

  • Key rule(s):
  • If the assessee has not paid or has short-paid advance tax, the AO may pass an order u/s 210 directing payment of advance tax in the instalment(s) falling due after the date of the order.
  • Such order can be passed up to the last day of February of the P.Y.
  • AO computes the advance tax using the higher of:

(i) Total income assessed in the latest completed assessment, or (ii) Total income declared in the ROI of any subsequent P.Y. (subsequent to the P.Y. for which assessment was last made).

  • Concept: A safety-net mechanism for AO to compel advance tax payment where self-estimation has clearly failed.

Interest u/s 234A — Delay in Filing Return

  • Key formula:

Interest u/s 234A = (Tax as per ROI - TDS/TCS/Advance Tax/MAT-AMT credit/Relief u/s 89, 90, 91) × 1% × No. of months (or part) of delay

  • Period: from the day after the due date of filing u/s 139(1) till the date of actual filing.
  • If return not filed at all, interest runs till the date of completion of assessment u/s 144.
  • Concept: Compensatory interest for delay in filing, computed on the net unpaid tax as on 1st April of the A.Y.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • CIT v. Dr. Prannoy Roy (SC): Credit is given for self-assessment tax paid before the due date of filing while computing 234A — i.e., interest is not charged on tax already discharged before the due date even though the return itself was filed late.
  • Interest is calculated at 1% per month or part of a month — even a single day's delay counts as a full month.

Interest u/s 234B — Non-payment/Short Payment of Advance Tax

  • Key formula:

Interest u/s 234B = Advance Tax Short-paid × 1% × No. of months (or part) from 1st April of A.Y. till date of payment

  • Rule: Not applicable at all if the assessee has paid 90% or more of the assessed advance tax by 31st March of the P.Y.
  • Note: If total income changes upon processing u/s 143(1) or assessment u/s 143(3), the tax as per 143(1)/143(3) replaces "tax as per ROI" for both 234A and 234B (this substitution rule applies only to these two sections, not 234C).
  • Concept: Penal interest for genuinely defaulting on the advance-tax schedule as a whole (tested against the 90% threshold), unlike 234C which tests each instalment.

Interest u/s 234C — Deferment of Advance Tax Instalments

  • Key formula:

Interest u/s 234C = Shortfall in instalment × 1% × 3 months & for 1st, 2nd & 3rd instalment shortfall 1 month & for the last (15 March) instalment shortfall

  • Always computed on tax as per ROI (never on assessed tax, unlike 234A/234B).
  • No interest for 1st or 2nd instalment shortfall if the assessee has paid at least 12% of tax (by 15 June) and at least 36% of tax (by 15 September) respectively.
  • Capital gains / casual income (lottery, game-show winnings) / dividend / PGBP income arising for the first time: since these cannot be estimated in advance, the corresponding advance tax must be paid in the remaining instalments after the income actually arises; if no instalment remains (income received between 16th March and 31st March), the tax must still be paid by 31st March of the P.Y. Interest u/s 234C for such income runs only from the quarter in which it is actually received.
  • Concept: Penalises deferment of each instalment individually (as opposed to 234B, which looks at the year-end 90% test).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Remember the asymmetry — 12%/36% concession exists only for instalments 1 & 2; there's no such cushion for the 3rd (75%) instalment.

Interest u/s 234A(3) & 234B(3) — Reassessment u/s 147 after 143(1)/143(3)

  • Key rule(s):
  • 234A(3): Where assessee files a late return (or does not file at all) in response to notice u/s 148, interest @1% p.m. or part thereof is charged on: Tax on income assessed/reassessed u/s 147 minus tax as per earlier intimation u/s 143(1)/assessment.
  • Period if return filed u/s 148: from expiry of time allowed in the 148 notice till date of filing.
  • Period if return not filed: from expiry of time allowed in the 148 notice till completion of assessment u/s 147.
  • 234B(3): Interest @1% p.m. or part thereof on the same amount, from 1st April of the A.Y. till the date of completion of assessment u/s 147.
  • Concept: Extends 234A/234B logic to the reassessment scenario, so that delay/shortfall discovered only at reassessment stage is not left uncompensated.

Interest u/s 234D — Excess Refund

  • Key rule(s):
  • Applicable where a refund granted u/s 143(1) turns out, on completion of regular assessment, to be excess or not due at all.
  • Interest @0.5% per month or part of a month on the excess refund, from the date of grant of refund till the date of completion of assessment.
  • Concept: Mirror-image of 244A (interest on refund) — here the assessee pays interest for having enjoyed a refund that later proves excessive.

Fees u/s 234E, 234F, 234G & 234H

SectionDefaultFee
234EDelay in filing quarterly TDS/TCS statement₹200/day of default (cannot exceed TDS/TCS deductible/collectible); payable before filing the statement
234FFailure to furnish ROI within time u/s 139(1)₹5,000; capped at ₹1,000 if total income does not exceed ₹5 lakh
234GDonee trust/institution u/s 35(1)(ii)/(iia)/(iii) or 80G(5) fails to file statement/donation certificate to PDGIT(Systems)/donor by 31st May of next F.Y.₹200/day of default, capped at the amount in respect of which the failure occurred
234HLinking PAN with Aadhaar after the prescribed date₹500 if linked between 1/4/2022–30/6/2022; ₹1,000 if linked on/after 1/7/2022
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: 234F's ₹1,000 concession is based on total income, not gross total income — watch this in problems combining deductions.

Sec 245 — Set-off & Withholding of Refunds

  • Key rule(s):
  • Where refund is due for one A.Y. and demand is payable for another, PCCIT/CCIT/PCIT/CIT/AO may — after intimating the assessee — set off the refund against the outstanding demand instead of paying it out.
  • If no such set-off is made and assessment/reassessment for that year is pending, the AO may (for reasons recorded in writing, with prior approval of PCIT/CIT) withhold the refund up to 60 days from the date such assessment/reassessment is made.
  • Concept: Protects revenue interest while an assessment is still open, without indefinitely denying the assessee's refund.

Interest on Refund — Sec 244A

  • Key rule(s): Simple interest @0.5% per month or part of a month, paid by the Department.
Source of refundReturn filed on/before due date u/s 139(1)Return filed after due date
Out of TDS/TCS & Advance Tax (Part A)From 1st April of A.Y. till date refund is grantedFrom date of filing return till date refund is granted
Out of Self-Assessment Tax u/s 140A (Part B)From date of filing return or date of payment of tax, whichever is later, till date refund is grantedSame as above
  • No interest under Part A/B if the refund is less than 10% of the tax determined u/s 143(1) or on regular assessment.
  • Interest on refund is taxable under "Income from Other Sources".
  • If a deductor deposits excess TDS with Govt., he is entitled to a refund (via Form 26B) and interest @0.5% p.m. from the date he claims the refund till the date it is granted.
  • For any other refund reason, interest runs from the date of payment of the tax/penalty till the date of grant of refund.
  • Additional interest @3% p.a. (Sec 244A(1A)) is payable where refund arises from giving effect to an order u/s 250/254/260/262/263/264 (other than by a fresh assessment/reassessment) — from the day following expiry of the time allowed u/s 153(5) till the date the refund is granted; any period during which the refund was validly withheld u/s 245(2) is excluded.

TDS — General Principles

  • Key rule(s):
  • TDS obligation arises at payment or at crediting the payee's account, whichever is earlier — except for the following, where TDS applies only at the time of payment: Salary (192), EPF payment (192A), Dividend (194), Winnings under 194B/194BB/194BA, Maturity of life insurance policy (194DA), Compensation on compulsory acquisition (194LA), Cash withdrawal from bank (194N).
  • TDS rates under the Act (other than salary/NR payments) are flat rates (1%, 2%, 5%, 10% etc.) — surcharge & Health-and-Education Cess apply only for payments to NR/Foreign Company or for salary.
  • Sec 206AA — No PAN furnished by payee: TDS = higher of (i) rate under the respective section, or (ii) 20% (5% instead of 20% specifically for sec 194-O / 194-Q).
  • Sec 206AA does not apply to NR/Foreign Company payees (for interest, dividend, royalty, FTS, or transfer of capital asset) if they furnish: name, email & contact; foreign address; Tax Residency Certificate from their government; and Tax Identification Number (or a unique identifying number if TIN unavailable).
  • If payer fails to deduct TDS, the payee remains liable to pay the tax directly; but if TDS was deducted and not deposited by the payer, the payee cannot be asked to pay that tax again (Sec 205).

  • Concept: This chart is the single most tested part of the chapter — rate + threshold recall drives most MCQs and computation problems.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Watch the "Individual/HUF payer" carve-outs (194C/H/I/J/M/R) — TDS liability is triggered only if last year's turnover (business) exceeded ₹1 crore or gross receipts (profession) exceeded ₹50 lakh.
  • Thresholds for 194, 194A, 194D/G/H, 194-I, 194J, 194K, 194LA were raised effective 1 April 2025 (Finance Act 2025) — make sure you quote the current figures in the table above, not older textbook numbers.
  • 194-IB and 194M rates were cut from 5% to 2% with effect from 1 October 2024.
  • 194-O rate was cut from 1% to 0.1% with effect from 1 April 2025, aligning it with 194-Q.

Sec 194BA — TDS on Net Winnings from Online Games

  • Key formula(s):

Net winning (first withdrawal) = A - (B + C)
Net winning (subsequent withdrawal) = A - (B + C + E)
Net winning (at year-end, on closing balance) = (A + D) - (B + C + E)

SymbolMeaning
AAggregate amount withdrawn from user account till date (of that withdrawal, or during the F.Y. for the year-end computation)
BAggregate non-taxable deposits made till that date
COpening balance of user account at the start of the F.Y.
DClosing balance of user account at the end of the F.Y.
ENet winnings on which TDS has already been deducted at earlier withdrawal(s)
  • TDS is deducted at 30% on net winnings, both at every withdrawal during the year and again at year-end on the closing balance.
  • Concept: Sec 115BBJ taxes "net winnings" from online games at 30% (flat, no basic exemption/slab benefit); Sec 194BA operationalises TDS on the same base at each withdrawal event.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Deposits that are non-taxable (i.e., from already-taxed funds, including borrowed money) reduce net winnings; taxable deposits (bonus/referral bonus/promotional credits usable only for play, not withdrawal) are excluded from B/C/D unless later "recharacterised" as withdrawable.
  • Winnings wholly/partly in kind (car, gadgets) are treated as a deemed taxable deposit and simultaneous withdrawal of the FMV, and TDS must be ensured before the prize is released.
  • CBDT relaxation: tax need not be deducted on a withdrawal if net winnings comprised in it do not exceed ₹100 in a month — provided the shortfall is made good at the next qualifying withdrawal or at year-end, and the deductor undertakes to bear any shortfall.
  • Multiple user accounts of the same person are aggregated; inter-account transfers are not treated as deposit/withdrawal.

Sec 194-O / 194-Q Interplay & E-commerce Nuances

  • Key rule(s):
  • If both 206C(1)/(1F)/(1G) (TCS) and 194Q (TDS) apply to the same transaction, TCS prevails (buyer's 194Q obligation is excused).
  • If both 194-O and 194Q apply to the same transaction, 194-O (TDS by e-commerce operator) prevails.
  • If payee's PAN is unavailable, TDS under 194-O and 194Q is at 5% (not the general 206AA rate of 20%).
  • Once TDS is deducted (or excused only due to the ₹5 lakh threshold) u/s 194-O, no TDS is required under any other section on the same amount, except for amounts the e-commerce operator earns for advertising/other unrelated services.
  • 194-Q does not apply to transactions in securities/commodities traded through recognised stock/commodity exchanges (including IFSC exchanges) or electricity/REC/energy-saving certificates traded through power exchanges.
  • 194-Q is not applicable to NR buyers (unless they have a PE in India to which the purchase relates), nor where CG/SG is the seller (though PSUs/statutory bodies as sellers are still covered).
  • Concept: These are the CBDT-clarified "tie-breaker" rules students must apply whenever a fact pattern triggers more than one TDS/TCS section simultaneously.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: GST/IDT shown separately in the invoice is excluded from the 194Q TDS base — but on advance payments, TDS must be deducted on the full advance since the GST component is not yet known.

Sec 194R — TDS on Benefits/Perquisites in Business/Profession

  • Key rule(s):
  • 10% TDS on any benefit or perquisite (whether or not convertible into money) arising from carrying on business/profession, if the aggregate value to a person in the P.Y. exceeds ₹20,000.
  • Applies even to capital-nature benefits (e.g., a car or land given free).
  • If the benefit is wholly/partly in kind and the cash portion is insufficient to cover TDS, the payer must ensure tax has been paid before releasing the benefit — either by collecting the TDS amount from the recipient, paying it himself, or the recipient pays it as advance tax and furnishes proof.
  • Concept: Targets non-cash incentives (freebies, sponsored trips, free samples, discounted schemes) given in the course of business that were earlier escaping the TDS net.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Sales discounts, cash discounts and rebates given to customers are excluded — but free samples (e.g., to doctors) are not excluded.
  • Bonus shares/rights shares issued to all shareholders are outside the scope of 194R.
  • Where group-activity benefits (e.g., dealer conferences) cannot be reasonably allocated to individual participants, the payer may choose to forgo the expense deduction instead of deducting TDS — in which case he is not treated as an assessee-in-default u/s 201.
  • Loan waiver/settlement by scheduled banks/co-op banks/PFIs/NBFCs/ARCs is not treated as a benefit/perquisite for this section.

Sec 194N — TDS on Cash Withdrawal

  • Key rule(s):
  • 2% TDS on cash withdrawal in excess of ₹1 crore in a P.Y. (₹3 crore for a co-operative society recipient), deducted only on the excess.
  • If the recipient has not filed ROI for all three preceding P.Y.s (for which the 139(1) due date has expired): 2% on withdrawal between ₹20 lakh–₹1 crore, and 5% above ₹1 crore.
  • TDS required only at the time of payment.
  • Excluded payees: Government, banks/co-op banks/post office & their business correspondents, White Label ATM operators, Cash Replenishment Agencies, registered APMC commission agents (certified farmer payments), and authorised dealers/FFMCs for specified forex-related cash disbursements.
  • Concept: A quasi-anti-black-money provision discouraging large cash withdrawals rather than a conventional income-based TDS.

TCS — Sec 206C(1F): Sale of Motor Vehicle/Notified Goods

  • Key rule(s):
  • 1% TCS on sale of a motor vehicle, or of specified notified luxury goods, where the value of a single transaction exceeds ₹10 lakh (threshold tested transaction-wise, not on aggregate annual sales).
  • Applies only at the retail sale level — no TCS on sale by manufacturers to dealers/distributors.
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — the OCR lists an expanded notified-goods list (wrist watches, art pieces/antiques, collectibles, yachts/rowing boats/canoes/helicopters, sunglasses, handbags, shoes, sportswear equipment, home theatre systems, race/polo horses) that reflects a 2025 CBDT notification expanding Sec 206C(1F) beyond motor vehicles — confirm the exact notification number/date before quoting it as authority in an answer.
  • Concept: Extends TCS to high-value discretionary/luxury purchases as a data-gathering and anti-evasion tool.

TCS — Sec 206C(1G): Liberalised Remittance Scheme (LRS) & Overseas Tour Packages (OTPP)

  • Key formula/rule:
PurposeRate
LRS remittance — education or medical treatment5% of amount in excess of ₹10 lakh
LRS remittance — any other purpose20% of amount in excess of ₹10 lakh
Sale of Overseas Tour Programme Package (OTPP)5% of sale value up to ₹10 lakh, and 20% of the amount exceeding ₹10 lakh
  • Collector: Authorised Dealer (for LRS remittances); Seller of the OTPP (for tour packages).
  • No TCS if: buyer has deducted TDS under any provision on the same amount, buyer is CG/SG/embassy/consulate/local authority, or buyer is an NR visiting India.
  • LRS remittance funded out of an education loan taken from a specified financial institution (Sec 80E) — no TCS.
  • The ₹10 lakh threshold for LRS is a combined limit across purposes and across authorised dealers for the same remitter in a P.Y. (the second dealer takes a self-declaration of prior remittances).
  • Overseas credit-card spends are not counted within LRS (no TCS on international credit card spend while abroad).
  • Concept: Captures high-value outward personal remittances and holiday packages within the tax net at source.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Note the OTPP rate structure has no nil slab up to ₹10 lakh — the first ₹10 lakh of an OTPP sale is itself taxed at 5% (unlike ordinary LRS remittances, where amounts up to ₹10 lakh escape TCS entirely).

Sec 206CC — Higher TCS Rate for Non-furnishing of PAN/Aadhaar

  • Key rule(s): TCS rate = higher of (a) twice the specified rate, or (b) 5%.
  • From 1 July 2023, this higher rate is capped at 20%.

Miscellaneous TDS Provisions

  • Sec 196: No TDS where payee is Government, RBI, a statutory corporation whose income is exempt, Mutual Fund, or the New Pension System Trust.
  • Sec 197 — Lower/Nil deduction certificate: Where the assessee's income is not liable to tax, or taxable at a lower rate (e.g., due to brought-forward losses), the AO may — on application — issue a certificate for nil/lower TDS; the payer then deducts as per the certificate.
  • Sec 197A — Form 15G/15H: Resident (other than a company/firm) whose total income is below the basic exemption limit may furnish Form 15G for no TDS u/ss 192A, 193, 194, 194A, 194D, 194DA, 194-I, 194K. Resident senior citizens may furnish Form 15H so long as tax payable for the year is NIL (even after rebate u/s 87A). The benefit is unavailable if the very income covered by these sections itself exceeds the basic exemption limit.
  • Sec 198: TDS is deemed income of the payee, except tax borne by employer on non-monetary perquisites (exempt to employee u/s 10(10CC)) and TDS u/s 194N.
  • Sec 199: TDS credit is available to the person from whose income the deduction was made, except (i) under clubbing provisions, credit goes to the person in whose hands the income is ultimately taxed, and (ii) tax borne by employer on non-monetary perquisites — credit available to the employee.

Due Dates — TDS/TCS Payment & Quarterly Returns

TDS/TCS deducted/collected inTDS payment due dateTCS payment due date
April to February7th of the next month7th of the next month
March30th April of next F.Y.7th April of next F.Y.
  • Sec 194-IA, 194-IB, 194M: No TAN required; TDS to be deposited within 30 days from the end of the month of deduction, along with the return-cum-challan in Form 26QB / 26QC / 26QD respectively.
Quarter endedTDS return due dateTCS return due date
30th June31st July15th July
30th September31st October15th October
31st December31st January15th January
31st March31st May15th May
  • Late filing of TDS/TCS return: fee of ₹200/day u/s 234E; if filed after 1 year from the prescribed date, penalty u/s 271H of ₹10,000 to ₹1,00,000 also applies.

Sec 200A/206CB — Processing of TDS/TCS Statements

  • Key rule(s):
  • TDS/TCS statements are processed electronically, permitting adjustment for arithmetical errors and incorrect claims apparent from the statement.
  • Intimation of the resulting demand/refund (with interest/fees) is sent to the deductor/collector within 1 year from the end of the F.Y. in which the statement was filed.

Sec 201 — Assessee-in-Default & Interest u/s 201(1A)

  • Key rule(s):
  • If TDS is not deducted, or deducted but not deposited, the payer is treated as "assessee in default" and is liable to penalty u/s 221, capped at 100% of the TDS amount.
  • Time limit for AO's order treating a person as assessee-in-default for non-deduction: within 6 years from the end of the F.Y. in which payment/credit was made (⚠️ VERIFY — several ICAI/professional summaries note a longer 7-year limit specifically for payments to non-residents u/s 195; confirm which limit your source material intends before quoting a single figure in an answer).
  • If TDS was deducted but not deposited, there is no time limit to treat the payer as assessee-in-default.
  • Exception — payer is not treated as assessee-in-default (though interest u/s 201(1A) may still apply) if the payee: (i) has filed his ROI u/s 139, (ii) has included the relevant sum in that ROI, (iii) has paid tax due on the income so declared, and (iv) the payer obtains a CA certificate in Form 26A confirming all this.
  • Interest u/s 201(1A): Late deduction — 1% p.m. or part thereof, from the date TDS was deductible till the date actually deducted. Late payment — 1.5% p.m. or part thereof, from the date TDS was actually deducted till the date actually paid.
  • Concept: Distinguishes the penalty for default (201/221, requiring the default to be established) from the automatic compensatory interest (201(1A), which applies regardless of bona fide belief).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Per Sun Outsourcing Solutions (T&AP Trib.), interest u/s 201(1A) is automatic and does not require proof of wilful default — even a bona fide belief that TDS did not apply will not save the payer from interest. Per BDR Finvest (Delhi HC), credit for TDS cannot be denied to the deductee merely because the deductor failed to deposit it or it doesn't reflect in Form 26AS — recourse lies against the defaulting deductor, not the deductee.

Sec 239A — Refund for Denying Liability to Deduct Tax

  • Key rule(s):
  • Applies where, under a written arrangement, TDS u/s 195 (on income other than interest) is to be borne by the payer, and the payer, having paid such tax, later claims no tax was actually required to be deducted.
  • Payer may apply to the AO in Form 29D within 30 days of payment of such tax, seeking a refund.
  • AO passes a reasoned order (after hearing the applicant) within 6 months from the end of the month in which the application is received.
  • Concept: A dedicated refund route for the (fairly common in cross-border contracts) "grossed-up"/tax-borne-by-payer arrangements where the deduction later proves to have been unnecessary.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Air India Ltd. (SC, 2023) held that Sec 90(2) gives primacy to a more beneficial DTAA rate over Sec 4/5 charging provisions, so Sec 206AA's mandatory 20% cannot override a lower DTAA rate where the payee has no PAN — TDS at the DTAA rate is valid and 206AA is not attracted in such a case.

  2.   3. CBDT Circulars/Notifications — Circular 9/2012 (gas transportation, Sec 194C), Circular 21/2017 (PSF, Sec 194-I), CBDT guidelines on Sec 194R, 194-O and 194Q (issued under respective introducing Finance Acts), and Notification 05/2017 (interest income of minor child, Sec 194A).
  4. Key Supreme Court/High Court rulings referenced: CIT v. Dr. Prannoy Roy (Sec 234A), ITC Ltd. (2016) (tips not salary), Kotak Securities Ltd. (2016), Bharti Cellular Ltd. (2024), Air India Ltd. (2023) (Sec 206AA vs DTAA), Pioneer Overseas Corporation (2022), BDR Finvest Pvt. Ltd. (2024).
