153(5A)TPO gives effect to Sec 263 order and forwards to AOAO modifies assessment within 2 months from end of the month of receipt
153(6)(i)Assessment/reassessment per a court/appellate finding or direction (Sec 150)12 months from end of the month the order is received/passed
153(6)(ii)Assessment on a partner consequent to Sec 147 assessment on the firm12 months from end of the month the firm's assessment order was passed
  • Exclusions extending the Sec 153 clock (illustrative): period between AO informing government of a Sec 10(21)/(22B)/(23A)/(23B) contravention and receipt of the withdrawal notification; period of a Sec 142(2A) special-audit direction (till report due date, or till a court order on a challenge is received); period of a Sec 142A valuation reference (till report received); period of a Sec 158A declaration (max 60 days); period of an application to the BAR (Board for Advance Rulings); period of a Sec 90/90A information-exchange reference (till info received, or 1 year, whichever is less); period of a Sec 12AB(4) reference to PCIT/CIT (till order copy received); period a court stays the assessment proceeding.
  • Floor rule: after excluding the above periods, if the remaining time available to the AO is less than 60 days, it is extended to 60 days.
  • Concept: Sec 153 is the master assessment-completion clock — every assessment type (scrutiny, BJA, reassessment, giving-effect orders) has its own trigger date and duration, further stretched by search/TPO-reference extensions and specific procedural exclusions.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: The 12-month standard period (post AY 2022-23) is the default to memorise cold; older-AY variants (9/18/21 months) are largely historical/legacy and less likely to be tested directly, but the +12 months for search-pending or TPO-reference cases, and the 60-day floor rule, are high-yield numericals.

Rectification & Demand Notice — Sec 154, 156, 156A

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Sec 154 — Rectification of mistake apparent from record (not a debatable mistake), in: any order passed by the authority; Sec 143(1) intimation; TDS/TCS intimation u/s 200A/206CB(1).
  • Can be done suo motu or on assessee's application; no fee, no prescribed form.

Time limit (suo motu) = 4 years from end of the FY in which the order sought to be rectified was passed
Time limit (on application) = 6 months from end of the month the application is received

  • A rectified order can itself be further rectified — the 4-year clock resets from the end of the year the rectified order was passed.
  • A rectified order (whether passed suo motu or on application) is an appealable order.
  • Sec 156 — Demand notice: issued for tax/interest/penalty/other sum payable per any order; assessee must pay within 30 days of receipt; default ⇒ assessee-in-default, liable to interest u/s 220 and penalty u/s 221. Intimations u/s 143(1)/200A(1)/206CB(1) are deemed demand notices.
  • Sec 156A: where a demand under Sec 156 is reduced by an order of the Adjudicating Authority under the IBC, 2016, AO modifies and re-serves a revised demand notice; if that IBC order is itself modified by NCLT/Supreme Court, the demand notice is revised again accordingly.
  • Concept: Sec 154 fixes clerical/apparent errors without reopening the substantive assessment; Sec 156 crystallises the payable amount into an enforceable demand.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: "Mistake apparent from record" excludes anything debatable (requiring long-drawn reasoning/argument) — a classic exam distinguishing test.

Protective Assessment (No Specific Section)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s): where ownership of income is disputed/doubtful, AO may assess the same income in the hands of all claimants, to protect revenue's interest — but tax can be recovered from only one of them (whichever is ultimately held to be the real owner).
  • Concept: A safeguard mechanism for genuine ownership disputes (e.g., civil litigation, benami transactions), not a device to double-tax the same income.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Protective assessment ≠ double taxation — recovery is restricted to a single person once ownership is finally determined.

Special Procedure for Assessment in Search Cases — Chapter XIV-B (Sec 158BA–158BFA)

(Applies to search u/s 132 / requisition u/s 132A initiated/made on or after 1st September 2024, added by FA 2024)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):
  • Block Period: the 6 AYs preceding the PY of search/requisition, plus the period from 1st April of the search-PY to the date of execution of the last search authorisation (or actual receipt of assets/books, for a requisition).

Undisclosed income of Block Period = Income declared in the ITR-B return (Sec 158BC) + Income determined by AO

  • Excluded from undisclosed income: income already assessed u/s 143(3)/144/147/153A/153C/158BC before the date of search/requisition; income already declared in a Sec 139/142(1) return (not otherwise covered); income computed from regular books/documents for the pre-search period (past completed years, current year up to search date, and the search-execution period itself), unless AO finds part of it undisclosed; income referred to u/s 115A(5)/115G/194P.
  • Sec 158BC: AO issues notice for an ITR-B return within a period specified, max 60 days (extendable by a further 30 days in limited audit-pending circumstances), with prior approval of Addl. CIT/Addl. DIT/JC/JD. Such return is deemed a Sec 139 return (notice u/s 143(2) then follows) but cannot be revised; Sec 143(1) does not apply to it; no separate Sec 148 notice is needed for this chapter.
  • Abatement: any assessment/reassessment pending as on date of search/requisition (for the block-period years) abates (except appeals/revision, which continue); any TPO reference/order also abates.
  • Sec 158BD — Other person's undisclosed income: where seized material belongs/pertains/relates to a person other than the one searched, it is handed to that person's jurisdictional AO, who then follows the same Sec 158BA/BB/BC procedure; the "date of search" for that other person is the date his AO actually receives the material.
  • Tax rate — Sec 113: flat 60% on the total undisclosed income of the block period (plus applicable surcharge/cess).
  • No interest/penalty overlap — Sec 158BF: no interest u/s 234A/234B/234C, and no Sec 270A penalty, on the block-period undisclosed income.
  • Sec 158BE — Time limit for block assessment: 12 months from the end of the quarter in which the last search authorisation was executed/requisition made (searched person); 12 months from end of the quarter the Sec 158BC notice was issued (other person, Sec 158BD); +12 months if referred to TPO; time extended to 13 months where the 30-day return-filing extension was granted; exclusion available (max 6 months) for the period between search initiation and handover of seized material to the jurisdictional AO.
  • Sec 158BFA — Interest & penalty:
  • Interest: simple interest @1.5% per month (or part) on the tax on undisclosed income, from the day after expiry of the notice period to completion of assessment, if the ITR-B return is filed late/not filed.
  • Penalty: 50% of the tax payable on the undisclosed income; this penalty (and Sec 271AAD/271D/271DA/271E) is waived if the assessee has filed the ITR-B return, paid the tax due (or offered seized money for adjustment), furnished proof of payment with the return, and has not appealed the assessed portion matching the return — waiver does not extend to the excess where the AO's determined undisclosed income exceeds the returned figure.
  • Concept: Chapter XIV-B reintroduces a separate, fixed-rate block assessment for post-1/9/2024 search cases (in place of the earlier Sec 153A/153C regime), taxing undisclosed income of a defined multi-year block at a flat 60%, outside the normal slab/interest/Sec 270A framework.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Do not confuse this with the old Sec 153A/153C search-assessment machinery — that regime still governs searches conducted before 1st September 2024; Chapter XIV-B is exclusively for searches/requisitions on/after that date.
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — the Sec 158BFA(1) interest rate of 1.5% per month should be cross-checked against the bare Act/latest CBDT clarification for your exact exam attempt; the historical (pre-2003) block-assessment interest rate under this section was aligned to the Sec 234A rate of 1% per month, and this chapter's reintroduction via FA 2024 is one of the newest provisions in the syllabus.
  • Interest/penalty waiver conditions under Sec 158BFA(2) are cumulative — missing even one (e.g., filing an appeal on the returned portion) forfeits the entire concession.

Definitions

TermMeaning
Block Period6 AYs preceding the search/requisition PY, plus the part-year up to the last search-authorisation/receipt date
ITR-BPrescribed return form for declaring undisclosed income of the block period under Sec 158BC
PanchnamaSearch-conclusion document; its date fixes the "date of search" for limitation purposes

References

  1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 116–156A, 158B–158BFA (as amended up to Finance (No. 2) Act 2024 and Finance Act 2025), for authority hierarchy, PAN/Aadhaar, search & seizure, assessment/reassessment procedure, updated return, and block assessment provisions.
  2. Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024 — reconstitution of reassessment time limits (Sec 148/149/151) w.e.f. 1st September 2024, and reintroduction of block-assessment Chapter XIV-B (Sec 158BA–158BFA) for searches/requisitions on/after that date.
  3. Finance Act, 2025 (and preceding Finance Act 2022 for original enactment) — extension of the updated-return time limit under Sec 139(8A)/140B to 48 months with graded additional-tax slabs (25%/50%/60%/70%).
  4. CBDT Circular No. 11/2024 (w.e.f. 1/10/2024) — revised monetary limits of authorities (CIT/PCIT, CCIT, PCCIT) for condonation of delay in filing a loss return, u/s 119(2)(b) read with Sec 139.
  5. ICAI — Study Material / RTP / MTP for CA Final Direct Tax Laws & International Taxation (Assessment Procedure chapter), for the seventh-proviso Sec 139(1) high-value-transaction thresholds and PAN quoting (Rule 114B) thresholds.

13. Appeals, Revisions & Dispute Resolution Committee

Where it fits: the litigation ladder after an assessment/penalty order — JC(A)/CIT(A) → ITAT → High Court → Supreme Court, plus the departmental revision powers (Sec 263/264) and the alternate, faster Dispute Resolution Committee (Sec 245MA) route for small, uncomplicated disputes.

Appeal to Joint Commissioner (Appeals) / Commissioner (Appeals) — Sec 246, 246A–251

  • Key rules:
  • Sec 246(1) — Appeal to JC(A): for orders passed on or after 1.4.2023 by an AO below the rank of Joint Commissioner, appeal lies to JC(A) — covers assessment orders u/s 143(3)/144/147, intimation u/s 143(1)/200A/206CB, rectification u/s 154/155, order u/s 201/206C(6A) (assessee-in-default), and penalty orders. Exception: if the AO's order was passed with the prior approval of an authority above the rank of Deputy Commissioner, appeal goes to CIT(A) instead.
  • Sec 246A — Appeal to CIT(A): covers a wider list — assessment/reassessment orders u/s 143(3), 144, 147, 158BC; intimations u/s 143(1)/200A/206CB; rectification u/s 154/155; an order where the assessee denies liability to be assessed; and orders u/s 92CD, 115VP, 163, 170, 171, 201, 206C(6A), 221, 237, 239A, and penalty orders.
  • CBDT (or an authorised IT authority) may transfer a pending appeal between JC(A) and CIT(A); the appellant must be given a fresh opportunity of being heard after transfer.
  • Time limit to file: 30 days from date of receipt of the notice of demand (assessment/penalty) or of the order/intimation (any other case); JC(A)/CIT(A) may condone delay for sufficient cause.
  • Form: Form No. 35 (Memorandum of Appeal), with statement of facts, grounds of appeal, copy of order/intimation, and filing fee.
  • Time to dispose (advisory): where possible, within 1 year from the end of the FY in which the appeal is filed or transferred.
  • Pre-condition for admission of appeal: assessee must have paid tax on the income returned by him; if no return was filed, tax equal to advance tax payable — though JC(A)/CIT(A) may, on application, exempt the assessee from this payment and still admit the appeal.
  • Only the assessee can file this first appeal (department has no right of first appeal).
  • Concept: the first appellate stage against an AO-level order; choice of forum (JC(A) vs CIT(A)) turns on the rank of the officer who passed the order and the nature of the order.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Do not confuse the 30-day limitation (first appeal) with the 60-day limit for ITAT appeals.
  • Remember the JC(A) forum is a Finance Act 2023 innovation — apply the "below rank of JC" test carefully in MCQs/case scenarios.
  • The 1-year disposal timeline is advisory ("if possible"), not a hard limitation — do not treat it as void if breached.

Appeal to ITAT — Sec 252–255

  • Key rules:
  • Bench: normally a Division Bench (1 Judicial + 1 Accountant Member); a Single Member Bench may hear the case if the assessee's total income does not exceed ₹50 lakh. Decision is by majority; on an equal split, the point goes to the President, who refers it to another member — decision then follows majority.
  • Time limit to file: 60 days from the end of the month in which the order appealed against is communicated (Sec 253(3)).
  • Form: Form No. 36, with statement of facts, grounds of appeal, copy of order, and filing fee.
  • Cross objections: the other party may file Form No. 36A within 30 days of receiving notice that an appeal has been filed — no fee payable.
  • Time to dispose (advisory): where possible, within 4 years from the end of the FY in which the appeal is filed (Sec 254(2A)).
  • Appealable orders: order of JC(A)/CIT(A); AO's order passed on DRP directions u/s 144C; revision order u/s 263; AO's order passed with CIT/PCIT approval u/s 144BA (GAAR); and other specified orders of CIT/CCIT/DIT/DGIT/PCIT/PDIT/PDGIT.
  • Rectification u/s 254(2): ITAT may rectify a mistake apparent from the record, within 6 months from the end of the month in which the order was passed, suo motu or on application by the assessee/AO. ITAT has no power of review — only rectification of an apparent mistake.
  • Concept: the first forum that is a mixed judicial-cum-technical Tribunal and the last forum on pure questions of fact.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • ITAT can set aside and remand to the AO for fresh assessment — JC(A)/CIT(A) generally cannot, except where the appeal is against an order u/s 144 (best judgment assessment), where CIT(A) may set aside and remand — inserted by FA 2024 w.e.f. 1.10.2024.
  • ITAT has no power to review/re-appreciate its own order under Sec 254(2) — Earnest Exports Ltd. (Bom.) / Lachman Dass Bhatia Hingwala (Delhi HC), reaffirmed in Reliance Telecom Ltd. (2022)(SC).
  • ITAT cannot dismiss an appeal for mere non-appearance without deciding on merits — Ritha Sabapathy (2019)(Mad.).

Stay of Demand by ITAT — Sec 254(2A)

  • Key formula(s)/rule(s):

Minimum deposit for stay = 20% × (disputed tax + interest + penalty + fee)
— or the assessee furnishes security of an equivalent amount.

  • Initial stay period: up to 180 days.
  • Extension: if ITAT cannot dispose of the appeal within 180 days for reasons not attributable to the assessee, it may extend the stay, but the total stay (original + extensions) cannot exceed 365 days.
  • Beyond 365 days, the stay stands automatically vacated — even if the delay is due to the Department — subject to the SC's reading down below.
  • Concept: a partial-payment safeguard so recovery doesn't proceed while a bona fide appeal is pending, balanced against a hard outer time cap to prevent indefinite stays.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • ⚠️ VERIFY — the OCR cites Pepsi Foods Ltd. (2021) as a Supreme Court ruling; the landmark judgment reading down the third proviso to Sec 254(2A) (striking the automatic vacation of stay where delay is not attributable to the assessee) is generally attributed to the Delhi High Court (2015), later followed/affirmed in subsequent rulings — confirm the exact forum/year before quoting in an answer.
  • Key holding (regardless of forum): the automatic-vacation-of-stay proviso applies only if the delay in disposal is attributable to the assessee; if the delay is the Department's fault, the stay does not automatically lapse at 365 days.
  • Fee for a stay application to ITAT: ₹500.

Difference in powers — JC(A)/CIT(A) vs ITAT

PowerJC(A)/CIT(A)ITAT
Enhance the assessmentYesNo
Reduce/confirm the assessmentYesYes
Cancel the assessmentYesYes
Set aside & remand to AO for fresh assessmentNo (except Sec 144 orders, w.e.f. 1.10.2024)Yes
Condone delayYesYes
Make further inquiriesYesYes
Rectify its own orderYes — Sec 154Yes — Sec 254(2)
Review its own orderNoNo
Admit additional grounds of appealYesYes
Admit additional evidenceYes (conditions apply)Yes (conditions apply)
Grant stay of demandYesYes
Award costs for a frivolous appealNoYes
Reject the appealYesYes
  • Concept: JC(A)/CIT(A) has enhancement power (can worsen the assessee's position) that ITAT lacks; ITAT alone can remand generally and award costs.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: neither forum can review its own order — only rectify an apparent mistake; do not conflate the two powers.

Additional Evidence before Appellate Authorities

  • Key rule(s) — JC(A)/CIT(A) may admit additional evidence where:
  • the AO rejected evidence produced by the assessee;
  • the AO completed assessment without giving an opportunity to produce the evidence;
  • the AO demanded such evidence but the assessee could not produce it for sufficient cause; or
  • the AO never asked for it, but it was relevant and the assessee could not produce it for sufficient cause.
  • Key rule(s) — ITAT may admit additional evidence where:
  • it is satisfied the income-tax authorities decided the case without giving sufficient opportunity to the assessee to produce evidence; or
  • ITAT itself requires the additional evidence/documents to enable it to pass its order.
  • Concept: additional evidence is the exception, not the rule — appellate authorities must record satisfaction on one of the above grounds before admitting it.

Appeal Filing Fees — JC(A)/CIT(A) vs ITAT

Assessed income slabJC(A)/CIT(A) feeITAT fee
Up to ₹1,00,000₹250₹500
More than ₹1,00,000 up to ₹2,00,000₹500₹1,500
More than ₹2,00,000₹1,0001% of assessed income, subject to min. ₹5,000 and max. ₹10,000
Any other case (no assessed total income, e.g. TDS-default/penalty-only orders)₹250₹500
Appeal filed by the Department—No fee
Cross objections (Form 36A)—No fee
Stay of demand application to ITAT—₹500
  • Key formula:

ITAT fee (income > ₹2 lakh) = clip(1% × Assessed Total Income, ₹5,000, ₹10,000)

  • Pitfalls / exam tips: the department never pays a filing fee at any forum; do not apply the % formula to the JC(A)/CIT(A) slab — that fee is a flat ₹1,000 above ₹2 lakh.

Appeal to High Court — Sec 260A & 260B

  • Key rules:
  • Appeal lies to the HC only if it involves a substantial question of law.
  • Time limit: 120 days from the date on which the order appealed against is received.
  • Form, fees, and procedure are governed by the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908.
  • HC has an inherent power to review its own order — Meghalaya Steels Ltd. (2015)(SC); grounds for review per Sunil Vasudeva v. Sundar Gupta (2019)(SC): discovery of new/important evidence not earlier available despite due diligence, or a mistake/error apparent on the face of the record, or any other sufficient reason — but not mere repetition of an overruled argument or a minor/inconsequential error.
  • Concept: the HC's jurisdiction is confined to law, not fact — it must itself formulate the substantial question of law and decide only on that (A.A. Estate Pvt. Ltd. (2019)(SC)).
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • A cryptic ITAT order that doesn't engage with the merits does not, by itself, raise a substantial question of law for the HC — Ritha Sabapathy (2019)(Mad.).
  • Delay in filing the HC appeal cannot be condoned merely because a Sec 254(2) rectification application was pending before ITAT — Spinacom India (P.) Ltd. 2018.
  • HC can go into ALP/transfer-pricing determination as a question of law where ITAT failed to follow the Sec 92–92F TP guidelines, including comparability/filter selection — SAP Labs India Pvt. Ltd. 2023.

Appeal to Supreme Court — Sec 261 & 262

  • Key rules:
  • Appeal lies against an HC order.
  • Time limit: 90 days (governed by the Limitation Act, 1963 / Supreme Court Rules, since Sections 261/262 do not themselves prescribe a period).
  • SC has power to review its own order.
  • Form, fees, and procedure are governed by the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908.
  • Concept: the final appellate forum; typically requires an HC certificate that the case is fit for appeal, or leave to appeal.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: don't confuse the 90-day SC limitation with the 120-day HC limitation — they are commonly swapped in exam answers.

Sec 263 — Revision of Orders Prejudicial to the Interest of Revenue

  • Key rules:
  • CIT/PCIT/CCIT/PCCIT may call for and examine the record of any proceeding where the AO's/TPO's order is both (a) erroneous and (b) prejudicial to the interest of revenue, and pass such revisional order as deemed fit — including enhancing, modifying, or cancelling the assessment and directing a fresh assessment (or a fresh order u/s 92CA).
  • Opportunity of being heard must be given to the assessee before passing the order.
  • Time limit: 2 years from the end of the FY in which the original order sought to be revised was passed.
  • Order u/s 263 is appealable to ITAT.
  • Partial merger: matters already decided/considered in an appeal cannot be revised u/s 263, but other (non-appealed) matters in the same order can still be revised.
  • "Record" = everything on record at the time of examination by the revisional authority — not limited to what was on record when the AO/TPO passed the order (e.g., a valuation report received later can still be considered).
  • Deemed erroneous & prejudicial (Explanation 2) if, in the Commissioner's opinion:

(i) the order was passed without making inquiries/verification that should have been made; (ii) relief was allowed without inquiring into the claim; (iii) the order was not made in accordance with any CBDT order/direction/instruction; or (iv) the order was not passed in accordance with a decision of the jurisdictional HC/SC prejudicial to the assessee, in the assessee's own case or any other person's case.

  • Concept: a departmental safeguard against under-assessment/erroneous relief that damages revenue — distinct from Sec 264, which protects the assessee.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Where the reassessment covers only certain issues, the Sec 263 limitation for issues not covered by the reassessment runs from the original assessment order, not the reassessment order — Industrial Development Bank of India Ltd. 2023.
  • Once CIT(A)'s order on an issue is final and pending in appeal before ITAT, PCIT/CIT cannot invoke Sec 263 on that same issue (order merges with CIT(A)'s order) — Fortaleza Developers (2015)(Bom.).
  • If proceedings are stayed by any court, the period from the stay to the date the certified copy of the vacating order is received is excluded from the 2-year limitation.

Sec 264 — Revision of Other Orders (+ Sec 264A Faceless Revision)

  • Key rules:
  • CIT/PCIT/CCIT/PCCIT may, suo motu or on assessee's application, revise any order (other than one covered by Sec 263) passed by the AO.
  • Suo motu revision time limit: 1 year from the date of passing of the AO's order.
  • Application by assessee: within 1 year from the date the assessee receives a copy of the order.
  • Disposal time limit (where assessee applies): within 1 year from the end of the FY in which the application was made.
  • An order prejudicial to the assessee cannot be passed u/s 264 — it is a taxpayer-protective revision.
  • No appeal lies against an order u/s 264.
  • Assessee can apply for revision u/s 264 only if: (i) the 30-day time limit to file appeal to JC(A)/CIT(A) has expired, or (ii) the assessee has waived the right of appeal in writing.
  • Total merger: an assessee cannot simultaneously pursue appeal and Sec 264 revision, even on different matters of the same order — one must be chosen.
  • Sec 264A: CG may notify a scheme for Faceless Revision of orders under both Sec 263 and Sec 264.
  • Concept: a taxpayer's alternate, appeal-like remedy against orders that don't prejudice revenue, available only once the appeal route is foreclosed.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • If the order is subject matter of a pending appeal, it can be revised u/s 263 but not u/s 264.
  • Stay-period exclusion (as under Sec 263) applies equally to the Sec 264 limitation clock.

Sec 158A — Avoiding Repetitive Appeals

  • Key rule: where an identical question is already pending before the HC/SC for an earlier AY of the same assessee, and the same matter arises again for a subsequent year before the AO/JC(A)/CIT(A)/ITAT, the assessee may (instead of filing a fresh appeal) furnish a declaration in Form No. 8 asking that the eventual HC/SC decision be applied to the current year. The authority may admit or reject this application.
  • Concept: saves the assessee (and the system) the cost of parallel litigation on a point already sub judice at a higher forum.

Sec 158AB — Identical Question of Law Pending Before HC/SC (Department-side)

  • Key rules:
  • Where a question of law for an AY is already pending before the jurisdictional HC/SC in an earlier case decided against the Department (first case), and the same question is decided in the assessee's favour by JC(A)/CIT(A)/ITAT in a later case (second case), the Collegium may decide not to press the Department into filing a fresh appeal on that point immediately.
  • "Collegium" = 2 or more CCIT/PCCIT/CIT specified by CBDT.
  • On the Collegium's communication, CIT/PCIT directs the AO to file Form No. 8A within 120 days from receipt of the JC(A)/CIT(A)/ITAT order, stating that an appeal may be filed once the first case attains finality.
  • This deferral requires the assessee's acceptance that the question of law is identical; absent such acceptance, PCIT/CIT must file the appeal in the normal course.
  • If the first case is ultimately decided in the Department's favour, CIT/PCIT directs the AO to appeal — to ITAT within 60 days, to HC within 120 days — from the date the HC/SC order is received by CIT/PCIT.
  • Concept: mirrors Sec 158A but from the Department's side — avoids duplicative departmental appeals while an identical legal question is already before a higher court.

Sec 268A — Monetary Limits for Departmental Appeals

  • Key rule(s) — CBDT's current monetary (tax-effect) limits below which the Department will not file an appeal:
ForumMonetary limit (tax effect)
ITAT₹60,00,000
High Court₹2,00,00,000
Supreme Court₹5,00,00,000
  • These limits are fixed by CBDT circular under Sec 268A to curb small-value litigation (current figures per CBDT Circular No. 5/2024 dated 15.03.2024, raising the earlier ₹50 lakh/₹1 crore/₹2 crore thresholds).
  • Non-filing of an appeal on an issue in one year/one assessee does not bar the Department from raising the same issue: (a) for the same assessee in another year, or (b) for another assessee in any year.
  • The assessee cannot argue that the Department has "accepted" a position merely because it did not appeal on that issue.
  • Concept: an administrative litigation-management filter, not a substantive concession on the merits.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: the limits are tax effect, not total demand or total addition — compute tax effect (excluding interest/penalty unless the tax effect itself is only interest/penalty) before applying the threshold.

Dispute Resolution Committee (DRC) — Sec 245MA

  • Key rules — constitution & composition:
  • CG constitutes one or more DRCs, one for every region of a Pr. CCIT.
  • Composition: 3 members — 2 retired IRS officers who held the post of CIT (or equivalent/higher) for 5 years or more, plus 1 serving officer not below the rank of CIT/PCIT.
  • Term: members appointed for 3 years; decisions by majority; CG may remove a member after giving an opportunity of being heard.
  • The assessee has an option to opt in or out of DRC resolution.
  • Key rules — eligibility ("Specified Order"):
  • An order specified by CBDT (draft order with variation u/s 144C(1); intimation u/s 143(1)/200A/206CB; assessment/reassessment order other than one passed on DRP directions; rectification order u/s 154 enhancing assessment/reducing loss; order u/s 201/206C(6A) treating a person as assessee-in-default).
  • Aggregate amount of variation in the order ≤ ₹10 lakh.
  • Returned total income (if a return was filed) ≤ ₹50 lakh for that year.
  • Order must not be based on a search (Sec 132)/requisition (Sec 132A), a survey (Sec 133A), or information received under a DTAA (Sec 90/90A).
  • Ineligible persons: those under preventive detention under COFEPOSA, 1974; those prosecuted and convicted under IPC/UAPA/NDPS Act/Benami Act/PMLA/Prevention of Corruption Act; those facing IT-authority-initiated prosecution (or already convicted on it); persons notified under the Special Courts (Securities Transactions) Act, 1992; and those with pending Black Money Act, 2015 proceedings for the relevant AY.
  • Key rules — application & timelines:
  • Application in Form No. 34BC, within 1 month of receiving the specified order, with a fee of ₹1,000.
  • DRC screens the application (issuing a show-cause notice if minded to reject; hearing via video conference on request); if admitted, the assessee must, within 30 days, submit proof of withdrawal of the pending CIT(A) appeal/DRP application (or confirm none is pending) — failing which the application may be rejected.
  • DRC decision on the merits: within 6 months from the end of the month in which the application is admitted — DRC may (a) modify the variation favourably and grant penalty waiver/prosecution immunity, (b) retain the variation but still grant penalty waiver/immunity, or (c) make no modification at all — options (b) and (c) are deemed not prejudicial to the assessee.
  • No appeal/reference lies against the DRC-modified order (no CIT(A) appeal, no DRP reference).
  • AO's follow-through (Sec 245MA(2A)): AO must pass/modify the assessment/reassessment/recomputation order in conformity with the DRC's order within 1 month from the end of the month in which the DRC order is received.
  • Immunity/penalty waiver: granted on confirmation of payment of the demand, provided the assessee has paid tax due on returned income (if any) and cooperated with the DRC — no immunity if prosecution was already initiated before the application date; immunity is withdrawn (as if never granted) if conditions are later breached.
  • Termination of proceedings: DRC may terminate (after hearing the assessee) for non-cooperation, failure to respond to notices, concealment/false evidence, or failure to pay the demand — and must intimate the IT authority for further action.
  • Concept: a faster, paper-based (video-conferencing for hearing), small-ticket alternative to the JC(A)/CIT(A) appeal route, trading finality (no further appeal) for speed and potential penalty/prosecution relief.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Both the ₹10 lakh (variation) and ₹50 lakh (returned income) caps must be satisfied — failing either makes the order ineligible for DRC.
  • DRC route and CIT(A)/DRP route are mutually exclusive once the DRC application is admitted — the assessee must withdraw the parallel appeal/DRP application.
  • Distinguish DRC (Sec 245MA, small-value, no further appeal, includes penalty/prosecution relief) from the DRP (Sec 144C, transfer-pricing/foreign-company disputes, no monetary cap, and whose directions are appealable).

References

  1. Income-tax Act, 1961 — Sections 246, 246A–251 (appeal to JC(A)/CIT(A)), 252–255 (ITAT, incl. 253(3)/(6), 254(2), 254(2A)), 260A–260B (High Court), 261–262 (Supreme Court), 263, 264, 264A (revision), 158A, 158AB (repetitive-appeal provisions), 268A (monetary limits for departmental appeals), and 245MA (Dispute Resolution Committee) — as amended up to Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024, for the CA Final May/Nov 2026 syllabus.
  2. CBDT Circular No. 5/2024 dated 15.03.2024 — revised monetary limits for departmental appeals u/s 268A (ITAT ₹60 lakh / HC ₹2 crore / SC ₹5 crore).
  3. Income-tax (Dispute Resolution Committee) Rules, 2022 (Notification-based scheme under Sec 245MA) — DRC constitution, Form 34BC application, and specified-order thresholds.
  4. ICAI Final Course Study Material — Direct Tax Laws & International Taxation, Chapter on Appeals and Revision / Dispute Resolution Committee (relevant assessment-year edition), used to cross-check time limits, fee slabs, and case-law summaries.
  5. Case laws as cited inline: Pepsi Foods Ltd. (stay-of-demand third proviso to Sec 254(2A) — forum/year flagged for verification), Ritha Sabapathy (Mad.), Earnest Exports Ltd. (Bom.)/Lachman Dass Bhatia Hingwala (Delhi), Reliance Telecom Ltd. (2022)(SC), Meghalaya Steels Ltd. (2015)(SC), Sunil Vasudeva v. Sundar Gupta (2019)(SC), A.A. Estate Pvt. Ltd. (2019)(SC), Spinacom India (P.) Ltd. 2018, Fortaleza Developers (2015)(Bom.), Industrial Development Bank of India Ltd. 2023, SAP Labs India Pvt. Ltd. 2023.

14. Miscellaneous Provisions, Penalties, Prosecutions & The Black Money Act, 2015

Where it fits: the "clean-up" chapter — cash-transaction curbs (269SS/269ST/269T/269SU), deemed-income sections (68–69D), reporting/administrative provisions, the penalty & prosecution code of the Income-tax Act, and the parallel Black Money Act, 2015 for undisclosed foreign income/assets. High yield for objective-type and 4–6 mark questions.

Cash Transaction Restrictions — Sec. 269SS, 269ST, 269T, 269SU

  • Key rule(s):
  • Sec. 269SS — no person shall take/accept a loan, deposit, or advance in relation to immovable property, otherwise than by account payee cheque/DD/prescribed electronic mode, if the amount is ₹20,000 or more (including the outstanding unpaid balance of earlier such loan/deposit/advance on that date).
  • Relaxed limit of ₹2,00,000 for deposits/loans between a Primary Agricultural Credit Society (PACS)/Primary Co-operative Agriculture & Rural Development Bank (PCARD) and its members.
  • Not applicable to: Government, Banking company/co-op bank, Post Office savings bank, Government company, persons with only agricultural income (both parties), corporations established under a Central/State/Provincial Act, and any class notified by CBDT.
  • Sec. 269T — no person shall repay a loan/deposit (with interest) or an advance in relation to immovable property otherwise than by account payee cheque/DD/prescribed electronic mode, if the amount is ₹20,000 or more (including outstanding balance on that date). Exceptions similar to 269SS (excluding the PACS/agriculturist carve-outs).
  • Sec. 269ST — no person shall receive an amount of ₹2,00,000 or more, otherwise than by account payee cheque/DD/prescribed electronic mode:

(a) in aggregate from a person in a day; or (b) in respect of a single transaction; or (c) in respect of transactions relating to one event/occasion from a person.

  • Sec. 269SU — a person carrying on business with turnover exceeding ₹50 crore in the immediately preceding year must provide facility for accepting payment through prescribed electronic modes (RuPay Debit Card, UPI, UPI QR Code — Notification 105/2019).
  • Penalties:

Penalty u/s 271D (for 269SS default) = 100% of the loan/deposit/advance
Penalty u/s 271E (for 269T default) = 100% of the amount repaid in contravention
Penalty u/s 271DA (for 269ST default) = 100% of the amount received
Penalty u/s 271DB (for 269SU default) = ₹5,000 per day of continuing failure

  • Levying authority: Joint Commissioner; w.e.f. 1.4.2025 (Finance (No. 2) Act, 2024) shifted to the Assessing Officer for 271D, 271DA, 271DB and 271E.
  • No penalty u/s 271DA if the person proves reasonable cause for the contravention.
  • Concept: These sections plug cash-based tax evasion at the loan/deposit/receipt stage; the counterparty giving/repaying cash, and the recipient receiving cash, both attract independent code sections.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Aggregate the ₹20,000 test with the outstanding unpaid balance of prior loans/deposits between the same two persons — a fresh ₹15,000 cash loan can still violate 269SS if an old ₹10,000 balance is unpaid.
  • 269ST tests three independent limbs (per day/per transaction/per occasion) — splitting one bill into cash instalments across several days still violates limb (c) (single "occasion", e.g. a wedding) — Mr Kejriwal hospital bill type facts.
  • Case law: cash advances between a firm and its own partner are not necessarily hit by 269SS if bona fide (V. Sivakumar (Mad.)); repayment of loan by book/adjustment entry does not violate 269T if genuine (Triumph International Finance (Bom.)); genuineness/bona fides can constitute "reasonable cause" against 271D/271E (Muthoot Financiers (Del.)).
  • Definitions:
TermMeaning
Account payee cheque/DDCheque/DD crossed "A/c Payee" — cannot be endorsed to a third party
Advance in relation to immovable propertyAny advance (whether or not it becomes refundable) taken in connection with transfer of an immovable property

Deemed Income — Sec. 68 to 69D

  • Key rule(s):
  • Sec. 68 (Cash credit): unexplained sum credited in books → deemed income of that PY. For a loan/borrowing, the explanation is deemed unsatisfactory unless both the assessee and the creditor (in whose name the credit is recorded) explain nature & source satisfactorily. For a closely held company's share application money/capital/premium, the resident share-subscriber must also explain source — except where the subscriber is a SEBI-registered Venture Capital Fund/Company.
  • Sec. 69: unexplained investments not recorded in books, with no/unsatisfactory explanation → deemed income.
  • Sec. 69A: assessee found owner of money/bullion/jewellery/valuable article not recorded in books, with no/unsatisfactory explanation → deemed income.
  • Sec. 69B: investment/acquisition amount recorded in books is less than actually spent, difference unexplained → deemed income of the excess.
  • Sec. 69C: unexplained expenditure → deemed income; such deemed income is not allowed as a deduction under any head.
  • Sec. 69D: amount borrowed/repaid on a hundi otherwise than by account payee cheque → deemed income of the borrower/repayer in the year of borrowing/repayment (no double taxation on subsequent repayment of an amount already taxed as income).
  • Tax rate — Sec. 115BBE:

Tax on income u/s 68–69D = 60% + 25% surcharge (on tax) + 4% HEC = 78% effective

No deduction for any expenditure/allowance/set-off of loss is permitted against such income.

  • Concept: These are anti-evasion deeming fictions shifting the onus onto the assessee to explain the nature and source of unrecorded credits/assets/expenditure; failure results in taxation at a steep flat 78% rate rather than slab/normal rates.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Sec. 68 has a higher bar for share capital/premium of closely held companies (post-2012 amendment) — even VC Fund/Company exception does not extend to the general "closely held company" onus.
  • Sec. 69C expenditure once deemed income can never be claimed as a deduction — a favourite trick MCQ.
  • Additional 10% penalty under Sec. 271AAC applies on tax payable u/s 115BBE(1) where such income is unexplained/not disclosed appropriately; note that Sec. 270A does not apply once 271AAC is levied.

Certain Transfers to be Void & Provisional Attachment — Sec. 281, 281B

  • Key rule(s):
  • Sec. 281: where tax/penalty/interest/fine exceeding ₹5,000 is payable and the assessee charges or transfers any asset exceeding ₹10,000 in value during the pendency of proceedings (till service of TRO notice), such charge/transfer is void against the tax claim — unless (a) it is of stock-in-trade of the business, or (b) made for adequate consideration without notice of the pending proceedings/sum due, or (c) with prior AO approval.
  • Sec. 281B: AO may provisionally attach any property of the assessee during pendency of assessment/reassessment proceedings, or for penalty u/s 271AAD where the penalty likely to be imposed exceeds ₹2 crore, with prior approval of PCCIT/CCIT/PCIT/CIT (or PDGIT/DGIT/PDIT/DIT). Attachment is valid for 6 months from the order, extendable up to 2 years, or 60 days after completion of assessment proceedings, whichever is later. Assessee may substitute a bank guarantee; AO must revoke provisional attachment within 15 days of receiving it.
  • Concept: Sec. 281 is a self-operating anti-avoidance rule protecting revenue's charge over assessee assets during litigation; Sec. 281B is a discretionary, higher-authority-sanctioned protective attachment power.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • A transfer void u/s 281 still requires the AO/Department to establish it through a civil suit under the Transfer of Property Act — the AO cannot unilaterally declare a sale deed void (Manoj Kabra, All. HC).
  • Remember the outer time cap for provisional attachment: 2 years OR 60 days post-assessment completion — whichever is later, not earlier.

Reporting Obligations — SFT, AIS & Crypto Reporting

  • Key rule(s):
  • Sec. 285B: film/OTT/event-management producers must file Form 52A with DGIT(Systems) within 60 days from end of PY, disclosing payments exceeding ₹50,000 in aggregate to each engaged person.
  • Sec. 285BA — Statement of Financial Transaction (SFT): specified reporting persons (banks, registrars, companies issuing shares/bonds, mutual fund trustees, property registrars, tax-audit assessees, etc.) must file SFT by 31st May following the FY. Key thresholds: cash deposits/withdrawals in current accounts ≥ ₹50 lakh; cash deposits in other accounts / time deposits / share & bond subscriptions / buybacks / MF units / forex sale ≥ ₹10 lakh; cash payment for bank drafts/pre-paid instruments ≥ ₹10 lakh; credit card bill payments ≥ ₹1 lakh cash or ₹10 lakh other mode; immovable property transactions ≥ ₹30 lakh (or SDV ≥ ₹30 lakh); cash receipt for sale of goods/services by a tax-audit assessee > ₹2 lakh.
  • Sec. 285BB: Annual Information Statement (AIS) to be uploaded in Form 26AS within 3 months from end of the month the information is received.
  • Sec. 285BAA (inserted by Finance Act 2025, w.e.f. AY 2026-27): prescribed reporting entities to report crypto-asset transactions in the prescribed form/manner; defective statement correctable within 30 days; inaccuracies discovered later to be corrected within 10 days.
  • Penalties:

Sec. 271FA (delay in SFT filing) = ₹500/day up to notice expiry; ₹1,000/day thereafter
Sec. 271FAA (inaccurate SFT) = ₹50,000 (+ ₹5,000 per reportable account if inaccuracy traceable to account holder)

  • Concept: This is the Department's data-gathering net (specified high-value transactions) feeding pre-filled returns and AIS/AS-26 — distinct from TDS/TCS reporting.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • SFT limit is applied separately to deposits and withdrawals (₹50 lakh each), and reporting person must aggregate across all accounts of like nature held by the same person during the FY.
  • Loan repayment instalments to an NBFC/HFC — each instalment is a separate "single transaction", not aggregated (CBDT clarification) — a common trap for 269ST-type reasoning carried into SFT MCQs.

Authorised Representative & Validity of Proceedings — Sec. 288, 292B, 292BB

  • Key rule(s): Sec. 288 lists eligible Authorised Representatives — employee, bank officer (of the bank where assessee has a/c), legal practitioner, Chartered Accountant, holders of CBDT-recognised accountancy qualifications (CS/CMA etc.), commerce/law graduates from CBDT-approved universities, and any other prescribed person.
  • Sec. 292B: a return/assessment/notice/summons is not invalid merely for a mistake, defect, or omission if it is, in substance, in conformity with the Act's intent.
  • Sec. 292BB: if the assessee has appeared/co-operated in proceedings, notice is deemed validly served (and the objection that it was not served/served late/served improperly is barred) — unless the objection is raised before completion of assessment/reassessment.
  • Concept: Curative/deeming provisions protecting revenue proceedings from technical challenge, subject to the assessee's timely objection right.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips:
  • Sec. 292B does not cure a jurisdictional defect — issuing a notice on a non-existent amalgamated entity is void ab initio, and mere participation does not cure it (Maruti Suzuki India Ltd., SC).
  • Sec. 292BB does not cure non-issuance of a mandatory notice u/s 143(2) even with full participation (Laxman Das Khandelwal, SC) — 292BB cures defects in service, not complete non-issuance of a jurisdictional notice.

Penalty for Under-Reporting/Misreporting of Income — Sec. 270A, 270AA, 273A

  • Key formula(s):

Penalty (under-reporting) = 50% × Tax payable on Under-Reported Income (URI)
Penalty (mis-reporting) = 200% × Tax payable on URI

First assessment: URI = Assessed income - Returned income (or Basic Exemption Limit if no return filed)

Reassessment: URI = Reassessed income - Income assessed/reassessed in the immediately preceding order
Tax on URI (reassessment) = Tax on (URI + last assessed income) - Tax on last assessed income

Losses claimed reduced/converted to income:

URI = (Loss claimed - Loss assessed/reassessed) or (Loss claimed - Income assessed/reassessed)
— tax computed treating URI as if it were the total income.

MAT/AMT cases (Sec. 115JB/115JC):

URI = (A-B) + (C-D)
where A/B are total income assessed under general provisions before/after excluding URI, and C/D are deemed total income assessed under 115JB/115JC before/after excluding URI; if the URI in B and D are identical, it is not counted twice (excluded from D).

  • Key rule(s) — Mis-reporting instances (Sec. 270A(9)): misrepresentation/suppression of facts; failure to record investments in books; unsubstantiated expenditure claims; false entries in books; failure to record receipts having a bearing on total income; failure to report an international transaction under transfer pricing.
  • Exclusions from "under-reported income" (Sec. 270A(6)): bona fide explanation with full disclosure; estimation-based additions where books are correct/complete but income can't properly be deduced; assessee's own lower self-estimated disallowance with full disclosure; TP additions in conformity with TPO's ALP where Sec. 92D documentation/disclosure was maintained.
  • Sec. 270AA — Immunity from penalty (270A) & prosecution: available only for under-reporting (not mis-reporting), if the assessee pays tax + interest per the demand notice within the time limit and does not file an appeal. Application to AO within 1 month from end of month of receipt of order; AO to dispose within 3 months from end of month of receipt of application, after hearing.
  • Sec. 273A — Waiver/reduction of penalty by PCIT/CIT: conditions — voluntary & full disclosure in good faith before detection, co-operation in enquiry, and payment of tax + interest in full. Relief available only once in the assessee's lifetime. ⚠️ VERIFY — OCR states CIT/PCIT can waive without higher approval where income is up to ₹5 lakh, and needs CCIT/PCCIT/DGIT approval above ₹5 lakh; this appears to be an administrative/circular-based monetary limit rather than a figure appearing in bare Sec. 273A text — confirm current CBDT instruction figure before quoting in an exam answer.
  • Concept: Sec. 270A replaced the earlier concealment penalty (old Sec. 271(1)(c)) with a two-tier (under-reporting/mis-reporting) structure and a menu of statutory carve-outs plus an immunity route.
  • Pitfalls / exam tips: Immunity u/s 270AA is a one-way street — filing an appeal (even on an unrelated ground) after seeking immunity forfeits it; misreporting can never get 270AA immunity.

General Penalty Code — Key Sections (271A–271K, 221)

  • Key rule(s):
SectionDefaultQuantumWho levies
221(1)Failure to pay self-assessment tax/demand/TDS/TCSUp to amount of tax in arrearsAO
271AFailure to keep/maintain/retain books u/s 44AA₹25,000AO, JC(A), CIT(A)
271AA / 271GTP documentation defaults2% of transaction valueAO, CIT(A)
271AACDeemed income u/s 68–69C not appropriately disclosed10% of tax u/s 115BBEAO, JC(A), CIT(A)
271AADFalse entry / omitted entry to evade tax100% of the false/omitted entryAO, JC(A), CIT(A)
271AAETrust/institution benefit to related person u/s 13(1)100% (1st violation) / 200% (subsequent)AO
271BFailure to get accounts audited u/s 44AB0.5% of turnover (max ₹1,50,000)AO
271BATP audit report (Form 3CEB) not furnished u/s 92E₹1,00,000AO
271CFailure to deduct/pay TDS incl. u/s 194B/194R/194S/194BA100% of tax not deducted/paidJC [AO w.e.f. 1.4.2025]
